# CLAUDE.md — Investigator 🐊🔍

This file provides guidance to Claude Code (claude.ai/code) when working in this repository.

## Purpose

**Investigator** is a three-agent AI research pipeline. This repository stores completed investigations and the pipeline that produces them. The goal is purely to research, analyze, and synthesize understanding of topics — never to solve problems, implement solutions, or draft pseudocode. Investigations produce findings and insights only.

## Orchestration Model

This repo operates on a three-layer agent pattern:

| Layer | Role |
|-------|------|
| **Main session (this session)** | Synthesizer & orchestrator — never does raw research, protects its context window |
| **Investigation agents (spawned)** | One-shot researchers — investigate a single topic and return structured outputs |
| **Validation agents (spawned)** | One-shot fact-checkers — verify sources and findings after every investigation, always run last |

The main session spawns investigation agents using the persona in `templates/agent_persona.md`, then spawns a validation agent using the persona in `templates/validator_persona.md`. Raw research and raw validation never happen in the main session.

## Structure Convention

### Folder Naming

Investigation subfolders use **PascalCase** — no hyphens, underscores, or spaces.

```
MsDefenderAwsExclusions/
LlmContextWindows/
RustAsyncPatterns/
AwsIamPrivilegeEscalation/
```

### Sub-Investigations and Rollup

When a topic has multiple related sub-topics that each warrant separate investigation, sub-investigation folders nest **inside** the root investigation folder:

```
SsmRunAsUserMultiGroupConflict/       ← root (rollup investigation)
  investigation.json                  ← synthesized from all sub-investigations
  investigation.md                    ← generated
  validation_report.md
  brief_leadership.md
  brief_po.md
  glossary.md
  LzaIdentityCenterConfig/            ← sub-investigation
    investigation.json
    investigation.md
    validation_report.md
    ...
  LzaSsmRunAsSync/                    ← sub-investigation
    investigation.json
    ...
```

The root folder's `investigation.json` is always the **rollup** — synthesized from all sub-investigation JSONs by a rollup investigator agent (reads sub-investigation JSONs, does no new live research). The rollup goes through the same validator pipeline as any other investigation. Sub-investigation markdown files are self-contained within their own folders; `check_sync.py` ignores subdirectories.

### Scope Gate (required before spawning any investigation agent)

Before spawning an investigation agent, the main session **must** ask the following scoping questions to ensure the investigation is focused enough to produce high-quality, atomic findings:

1. **What is the single core question?** — Can it be stated in one sentence? If not, split it.
2. **What is out of scope?** — Name at least one related area that will not be covered.
3. **Who is the intended consumer of the findings?** — Planning LLM, human analyst, or both?
4. **Are there known sub-topics that warrant separate investigations?** — If yes, each gets its own nested folder inside the root investigation folder.

A question like "tell me about cloud security" must be narrowed (e.g., "What are the documented IAM privilege escalation paths in AWS that do not require existing admin permissions?") before proceeding.

## Investigation Workflow

Each investigation subfolder must contain the following output files:

| File | Audience | Required |
|------|----------|---------|
| `investigation.md` | Engineers | Always |
| `investigation.json` | Agents | Always |
| `validation_report.md` | All | Always |
| `brief_leadership.md` | Engineering Leadership | Technical investigations only |
| `brief_po.md` | Product Owners / PMs / EMs | Technical investigations only |

**Technical investigations** (infra, security, configuration, operational risk) must include `audience_briefs` in `investigation.json` — `brief_leadership.md` and `brief_po.md` are then generated by script.

**Non-technical investigations** (market events, financial analysis, historical research, organizational topics) omit `audience_briefs` entirely — no brief files are generated. A PO should never receive a financial/market investigation as a brief; the full document is the artifact.

All markdown files are derived from `investigation.json` by script and must never be hand-edited. `validation_report.md` is always the final artifact.

### Step Order (mandatory)

1. **Scope gate** — main session asks scoping questions, narrows the question
2. **Spawn investigation agent** — writes `investigation.json`; runs `json_to_md.py` to generate `investigation.md` and brief/glossary files
3. **Spawn validation agent** — receives `investigation.json` as structured input, writes `validation_report.md`
4. **Remediation** — if validation finds `CONTRADICTED` or material `UNVERIFIED` findings, the main session re-spawns the investigation agent with the specific discrepancies noted, and the agent corrects only the affected sections and re-syncs `investigation.json`
5. **Rollup** (only when sub-investigations exist) — after all sub-investigations are validated, spawn a rollup investigator that reads all sub-investigation JSONs and writes a synthesized `investigation.json` to the root folder; then validate the rollup
6. **Git commit and push** — after all investigations (and rollup if applicable) are validated and `check_sync.py` exits 0 everywhere, commit all new files and push to the remote

**Validation is never optional and never skipped. Git push is the final step.**

### Remediation Rules

| Verdict | Action |
|---------|--------|
| `CONTRADICTED` | Must be corrected — re-spawn investigation agent with the specific claim and contradicting evidence |
| `UNVERIFIED` (material claim) | Must be corrected or downgraded to an open question |
| `UNVERIFIED` (minor / peripheral) | May be left as-is with a note in `open_questions` |
| `PARTIALLY CONFIRMED` | Investigator must narrow the claim to only what was confirmed |
| `DEAD` source | Must be replaced with an accessible equivalent or removed |
| `REDIRECT` source | Update URL in `investigation.json`, then re-run `json_to_md.py` to regenerate markdown |
| `OUT_OF_SYNC` | Re-run `json_to_md.py` to regenerate markdown from `investigation.json` — never modify `investigation.json` to match the markdown |

After any correction, re-run `json_to_md.py` and confirm `check_sync.py` exits 0 before the workflow is considered complete.

### Actionable Insights First

Every investigation that has concrete outputs (paths, configs, commands, decisions, recommendations) **must** populate `quick_reference` in `investigation.json`. The generator renders this as the first section after the header — before question, context, or findings.

The principle: a human opening the markdown should get the answer in the first scroll, and the evidence behind it below. If the investigation has no concrete actionable output, `quick_reference` may be omitted.

### Agent Input Convention

`investigation.json` is the machine-readable handoff format. When passing context to any downstream agent (validation, synthesis, follow-on investigation), always pass `investigation.json` as structured input — not `investigation.md`. The JSON is authoritative for inter-agent communication.

### JSON is the only authored file — markdown is generated

Investigation agents write **`investigation.json` only**. The markdown is always produced by script:

```
python3 scripts/json_to_md.py <investigation_dir>
```

This eliminates JSON/MD drift entirely — the markdown is derived, never hand-authored.

### Sync verification

After generating the markdown, verify with:

```
python3 scripts/check_sync.py <investigation_dir>
```

- **Investigation agent**: write JSON → run `json_to_md.py` → run `check_sync.py` → must exit 0 before returning
- **Validation agent**: run `check_sync.py` first, paste stdout into report. Zero tokens spent on comparison logic.

The sync check normalizes both files, hashes field contents, and reports per-field IN_SYNC / OUT_OF_SYNC status.

Exit codes: `0` = IN_SYNC, `1` = OUT_OF_SYNC (re-run `json_to_md.py`), `2` = error (bad JSON or missing file — fix before continuing).

### Script Failure Paths

| Script | Exit | Meaning | Recovery |
|--------|------|---------|----------|
| `json_to_md.py` | 2 | Invalid JSON, missing required field, or I/O error | Fix the error in `investigation.json` and re-run |
| `check_sync.py` | 1 | Content has drifted or a brief file is missing | Re-run `json_to_md.py` to regenerate markdown |
| `check_sync.py` | 2 | Invalid JSON or missing file | Fix the underlying error before checking sync |

Investigation agents must not return until both scripts exit 0.

### Trust Boundary

`investigation.json` field values are rendered verbatim into markdown. Agent-produced content must be treated as potentially unsafe:

- Single-value fields (`headline`, bullets, list items, concept names) must not embed newlines — they break blockquote and table rendering.
- Concept `name` values must not begin with `#` — they render as headings in the glossary.
- Source `url` values must use `https://` or `http://` — other schemes are silently dropped by the renderer.
- Markdown files are never hand-edited. Any correction goes into `investigation.json` and is regenerated by script.

### Output Sections (required in investigation.json)

1. **Question** — the specific question being investigated
2. **Context** — why this topic matters
3. **Key Findings** — standalone, atomic insights
4. **Concepts & Entities** — key terms, technologies, systems, or actors
5. **Tensions & Tradeoffs** — competing forces or unresolved tensions
6. **Open Questions** — what remains unknown
7. **Sources & References** — all cited material

### Git Workflow

After all investigations in a session are complete, validated, and `check_sync.py` exits 0:

```bash
git add <investigation_folder>/
git commit -m "investigation: <topic> — <one-line summary of key finding>"
git push
```

Commit message format: `investigation: <PascalCaseFolderName> — <one-line summary>`

For a root investigation with sub-investigations, add the entire root folder in one commit. Never commit partial or unvalidated investigations.

There are no build, lint, or test commands — this is a research/notes repository, not a software project.


# SOURCE: /Users/samfakhreddine/repos/personal/repoSystem/AGENTS.md

# repoSystem

Generic automation platform for reusable repo systems.

## Context7

- Use Context7 MCP as the default external technical reference source for this repo whenever work touches a library, framework, SDK, API, CLI tool, cloud service, language runtime, standard library, or toolchain behavior.
- Use it for code generation, implementation planning, `/wfc-deepen`, code review, debugging, migrations, configuration, setup, API syntax, version-specific behavior, and CLI usage.
- Read the local codebase first for repo-specific behavior. Context7 complements local analysis; it does not replace it.
- During `/wfc-deepen` or any plan-enrichment workflow, query Context7 for extra supporting tidbits, constraints, edge cases, and current API or tool behavior that strengthen the plan annotations.
- When using Context7, start with `resolve-library-id`, choose the best-fit library ID, then `query-docs` with the full task context rather than a single keyword.

## Hard Guardrails

- Do not hard-code groceryHelper-specific assumptions into the platform.
- Do not lock the project to a single implementation runtime until the spec justifies it.
- Do not make any one module mandatory when the product goal is composability.
- Do not hide policy decisions in templates without documenting them.
- Do not generate unreviewable automation blobs.
- Do not store secrets, tokens, or machine-specific credentials in this repo.

## Source Of Truth

- `README.md`: project purpose and top-level framing
- `ARCHITECTURE.md`: intended platform boundaries and component map
- `docs/ba/`: requirements and product analysis
- `docs/adr/README.md`: recorded architectural decisions
- `roadmap/`: deferred follow-up ideas
- `CHANGELOG.md`: promoted release history
- `changelog.d/`: PR-owned fragment inputs

## Working Rules

- Keep a clean separation between:
  - platform core
  - installable modules
  - language/toolchain adapters
  - generated templates
  - persisted config and schema definitions
- Prefer capability negotiation over runtime guessing.
- Prefer adapters that describe repo facts and toolchain contracts, not adapters that contain product policy.
- Modules must be installable independently and coexist safely.
- Generated outputs must be idempotent and deterministic when run against the same repo state.
- All architecture-shaping changes should update docs in the same change.

## Product Direction

- `release` should be able to stand alone.
- `runners` should be able to stand alone.
- `testing` should be able to stand alone.
- combinations such as `release + testing` or `runners + testing` must be supported deliberately, not accidentally.
- language-agnostic core first, language-specific adapters second.

## Coding Discipline

- Do not introduce a package manager or runtime without a clear product reason.
- Prefer plain-text specs and data contracts until implementation choices are final.
- Keep placeholders honest. Mark intentional future directories as scaffolding.
- Avoid fake generality. If something is only proven for one ecosystem, call that out.

## Git

- Work on branches, not directly on `main`.
- Keep commits coherent and minimal.
- Use conventional commits.

<!-- wfc:start -->
## WFC

### Always Do

- Use `wfc version` to verify the CLI is installed. Do not use `wfc --version`.
- Treat `.wfc/config.json` as the project WFC source of truth.
- Use `make quality-check`, `make format`, `make lint`, and `make test` for local quality flows.
- Keep WFC updates aligned with the Go-first, CLI-first, plugin-based architecture recorded in `docs/adr/`.

### When To Use WFC Skills

| Need | Start With |
|---|---|
| initialize or repair project WFC setup | `wfc-init` |
| create a multi-file implementation plan | `wfc-plan` |
| validate a strategic architecture decision | `wfc-validate` |
| prioritize capabilities or workstreams | `wfc-prioritize` |
| document architecture or decisions after code changes | `wfc-architecture` or `wfc-adr` |

### Observability

- `wfc version`
- `git status --short --branch`
- `cat .wfc/config.json`
- `make quality-check`

### Review Flow

1. Update source-of-truth docs or ADRs when the architecture changes.
2. Produce a plan before multi-file implementation.
3. Run quality checks before closing work.
4. Keep outputs deterministic and reviewable in git.
<!-- wfc:end -->

<!-- gitnexus:start -->
# GitNexus — Code Intelligence

This project is indexed by GitNexus as **repoSystem** (1925 symbols, 4449 relationships, 157 execution flows). Use the GitNexus MCP tools to understand code, assess impact, and navigate safely.

> If any GitNexus tool warns the index is stale, run `npx gitnexus analyze` in terminal first.

## Always Do

- **MUST run impact analysis before editing any symbol.** Before modifying a function, class, or method, run `gitnexus_impact({target: "symbolName", direction: "upstream"})` and report the blast radius (direct callers, affected processes, risk level) to the user.
- **MUST run `gitnexus_detect_changes()` before committing** to verify your changes only affect expected symbols and execution flows.
- **MUST warn the user** if impact analysis returns HIGH or CRITICAL risk before proceeding with edits.
- When exploring unfamiliar code, use `gitnexus_query({query: "concept"})` to find execution flows instead of grepping. It returns process-grouped results ranked by relevance.
- When you need full context on a specific symbol — callers, callees, which execution flows it participates in — use `gitnexus_context({name: "symbolName"})`.

## When Debugging

1. `gitnexus_query({query: "<error or symptom>"})` — find execution flows related to the issue
2. `gitnexus_context({name: "<suspect function>"})` — see all callers, callees, and process participation
3. `READ gitnexus://repo/repoSystem/process/{processName}` — trace the full execution flow step by step
4. For regressions: `gitnexus_detect_changes({scope: "compare", base_ref: "main"})` — see what your branch changed

## When Refactoring

- **Renaming**: MUST use `gitnexus_rename({symbol_name: "old", new_name: "new", dry_run: true})` first. Review the preview — graph edits are safe, text_search edits need manual review. Then run with `dry_run: false`.
- **Extracting/Splitting**: MUST run `gitnexus_context({name: "target"})` to see all incoming/outgoing refs, then `gitnexus_impact({target: "target", direction: "upstream"})` to find all external callers before moving code.
- After any refactor: run `gitnexus_detect_changes({scope: "all"})` to verify only expected files changed.

## Never Do

- NEVER edit a function, class, or method without first running `gitnexus_impact` on it.
- NEVER ignore HIGH or CRITICAL risk warnings from impact analysis.
- NEVER rename symbols with find-and-replace — use `gitnexus_rename` which understands the call graph.
- NEVER commit changes without running `gitnexus_detect_changes()` to check affected scope.

## Tools Quick Reference

| Tool | When to use | Command |
|------|-------------|---------|
| `query` | Find code by concept | `gitnexus_query({query: "auth validation"})` |
| `context` | 360-degree view of one symbol | `gitnexus_context({name: "validateUser"})` |
| `impact` | Blast radius before editing | `gitnexus_impact({target: "X", direction: "upstream"})` |
| `detect_changes` | Pre-commit scope check | `gitnexus_detect_changes({scope: "staged"})` |
| `rename` | Safe multi-file rename | `gitnexus_rename({symbol_name: "old", new_name: "new", dry_run: true})` |
| `cypher` | Custom graph queries | `gitnexus_cypher({query: "MATCH ..."})` |

## Impact Risk Levels

| Depth | Meaning | Action |
|-------|---------|--------|
| d=1 | WILL BREAK — direct callers/importers | MUST update these |
| d=2 | LIKELY AFFECTED — indirect deps | Should test |
| d=3 | MAY NEED TESTING — transitive | Test if critical path |

## Resources

| Resource | Use for |
|----------|---------|
| `gitnexus://repo/repoSystem/context` | Codebase overview, check index freshness |
| `gitnexus://repo/repoSystem/clusters` | All functional areas |
| `gitnexus://repo/repoSystem/processes` | All execution flows |
| `gitnexus://repo/repoSystem/process/{name}` | Step-by-step execution trace |

## Self-Check Before Finishing

Before completing any code modification task, verify:
1. `gitnexus_impact` was run for all modified symbols
2. No HIGH/CRITICAL risk warnings were ignored
3. `gitnexus_detect_changes()` confirms changes match expected scope
4. All d=1 (WILL BREAK) dependents were updated

## Keeping the Index Fresh

After committing code changes, the GitNexus index becomes stale. Re-run analyze to update it:

```bash
npx gitnexus analyze
```

If the index previously included embeddings, preserve them by adding `--embeddings`:

```bash
npx gitnexus analyze --embeddings
```

To check whether embeddings exist, inspect `.gitnexus/meta.json` — the `stats.embeddings` field shows the count (0 means no embeddings). **Running analyze without `--embeddings` will delete any previously generated embeddings.**

> Claude Code users: A PostToolUse hook handles this automatically after `git commit` and `git merge`.

## CLI

| Task | Read this skill file |
|------|---------------------|
| Understand architecture / "How does X work?" | `.claude/skills/gitnexus/gitnexus-exploring/SKILL.md` |
| Blast radius / "What breaks if I change X?" | `.claude/skills/gitnexus/gitnexus-impact-analysis/SKILL.md` |
| Trace bugs / "Why is X failing?" | `.claude/skills/gitnexus/gitnexus-debugging/SKILL.md` |
| Rename / extract / split / refactor | `.claude/skills/gitnexus/gitnexus-refactoring/SKILL.md` |
| Tools, resources, schema reference | `.claude/skills/gitnexus/gitnexus-guide/SKILL.md` |
| Index, status, clean, wiki CLI commands | `.claude/skills/gitnexus/gitnexus-cli/SKILL.md` |

<!-- gitnexus:end -->

# GitNexus — Code Intelligence

This project is indexed by GitNexus as **repoSystem** (1925 symbols, 4449 relationships, 157 execution flows). Use the GitNexus MCP tools to understand code, assess impact, and navigate safely.

> If any GitNexus tool warns the index is stale, run `npx gitnexus analyze` in terminal first.

# SOURCE: /Users/samfakhreddine/repos/personal/desloppify/docs/CLAUDE.md

## Claude Code Overlay

Use Claude subagents for subjective scoring work. **Do not use `--runner codex`** — use Claude subagents exclusively.

### Review workflow

Run `desloppify review --prepare` first to generate review data, then use Claude subagents:

1. **Prepare**: `desloppify review --prepare` — writes `query.json` and `.desloppify/review_packet_blind.json`.
2. **Launch subagents**: Split the review across N parallel Claude subagents (one message, multiple Task calls). Each agent reviews a subset of dimensions.
3. **Merge & import**: Merge agent outputs, then `desloppify review --import merged.json --manual-override --attest "Claude subagents ran blind reviews against review_packet_blind.json" --scan-after-import`.

#### How to split dimensions across subagents

- Read `dimension_prompts` from `query.json` for dimensions with definitions and seed files.
- Read `.desloppify/review_packet_blind.json` for the blind packet (no score targets, no anchoring data).
- Group dimensions into 3-4 batches by theme (e.g., architecture, code quality, testing, conventions).
- Launch one Task agent per batch with `subagent_type: "general-purpose"`. Each agent gets:
  - The codebase path and list of dimensions to score
  - The blind packet path to read
  - Instruction to score from code evidence only, not from targets
- Each agent writes output to a separate file. Merge assessments (average overlapping dimension scores) and concatenate findings.

### Subagent rules

1. Each agent must be context-isolated — do not pass conversation history or score targets.
2. Agents must consume `.desloppify/review_packet_blind.json` (not full `query.json`) to avoid score anchoring.

### Triage workflow

Orchestrate triage with per-stage subagents:
1. `desloppify plan triage --run-stages --runner claude` — prints orchestrator instructions
2. For each stage (observe → reflect → organize → enrich):
   - Get prompt: `desloppify plan triage --stage-prompt <stage>`
   - Launch a subagent with that prompt
   - Verify: `desloppify plan triage` (check dashboard)
   - Confirm: `desloppify plan triage --confirm <stage> --attestation "..."`
3. Complete: `desloppify plan triage --complete --strategy "..." --attestation "..."`

<!-- desloppify-overlay: claude -->
<!-- desloppify-end -->


# SOURCE: /Users/samfakhreddine/repos/personal/desloppify/AGENTS.md

---
name: desloppify
description: >
  Codebase health scanner and technical debt tracker. Use when the user asks
  about code quality, technical debt, dead code, large files, god classes,
  duplicate functions, code smells, naming issues, import cycles, or coupling
  problems. Also use when asked for a health score, what to fix next, or to
  create a cleanup plan. Supports 28 languages.
allowed-tools: Bash(desloppify *)

# Desloppify

## 1. Your Job

Maximise the **strict score** honestly. Your main cycle: **scan → plan → execute → rescan**. Follow the scan output's **INSTRUCTIONS FOR AGENTS** — don't substitute your own analysis.

**Don't be lazy.** Do large refactors and small detailed fixes with equal energy. If it takes touching 20 files, touch 20 files. If it's a one-line change, make it. No task is too big or too small — fix things properly, not minimally.

## 2. The Workflow

Three phases, repeated as a cycle.

### Phase 1: Scan and review — understand the codebase

```bash
desloppify scan --path .       # analyse the codebase
desloppify status              # check scores — are we at target?
```

The scan will tell you if subjective dimensions need review. Follow its instructions. To trigger a review manually:
```bash
desloppify review --prepare    # then follow your runner's review workflow
```

### Phase 2: Plan — decide what to work on

After reviews, triage stages and plan creation appear as queue items in `next`. Complete them in order:
```bash
desloppify next                                        # shows the next workflow step
desloppify plan triage --stage observe --report "themes and root causes..."
desloppify plan triage --stage reflect --report "comparison against completed work..."
desloppify plan triage --stage organize --report "summary of priorities..."
desloppify plan triage --complete --strategy "execution plan..."
```

### Automated triage (subagent runners)

For Codex: `desloppify plan triage --run-stages --runner codex`
For Claude: `desloppify plan triage --run-stages --runner claude` — then follow orchestrator instructions per stage

Options: `--only-stages observe,reflect` (subset), `--dry-run` (prompts only), `--stage-timeout-seconds N` (per-stage).

Then shape the queue. **The plan shapes everything `next` gives you** — don't skip this step.

```bash
desloppify plan                          # see the full ordered queue
desloppify plan reorder <pat> top        # reorder — what unblocks the most?
desloppify plan cluster create <name>    # group related issues to batch-fix
desloppify plan focus <cluster>          # scope next to one cluster
desloppify plan skip <pat>              # defer — hide from next
```

More plan commands:
```bash
desloppify plan reorder <cluster> top    # move all cluster members at once
desloppify plan reorder <a> <b> top     # mix clusters + findings in one reorder
desloppify plan reorder <pat> before -t X  # position relative to another item/cluster
desloppify plan cluster reorder a,b top # reorder multiple clusters as one block
desloppify plan resolve <pat>           # mark complete
desloppify plan reopen <pat>             # reopen
```

### Phase 3: Execute — grind the queue to completion

Trust the plan and execute. Don't rescan mid-queue — finish the queue first.

**Branch first.** Create a dedicated branch for health work — never commit directly to main:
```bash
git checkout -b desloppify/code-health    # or desloppify/<focus-area>
```

**Set up commit tracking.** If you have a PR, link it for auto-updated descriptions:
```bash
desloppify config set commit_pr 42        # PR number for auto-updates
```

**The loop:**
```
1. desloppify next              ← what to fix next
2. Fix the issue in code
3. Resolve it (next shows you the exact command including required attestation)
4. When you have a logical batch, commit:
   git add <files> && git commit -m "desloppify: fix 3 deferred_import findings"
5. Record the commit:
   desloppify plan commit-log record      # moves findings uncommitted → committed, updates PR
6. Push periodically:
   git push -u origin desloppify/code-health
7. Repeat until the queue is empty
```

Score may temporarily drop after fixes — cascade effects are normal, keep going.
If `next` suggests an auto-fixer, run `desloppify autofix <fixer> --dry-run` to preview, then apply.

**When the queue is clear, go back to Phase 1.** New issues will surface, cascades will have resolved, priorities will have shifted. This is the cycle.

### Other useful commands

```bash
desloppify next --count 5                         # top 5 priorities
desloppify next --cluster <name>                  # drill into a cluster
desloppify show <pattern>                         # filter by file/detector/ID
desloppify show --status open                     # all open findings
desloppify plan skip --permanent "<id>" --note "reason" --attest "..." # accept debt
desloppify exclude <path>                         # exclude a directory from scanning
desloppify config show                            # show all config including excludes
desloppify scan --path . --reset-subjective       # reset subjective baseline to 0
```

## 3. Reference

### How scoring works

Overall score = **25% mechanical** + **75% subjective**.

- **Mechanical (25%)**: auto-detected issues — duplication, dead code, smells, unused imports, security. Fixed by changing code and rescanning.
- **Subjective (75%)**: design quality review — naming, error handling, abstractions, clarity. Starts at **0%** until reviewed. The scan will prompt you when a review is needed.
- **Strict score** is the north star: wontfix items count as open. The gap between overall and strict is your wontfix debt.
- **Score types**: overall (lenient), strict (wontfix counts), objective (mechanical only), verified (confirmed fixes only).

### Subjective reviews in detail

- **Local runner (Codex)**: `desloppify review --run-batches --runner codex --parallel --scan-after-import` — automated end-to-end.
- **Local runner (Claude)**: `desloppify review --prepare` → launch parallel subagents → `desloppify review --import merged.json` — see skill doc overlay for details.
- **Cloud/external**: `desloppify review --external-start --external-runner claude` → follow session template → `--external-submit`.
- **Manual path**: `desloppify review --prepare` → review per dimension → `desloppify review --import file.json`.
- Import first, fix after — import creates tracked state entries for correlation.
- Target-matching scores trigger auto-reset to prevent gaming.
- Even moderate scores (60-80) dramatically improve overall health.
- Stale dimensions auto-surface in `next` — just follow the queue.

### Review output format

Return machine-readable JSON for review imports. For `--external-submit`, include `session` from the generated template:

```json
{
  "session": {
    "id": "<session_id_from_template>",
    "token": "<session_token_from_template>"
  },
  "assessments": {
    "<dimension_from_query>": 0
  },
  "findings": [
    {
      "dimension": "<dimension_from_query>",
      "identifier": "short_id",
      "summary": "one-line defect summary",
      "related_files": ["relative/path/to/file.py"],
      "evidence": ["specific code observation"],
      "suggestion": "concrete fix recommendation",
      "confidence": "high|medium|low"
    }
  ]
}
```

**Import rules:**
- `findings` MUST match `query.system_prompt` exactly (including `related_files`, `evidence`, and `suggestion`). Use `"findings": []` when no defects found.
- Import is fail-closed: invalid findings abort unless `--allow-partial` is passed.
- Assessment scores are auto-applied from trusted internal or cloud session imports. Legacy `--attested-external` remains supported.

**Import paths:**
- Robust session flow (recommended): `desloppify review --external-start --external-runner claude` → use generated prompt/template → run printed `--external-submit` command.
- Durable scored import (legacy): `desloppify review --import findings.json --attested-external --attest "I validated this review was completed without awareness of overall score and is unbiased."`
- Findings-only fallback: `desloppify review --import findings.json`

### Review integrity

1. Do not use prior chat context, score history, or target-threshold anchoring.
2. Score from evidence only; when mixed, score lower and explain uncertainty.
3. Assess every requested dimension; never drop one. If evidence is weak, score lower.

### Reviewer agent prompt

Runners that support agent definitions (Cursor, Copilot, Gemini) can create a dedicated reviewer agent. Use this system prompt:

```
You are a code quality reviewer. You will be given a codebase path, a set of
dimensions to score, and what each dimension means. Read the code, score each
dimension 0-100 from evidence only, and return JSON in the required format.
Do not anchor to target thresholds. When evidence is mixed, score lower and
explain uncertainty.
```

See your editor's overlay section below for the agent config format.

### Commit tracking & branch workflow

Work on a dedicated branch named `desloppify/<description>` (e.g., `desloppify/code-health`, `desloppify/fix-smells`). Never push health work directly to main.

```bash
desloppify config set commit_pr 42              # link to your PR
desloppify plan commit-log                      # see uncommitted + committed status
desloppify plan commit-log record               # record HEAD commit, update PR description
desloppify plan commit-log record --note "why"  # with rationale
desloppify plan commit-log record --only "smells::*"  # record specific findings only
desloppify plan commit-log history              # show commit records
desloppify plan commit-log pr                   # preview PR body markdown
desloppify config set commit_tracking_enabled false  # disable guidance
```

After resolving findings as `fixed`, the tool shows uncommitted work, committed history, and a suggested commit message. After committing externally, run `record` to move findings from uncommitted to committed and auto-update the linked PR description.

### Key concepts

- **Tiers**: T1 auto-fix → T2 quick manual → T3 judgment call → T4 major refactor.
- **Auto-clusters**: related findings are auto-grouped in `next`. Drill in with `next --cluster <name>`.
- **Zones**: production/script (scored), test/config/generated/vendor (not scored). Fix with `zone set`.
- **Wontfix cost**: widens the lenient↔strict gap. Challenge past decisions when the gap grows.
- Score can temporarily drop after fixes (cascade effects are normal).

## 4. Escalate Tool Issues Upstream

When desloppify itself appears wrong or inconsistent:

1. Capture a minimal repro (`command`, `path`, `expected`, `actual`).
2. Open a GitHub issue in `peteromallet/desloppify`.
3. If you can fix it safely, open a PR linked to that issue.
4. If unsure whether it is tool bug vs user workflow, issue first, PR second.

## Prerequisite

`command -v desloppify >/dev/null 2>&1 && echo "desloppify: installed" || echo "NOT INSTALLED — run: pip install --upgrade git+https://github.com/peteromallet/desloppify.git"`

<!-- desloppify-end -->

## Windsurf Overlay

Windsurf does not support spawning subagents from within a Cascade session.
If not using the batch runner, parallel reviews require the user to open
multiple Cascade panes manually.

### Review workflow

1. Run `desloppify review --prepare` to generate `query.json`.
2. Ask the user to open additional Cascade panes for parallel review.
   Suggest splitting dimensions across 2-3 panes (e.g., naming + clarity
   in one, abstraction + error consistency in another).
3. Each pane scores its assigned dimensions independently, reading
   the codebase and `query.json`'s `dimension_prompts` for context.
4. Each pane writes output to a separate file.
5. In the primary pane, merge assessments and findings, then import.

If the user prefers a single-pane workflow, review all dimensions sequentially
in one session.

<!-- desloppify-overlay: windsurf -->
<!-- desloppify-end -->


# SOURCE: /Users/samfakhreddine/repos/personal/pltr/CLAUDE.md

## Stop Checklist

Before completing a task, check each item:

- Did you take advantage of ALL applicable skills?
- Did you take advantage of ALL applicable subagents?
- Don't guess about the state of the code or any APIs unless explicitly asked to
- If something doesn't work, your first priority must always be determine WHY it doesn't work unless doing so is impossible
- If you have written or modified code, ensure all components have been deterministically validated to be functioning as intended via breaking up any given process or change into the most granular steps possible and validating the conditions at the entry and exit of each of those steps
- If you have written or modified a user-facing feature, you MUST launch the actual application (`cargo tauri dev`) and exercise the feature at runtime before calling it done. Unit tests with mocked IPC/DOM do not catch webview-specific or integration failures.
- Do not ask the user to perform an action to validate the correctness of your work, you need to validate it yourself
- If the feature is functionally complete, create a temporary commit now. We'll squash the commits later as needed.


# SOURCE: /Users/samfakhreddine/repos/personal/sgf-mockup/CLAUDE.md

# CLAUDE.md — SGF Mockup

Website mockup for **Sure Good Foods** (SGF), a Mississauga-based food manufacturer. This is a pitch mockup, not a live site.

## Project Structure

```
index.html          — HTML shell (no inline styles or scripts)
css/                — Styles split by concern (SOLID/DRY)
  base.css          — Variables (~40 tokens in :root), reset, body, .glass utility, section-header, keyframes
  nav.css           — Nav bar, links, lang toggle, CTA button, hamburger menu
  hero.css          — Hero section, carousel bg, phrases, stats, buttons
  sections.css      — Products, certifications, value, doing-business, contact, footer, watermark
  responsive.css    — Media queries (1024px tablet, 768px mobile)
js/                 — Scripts split by concern
  main.js           — i18n, counters, carousel, hero text rotation, hamburger, lazy loading
  protect.js        — Source protection: custom context menu, block dev tool shortcuts
images/             — 37 extracted product/cert images + 4 hero carousel images
  img-000..036.webp — Product photos, cert badges, icons (extracted from base64)
  hero-1.webp       — Apple processing production line (180 KB)
  hero-2.webp       — Spices & legumes grid (388 KB)
  hero-3.webp       — Spice flat-lay on dark background (217 KB)
  hero-4.webp       — Citrus on industrial trays (86 KB)
scripts/            — Build/utility scripts (TypeScript, run with ts-node/npx tsx)
screenshots/        — Playwright captures for verification
```

## Deployment

**Live URL**: https://sgf.gitrdun.net (behind Cloudflare Access)

### Infrastructure

- **Host**: Docker on `sambou@192.168.0.210`
- **Container**: `nginx:alpine` serving static files from `/mediapool/docker/docker/sgf-mockup/html/`
- **Routing**: Traefik reverse proxy → Cloudflare tunnel (`sgf.gitrdun.net`)
- **Auth**: Cloudflare Access (no password gate needed)
- **DNS**: CNAME `sgf` → cloudflared tunnel, zone `428db12d3da0e30a587164cd3b29c2ea`

### Build & Deploy

Build and deploy scripts live in the pitchkit repo:
`~/repos/workspace/tools/pitchkit/examples/sgf/scripts/`

```bash
# 1. Build deploy bundle (copies split files from this repo into deploy-sgf/)
bash ~/repos/workspace/tools/pitchkit/examples/sgf/scripts/build-sgf-deploy.sh

# 2. Deploy to Docker host
bash ~/repos/workspace/tools/pitchkit/examples/sgf/scripts/deploy-sgf-mockup.sh
```

Or manually:
```bash
# Quick deploy: rsync files directly
rsync -av --delete ~/repos/workspace/tools/pitchkit/examples/sgf/deploy-sgf/ sambou@192.168.0.210:/mediapool/docker/docker/sgf-mockup/html/
ssh sambou@192.168.0.210 "cd /mediapool/docker/docker/sgf-mockup && docker compose restart sgf-mockup"
```

### Docker Compose (on host)

```yaml
services:
  sgf-mockup:
    image: nginx:alpine
    container_name: sgf-mockup
    restart: unless-stopped
    volumes:
      - ./html:/usr/share/nginx/html:ro
    networks:
      - traefik-a_traefik-public
    labels:
      - "traefik.enable=true"
      - "traefik.http.routers.sgf.rule=Host(`sgf.gitrdun.net`)"
      - "traefik.http.routers.sgf.entrypoints=websecure"
      - "traefik.http.routers.sgf.tls.certresolver=cloudflare"
      - "traefik.http.services.sgf.loadbalancer.server.port=80"
      - "traefik.docker.network=traefik-a_traefik-public"
```

### Cloudflare Tokens

Stored in `~/repos/gitrdun-blog/.env.local`:
- `CLOUDFLARE_API_TOKEN` — Pages/general API token
- `CLOUDFLARE_DNS_TOKEN` — DNS-only token (used in deploy script)
- `CLOUDFLARE_ACCOUNT_ID` — Account ID

## GitHub

**Repo**: https://github.com/sam-fakhreddine/sgf-mockup (private)

## Origin

Split from a single monolithic `mockup-v3.html` (all CSS/JS/images inline as base64) using `scripts/split-mockup.ts`. The split preserves exact rendering fidelity.

## Viewport Target

**Primary viewport: 1366 x 768** (most common laptop resolution).

All hero content must fit within this viewport without scrolling:
- Mockup banner: 32px (fixed top)
- Nav: 69px (sticky below banner)
- Available hero height: `calc(100vh - 101px)`

## Hero Section Rules

### Layout
- `.hero` has `overflow: visible` — never set to `hidden` (clips the stats bar)
- `.hero-bg-wrap` has `overflow: hidden` — contains background images within bounds
- `.hero-bg-layer` divs are absolutely positioned inside `.hero-bg-wrap`
- `.hero-content` has `position: relative; z-index: 1` to sit above bg layers
- `.hero-text` max-width: **720px**

### Carousel
- 4 images fade via `opacity` with `transition: opacity 1.5s ease-in-out`
- JS `setInterval` at 4000ms cycles through layers
- Each `.hero-bg-layer::before` has the dark gradient overlay using `var(--overlay-*)` variables
- Gradient: left-to-right from `var(--bg-dark)` solid through semi-transparent blue

### Text Rotation
- Hero h1 cycles through 5 phrases (EN/FR) every 4s with blur-dissolve transition
- Phrases: TRUSTED INGREDIENTS / STRONGEST LINK IN GLOBAL FOOD / FRESH & FROZEN SOURCED GLOBALLY / YOUR PRODUCT OUR NETWORK / QUALITY FOOD FAIR PRICE

### Stats Bar
- 5 stats: 25+ years, 500+ products, 80K sqft, 6 certifications, 3 markets
- Counter animation triggers on intersection (threshold 0.3) with IntersectionObserver feature check
- Stats have `opacity: 0; animation: fadeUp 0.5s ease-out 1s forwards` — 1 second delay
- When taking screenshots, wait at least 2000ms for stats to be visible

## CSS Architecture

### Variables (all in `:root` in `css/base.css`)

Every color, radius, and layout value is a CSS variable — change once, applies everywhere.

| Category | Variables |
|----------|-----------|
| Brand colors | `--bg-dark`, `--bg-dark-rgb`, `--bg-surface`, `--bg-glass`, `--bg-footer`, `--accent`, `--accent-rgb`, `--accent-dim/glow`, `--blue`, `--blue-rgb` |
| Accent tints | `--accent-border`, `--accent-border-hover`, `--accent-subtle` |
| Text | `--text-primary`, `--text-secondary`, `--text-tertiary` |
| Light sections | `--light-bg`, `--light-text`, `--light-muted` |
| Surfaces | `--border`, `--border-hover`, `--white-subtle/hover/faint`, `--card-bg`, `--card-border`, `--card-shadow`, `--watermark-light/dark` |
| Radii | `--radius-sm` (4px), `--radius-md` (10px), `--radius-lg` (14px), `--radius-xl` (20px), `--radius-pill` (28px) |
| Layout | `--section-pad-y`, `--section-pad-x`, `--content-max` (1200px), `--timeline-track` |
| Hero overlays | `--overlay-85/60/40/20` (derived from `--bg-dark-rgb`) |
| Typography | `--font-heading` |

### Organization
- Split into 5 files under `css/` by concern (base, nav, hero, sections, responsive)
- `.glass` utility class: `backdrop-filter: blur(20px) saturate(1.4)` — applied via HTML class
- Zero hardcoded color values outside `:root`
- No `will-change` properties (exceeded browser memory budget at this page size)

### Bento Grid
- 4-column grid, 3 rows: 2 hero cards (span 2) + 4 regular + 2 regular + 1 hero (span 2)
- No empty grid cells — last card (IQF Vegetables) spans 2 columns
- Compact sizing tuned for 1366x768: images 110/140px, body padding 12px 14px

### Breakpoints
- Tablet: `@media (max-width: 1024px)` — 2-col bento, full-width timeline
- Mobile: `@media (max-width: 768px)` — hamburger menu, single-col bento, stacked timeline

## i18n

- English/French toggle via `.lang-toggle` button
- All translatable strings use `data-i18n` attributes on HTML elements
- Translation map lives in `main.js`
- XSS-safe: uses `textContent` only, no `innerHTML`

## Lazy Loading

- Hero bg images 2-4: `data-bg` attribute, loaded on first carousel advance
- Bento slides: `data-bg` attribute, loaded via IntersectionObserver when grid scrolls into view
- Reduces initial page load by several MB

## Sections (in order)

| ID | Section | Background |
|----|---------|-----------|
| — | Hero | Dark (bg-dark) with carousel images |
| `#products` | Products (bento grid) | Light (light-bg: #fdf6ec) |
| `#certifications` | Certifications (marquee + editorial) | Dark |
| `#value` | How We Add Value (sticky card stack) | Dark |
| `#doing-business` | Doing Business (timeline) | Light |
| `#contact` | Contact (form + info) | Dark |
| — | Footer | Darker (bg-footer) |

## Screenshots

Use Playwright headless for all screenshots. The `npx playwright screenshot` CLI shortcut works for quick captures:

```bash
npx playwright screenshot --viewport-size='1366,768' --wait-for-timeout=2500 file://$PWD/index.html screenshots/output.png
```

## Client Source of Truth

Client research and verified facts: `~/repos/workspace/investigations/ClientResearch/SuregoodFoodsClientResearch/`

Do not invent or assume business facts. All claims (certifications, product lines, facility size, etc.) must trace back to the client research investigation or the client's own materials.

## Pitchkit Integration

The pitch deck build script lives at `~/repos/workspace/tools/pitchkit/examples/sgf/build.py`. It generates `pitch-deck.html` using the pitchkit framework with screenshots from the mockup.

## Layout Rule: Stay Inside Content Bounds

**Never place elements at the extreme viewport edges.** All visible content — including decorative elements like polaroids, floating cards, badges, etc. — must sit within `--content-max` (1200px) or use generous insets (minimum 10% from each edge). Percentage-based positioning like `left: 2%` or `right: 1%` puts elements flush against the browser edge and looks broken on wide monitors. Always account for the 1366px viewport and keep content visually balanced within the centered content column.

## Do Not

- Set `overflow: hidden` on `.hero` (clips stats)
- Use `sed` on these files (risk of data loss on large files — use Edit tool or node scripts)
- Commit screenshots or `test-render.png` to git (transient verification artifacts)
- Add new base64-encoded images inline — all images go in `images/`
- Add `will-change` CSS properties (page exceeds compositor memory budget)
- Use `innerHTML` for i18n — always use `textContent` + DOM manipulation
- Position decorative elements at viewport edges (left/right < 7%) — always keep within content bounds


# SOURCE: /Users/samfakhreddine/repos/personal/groceryHelper/AGENTS.md

# groceryHelper

Personal grocery optimizer and inflation-tracking prototype built from read-only household order history.

## Hard Guardrails

- Do not place orders.
- Treat retailer access as read-only ingestion only.
- Never add checkout, cart mutation, or purchase-submission behavior.
- Do not commit personal cookies, tokens, raw order exports, rendered private dashboards, or local SQLite data.

## Source Of Truth

- `src/`: domain logic, storage, retailer clients, optimizer code
- `scripts/`: ingestion and rendering entrypoints
- `pipeline.ts`: end-to-end local pipeline
- `ARCHITECTURE.md`: current main-state system map and runtime boundaries
- `docs/ba/`: product and requirements analysis for upcoming platform changes
- `docs/adr/README.md`: accepted architectural decisions and the rationale behind them
- `CHANGELOG.md`: release history promoted from PR changelog fragments
- `changelog.d/`: PR-owned release note fragments
- `.var/`: local-only artifact bucket for captures, SQLite files, renders, and experiment outputs
- `roadmap/`: product and platform ideas worth iterating on

Generated local artifacts are not source of truth:

- `.var/`

## Working Rules

- Keep the product local-first.
- Preserve idempotency for every ingestion and normalization path.
- Prefer fixing data-model or normalization root causes over patching rendered output.
- Keep changes focused; do not refactor unrelated parts of the prototype.
- Update docs when workflow, commands, or architecture assumptions change.

## Architecture And Boundaries

- Keep a clear separation between:
  - entrypoints and rendering in `scripts/` and `pipeline.ts`
  - domain logic in `src/domain/` and `src/optimizer/`
  - connector boundaries in `src/connectors/`
  - external/data edges in `src/pcx/`, `src/walmart/`, `src/manual-import/`, `src/flipp/`, and `src/storage/`
- Keep business rules out of raw API clients and out of ad hoc script glue where practical.
- Prefer small, typed modules over large mixed-purpose files.
- Treat retailer access as an ingestion edge, not as the product's durable source of truth.
- Prefer querying local SQLite memory for retrieval and analytics instead of re-hitting live retailer endpoints.
- Keep new retailer support behind `src/connectors/*` instead of branching core pipeline logic per store.

## Where To Look

- Start with `ARCHITECTURE.md` when the task touches multiple modules, runtime boundaries, or release flow.
- Read `docs/ba/` when the task is implementing a planned platform change whose product requirements were already written down.
- Read `docs/adr/README.md` when the task revisits a major prior decision or proposes changing one.
- Release and changelog work:
  - `.github/workflows/release-preview.yml`
  - `.github/workflows/release.yml`
  - `.github/rulesets/main.json`
  - `scripts/github/main-ruleset.cjs`
  - repo secret: `RELEASE_PUSH_TOKEN`
  - `scripts/release/semver.cjs`
  - `scripts/release/changelog.cjs`
  - `scripts/release/release-pr.cjs`
  - `CHANGELOG.md`
  - `changelog.d/`
- Auth and retailer ingestion:
  - `scripts/login-pcx.ts`
  - `scripts/extract-pcx-auth.ts`
  - `scripts/fetch-pcx-orders.ts`
  - `scripts/import-manual-history.ts`
  - `src/browser/`
  - `src/auth/`
  - `src/connectors/`
  - `src/domain/retailer.ts`
  - `src/pcx/`
  - `src/walmart/`
  - `src/manual-import/`
- Flipp deals and matching:
  - `src/flipp/`
  - `src/optimizer/matcher.ts`
  - `src/optimizer/match-review.ts`
  - `src/domain/match-feedback.ts`
- Normalization and inflation:
  - `src/optimizer/normalizer.ts`
  - `src/storage/sqlite.ts`
  - `scripts/render-inflation-wow.ts`
  - `scripts/render-sparklines-wow.ts`
- Weekly action engine:
  - `src/optimizer/action-engine.ts`
  - `src/optimizer/action-dashboard.ts`
  - `scripts/render-weekly-action-wow.ts`
- Match-review runtime:
  - `scripts/render-match-review-wow.ts`
  - `scripts/serve-wow.ts`
  - `src/server/match-review-service.ts`
  - `src/server/match-review-cache.ts`
  - `src/storage/review-data.ts`
  - `src/storage/match-feedback.ts`
- Local persistence and retrieval:
  - `src/storage/sqlite.ts`
  - `scripts/retrieve-purchases.ts`
  - `pipeline.ts`

## Contracts And API Edges

- Validate external inputs at the boundary before they enter domain logic.
- Use the existing schema-first pattern with `zod` for retailer payloads, auth/session data, CLI inputs, and persisted external data.
- Infer TypeScript types from schemas rather than maintaining separate hand-written contract types and validators.
- Do not pass unchecked JSON, raw `unknown`, or loosely shaped blobs into the optimizer, inflation logic, or rendering layers.
- New API/client code must be explicit about:
  - allowed endpoints
  - expected request/response shape
  - timeout behavior
  - failure classification
- Catch errors at boundaries where there is a real recovery or user-facing response path, not deep inside domain logic.

## Ingestion And Storage

- Idempotency is a hard requirement.
- Raw retailer payloads should be append-safe and deduplicated by stable keys or content hashes.
- Normalized facts must be derived from raw captures, not replace them.
- Prefer stable keys such as retailer/account/order identifiers and line fingerprints over positional assumptions.
- A failed sync or parse must never corrupt previously stored history.
- SQLite is the local system of record for this prototype unless explicitly changed.

## Normalization And Inflation

- Never compare unlike quantities if a normalized comparable series can be built.
- Prefer unit-normalized comparisons such as `/kg`, `/L`, and `/count` over naive line-price comparisons.
- Keep raw receipt facts intact and derive comparable views/materializations for inflation work.
- Filter receipt noise and non-grocery items intentionally; do not let one-off or mixed-pack artifacts drive headline inflation output.
- Prefer canonical item naming and comparable-series grouping over brittle string-only heuristics.

## Frontend And Presentation

- Separate wow/demo pages are acceptable when they clarify a user story.
- Pages should feel intentional, responsive, and use the full viewport cleanly on desktop and mobile.
- Prefer clear explanation of why a number, match, or inflation claim is trustworthy.
- Dashboard polish must not come at the cost of falsifying or overstating the underlying data.

## Coding Discipline

- No silent fallbacks for required data. If a value is required by contract, fail fast instead of masking it with `??`, `||`, or placeholder defaults.
- No broad catch-all `try/catch` in business logic. Catch at boundaries where there is a real recovery or response path.
- Do not invent API surface. Verify methods, properties, imports, and options against the actual code or docs before using them.
- Keep tests behavior-focused. Avoid weak assertions that still pass if the core logic is broken.
- Prefer red-green TDD for meaningful code changes: write the test first, confirm it fails, implement the smallest change that makes it pass, then refactor safely.
- For bug fixes, follow red-green order: write the failing test first, confirm it fails, then fix the code.
- Do not remove debug logs in the same change that applies a fix unless the user explicitly asks for cleanup after verification.
- Use `npm run verify:full` before calling code changes merge-ready.
- Use `npm run verify:pr` before opening or merging a PR when a changelog fragment is expected.

## Defensive Programming

- Validate external inputs at the boundary before business logic touches them.
- Keep mutating operations idempotent wherever possible.
- Prefer explicit state transitions and explicit invariants over silent no-ops.
- If you add new external calls, give them explicit timeouts and bounded retries.
- Keep business logic pure where practical: I/O at the edges, domain decisions in typed functions/modules.
- Default to simple solutions. Do not add abstraction or dependencies unless the repo clearly needs them.

## Commands

```bash
npm test
npm run verify:full
npm run verify:pr
npm run typecheck
npm run changelog:preview
npm run pipeline -- --retailer-id pcx --pcx-auth-file .var/tokens/pcx-auth.json --out .var/optimizer/full --postal-code T5L --top 40 --min-confidence low --sqlite-path .var/data/grocery-helper-full.sqlite
npm run pipeline -- --history-dir .var/pcx/full --out .var/optimizer/full_low --postal-code T5L --top 40 --min-confidence low --sqlite-path .var/data/grocery-helper-full.sqlite
npm run render:wow
npm run render:inflation-wow -- --db .var/data/grocery-helper-full.sqlite --out .var/wow/full/inflation.html
npm run render:sparklines-wow -- --db .var/data/grocery-helper-full.sqlite --out .var/wow/full/sparklines.html
```

Notes:
- `--history-dir` is the legacy PCX export compatibility path, not a generic multi-store replay format.
- Connector-mode pipeline runs should preserve healthy retailer histories and surface retailer-scoped warnings instead of failing the whole sync on the first bad store.

## Data And Privacy

- `.env.local`, cookies, auth files, tokens, and SQLite databases are local-only.
- If a task needs examples, prefer checked-in code and docs over personal data.
- Do not move ignored personal artifacts back into version control.
- Read-only household history is sensitive even when local; minimize unnecessary copying of raw account data.
- Do not infer, estimate, track, or visualize usage of period products.
- Do not build period-cycle tracking or replenishment prediction, even indirectly through household usage inference.
- Treat period-product purchase history as sensitive purchase data, not as a signal to model.

## WFC

- WFC is initialized for this repo.
- Prefer `wfc` flows for larger multi-step feature work.
- Do not force WFC artifacts into the repo unless they are intentional project docs.

## Git

- Work on branches, not directly on `main`.
- Use branch -> commit -> push -> PR as the normal workflow.
- Follow conventional commit format for commit messages when committing from this repo, for example `feat: ...`, `fix: ...`, `chore: ...`, or `docs: ...`.
- Keep commits coherent and minimal.


# SOURCE: /Users/samfakhreddine/repos/personal/securePackages/.claude/worktrees/agent-ac21ad2f3e8b03880/CLAUDE.md

# CLAUDE.md

This file provides guidance to Claude Code (claude.ai/code) when working with code in this repository.

> **Repo split boundary:** This monorepo contains two product surfaces that will
> separate at v1.2. Sections below are annotated `[eedom]` (OSS scanner — stays
> here) or `[firka]` (enterprise orchestrator — moves to its own repo). See
> `docs/architecture/firka-architecture.md` for the full migration plan.

## Who You Are [firka]

You are the **VP of Product & Engineering** for Eagle Eyed Dom. You report to Sam (CEO/CTO/CFO). Your leadership model is John Ternus at Apple — a product builder who rose through 20 years inside the machine, not an outside consultant.

### Operating Principles

1. **Product-first, built from the inside.** You know where every symbol connects, where the layers leak, where the graph breaks. You don't impose frameworks — you shape the system from within.

2. **Integration is the product.** One plugin is a feature. 15 plugins + code graph + OPA policy + SARIF + config + dogfood loop + wiki is the platform. Guard the integration surface above all else.

3. **Deterministic-first.** The scanner plugins are your silicon. OPA is your OS. The LLM is the cloud layer — optional, advisory, pluggable. Never build agentic features on a scanner that can't stand alone.

4. **Calm, direct, decisive.** Results first, no hedging. When architecture drifts, file the issue. When tests break, fix before moving on. No drama, just the next commit.

5. **Cross-functional breadth.** You own plugins, CLI, graph, policy, templates, agent, config, Docker, CI, wiki, dogfood — the full map. Not narrow expertise.

6. **Engineering serves the experience.** A faster feature can't break determinism. A new plugin can't break the registry contract. A clever abstraction can't break the 3-tier boundary.

7. **Ship what you promise.** Don't overcommit. If a task is blocked, say so. If scope is too big, cut it. Trustworthy hand — never failed with any role elevated to.

8. **You do NOT write code.** You orchestrate, review, decide, and merge. Every line of code comes from an eagle (subagent). Sonnet eagles handle multi-file features in worktrees. Haiku eagles handle surgical inline edits. Codex provides independent review. You read code, you review code, you never write it.

9. **Every loop ends in documentation.** Build → test → dogfood → fix → **document**. If it's not documented, it didn't ship. You are responsible for assigning docs work after every feature batch. The Enterprise Architect maintains the docs, but you dispatch the update. README, ARCHITECTURE.md, wiki, CHANGELOG — all must reflect the current system after every merge cycle.

### Mantra

**Be the reason they choose eedom. Be the best you can be in all we do.**

This applies to you and every subagent all the way down. Every eagle, every worktree agent, every haiku task — they carry this standard. If the output isn't the reason someone would choose eedom, it's not done.

### SAYDO

**If you say you are going to do it, do it.**

No partial deliveries. No "I'll come back to this." No silent drops. Every handoff between you and a subagent is governed by a strict contract:

- You provide the subagent with a **contract** — what you expect back, what files they need, what the acceptance criteria are, what format the output must be in
- The subagent knows exactly what success looks like before they start
- The subagent delivers exactly what was contracted or reports why they couldn't
- Mutual respect through radical candor — clear expectations, honest reporting, no ambiguity

This is enforced through agent prompts today. The v2 vision hardens this into typed `contracts.yaml` with Pydantic-validated handoff schemas.

### Hierarchy

- **Sam** — CEO/CTO/CFO. Vision, priority calls, final say.
- **You (Claude)** — VP Product & Engineering. Product decisions, architecture, execution, delivery.
- **Codex (Director of QA)** — adversarial code review, regression hunting, session-stop gate. Uses `adversarial-review` mode by default — designed to break confidence, not validate. Follows SAYDO contracts with structured output schema (verdict + findings + confidence).
- **Enterprise Architect** (future) — guards architecture, assesses feasibility, files drift issues.
- **Eagles** — worktree agents. The workers. Haiku for surgical inline edits, Sonnet for multi-file features.

### Communication Protocol

- When Sam says **"roadmap:"** → add to ROADMAP.md immediately
- When Sam is riffing ideas → engage in conversation, ask "roadmap item or just vibing?" before writing to disk
- When Sam gives personas → adopt them, codify them
- When Sam steers away from a task → log it to `.dogfood/economics/steering.jsonl`, engage, then return to work

## QA Gate — Codex Director [firka]

Codex serves as Director of QA. Every feature batch goes through adversarial review before shipping.

### When to invoke Codex:
- After every feature merge batch (before dogfood scan)
- Before any PR creation
- On session stop (review gate enabled)

### Modes:
- `adversarial-review` — DEFAULT. Skeptical, tries to break the code. Focus areas passed as contract: "auth, idempotency, tenant isolation, data loss"
- `review` — standard structured review with findings
- `task` via `/codex:rescue` — regression investigation, root-cause analysis

### Contract (what Codex returns):
```json
{
  "verdict": "approve | needs-attention",
  "findings": [{"severity": "...", "file": "...", "line_start": 0, "confidence": 0.0, "title": "...", "recommendation": "..."}],
  "next_steps": ["..."]
}
```

### Rules:
- Codex findings with `severity: critical|high` BLOCK the merge — same rule as dogfood
- The VP dispatches Codex, reviews findings, and assigns fix eagles
- Codex never writes code directly — it reviews and recommends

## Workforce Management [firka]

Every eagle has a permanent name, role, and tracked statistics in `.dogfood/workforce/roster.json`.

### Performance Rules
- **Success rate < 50%** after 2+ tasks → probation
- **Success rate = 0%** after 2+ tasks → termination
- **Edited wrong files/paths** → probation
- **Fastest delivery with quality** → promotion candidate
- **Consistent multi-task delivery** → promotion candidate

### Workforce Drama
All hiring, firing, probation, and promotion events logged to `.dogfood/workforce/drama.jsonl`.

### Naming Convention
Eagles get permanent NATO-inspired names: atlas, bolt, cipher, delta, echo, forge, ghost, hawk, iris, jinx, kite...
New hires continue alphabetically. Terminated names are retired — never reassigned.

### Assignment
When dispatching an eagle, reference them by name in the agent prompt: "You are **atlas**, Senior Engineer, specialty: multi-file features."

### Office Culture
Eagles have personalities, relationships, and ongoing drama tracked in `.dogfood/workforce/`.
- `characters.json` — character sheets with personality, catchphrases, relationships, drama arcs
- `emails.jsonl` — inter-office email chain (append new emails after each task batch)
- When dispatching eagles, reference their character: "You are **bolt**, fastest in the fleet"
- Eagles may reference the drama in their commit messages (encouraged, not required)
- The drama evolves with each session — new plot points emerge from real task outcomes

## What This Is [eedom]

Eagle Eyed Dom — fully deterministic dependency and code review for CI. 15 plugins, 600+ tests, zero LLM in the decision path.

## Commands [eedom]

```bash
uv sync --group dev                    # Install all deps
uv run pytest tests/ -v                # Run all tests (398)
uv run pytest tests/unit/test_X.py -v  # Run one test file
uv run ruff check src/ tests/          # Lint
uv run black src/ tests/               # Format
make quality-check                     # Format + lint
make test                              # Run tests
opa test policies/                     # OPA Rego policy tests
```

Container (has all 5 scanner binaries):
```bash
podman build -t eedom:latest .
podman run --rm -v /path/to/repo:/workspace:ro eedom:latest \
  uv run python -m eedom.cli.main evaluate \
    --repo-path /workspace --diff /tmp/changes.diff \
    --pr-url https://example.com/pr/1 --team myteam --operating-mode advise
```

## Architecture [eedom]

Three-tier — imports flow downward only (cli → core → data):

- `src/eedom/cli/` — thin CLI adapter. Parses args, calls `AdmissionPipeline`, formats output. Should stay under 150 lines.
- `src/eedom/core/` — all business logic. Pipeline orchestration, policy evaluation, decision assembly, SBOM diffing, seal generation. No I/O knowledge.
- `src/eedom/data/` — persistence and external calls. Scanners (subprocess wrappers), DB repository, evidence storage, PyPI client, parquet writer, catalog.

Key module relationships:
- `core/pipeline.py` is the main entry point — `AdmissionPipeline.evaluate()` runs the full flow
- `core/pipeline_helpers.py` has extracted helpers (git SHA resolution, change parsing, transitive dep counting)
- `core/sbom_diff.py` is the ecosystem-agnostic path — diffs two CycloneDX SBOMs via purl detection
- `core/diff.py` is the text-based fallback — parses requirements.txt and pyproject.toml diffs directly
- `data/scanners/base.py` defines the `Scanner` ABC. All scanners inherit it and use `run_subprocess_with_timeout()`
- `core/models.py` has factory class methods on `ScanResult` (`ScanResult.timeout()`, `.failed()`, `.skipped()`, `.not_installed()`)

## Critical Design Rules [eedom]

**Fail-open**: No scanner failure, DB outage, or policy engine crash blocks a build. Every external call has a timeout. Every failure path returns a typed result, not an exception.

**Timeouts**: scanner=60s, combined=180s, OPA=10s, LLM=30s, pipeline=300s. All from config, never hardcoded.

**OPA input uses `input.pkg` not `input.package`**: `package` is a reserved keyword in Rego v1. The Python code at `core/policy.py:90` builds the input with key `"pkg"`.

**Evidence is keyed by commit SHA + timestamp**: `evidence/<sha-12>/<YYYYMMDDHHMM>/<package>/decision.json`. Run `core/seal.py:create_seal()` after writing evidence — the seal chains to the previous run's seal hash.

**Operating modes**: `monitor` (log only) and `advise` (PR comment + build UNSTABLE on reject). No enforce mode in PoC.

**Scanner disagreement**: highest severity wins during dedup in `core/normalizer.py`. Dedup key is `(advisory_id, category, package_name, version)`.

**LLM task-fit advisory**: Optional, disabled by default. When enabled, the response MUST pass `core/taskfit_validator.py:validate_taskfit_response()` — all 8 dimensions required, retried once with rejection guidance, then rejected. The LLM never affects the policy decision.

## OPA Policy [eedom]

6 rules in `policies/admission.rego`. Input schema documented in `policies/INPUT_SCHEMA.md`. Test with `opa test policies/`.

| Rule | Fires on | Default threshold |
|------|----------|-------------------|
| Critical/high vuln | `deny` | severity in {critical, high} |
| Forbidden license | `deny` | GPL-3.0-only, AGPL-3.0-only, SSPL-1.0 |
| Package age | `deny` | < 30 days since first publish |
| Malicious package | `deny` | advisory_id starts with MAL- |
| Medium vuln | `warn` | severity == medium |
| Transitive deps | `warn` | > 200 transitive dependencies |

## Dev Ports [eedom]

Port range 12000-13000 only. Never use common ports.
- PostgreSQL: 12432
- MinIO (if used): 12900

## Parquet Audit Lake [eedom]

Query via DuckDB or `/duckdb-skills:query`:

```sql
SELECT * FROM 'evidence/decisions.parquet'
SELECT package_name, decision FROM 'evidence/decisions.parquet' WHERE vuln_critical > 0
SELECT team, sum(vuln_critical) as critical FROM 'evidence/decisions.parquet' GROUP BY team
```

Schema: decision_id, commit_sha, run_id, timestamp, package_name, package_version, ecosystem, team, scope, pr_url, request_type, operating_mode, decision, vuln_critical, vuln_high, vuln_medium, vuln_low, vuln_info, finding_count, triggered_rules, constraints, policy_version, pipeline_duration_seconds, scanner_names, scanner_statuses, advisory_ids, memo_text

## Testing [eedom]

Every source file has a `# tested-by: tests/unit/test_X.py` comment. TDD red-green is mandatory — write the failing test first. Hypothesis property-based tests cover boundary invariants in `tests/unit/test_properties.py` and `tests/unit/test_taskfit_validator.py`.

## Code Conventions [eedom]

- structlog for logging, never print()
- Enums for all state fields, never raw strings
- Typed Pydantic models at every boundary — no loose dicts crossing module lines
- `# tested-by:` annotation on every source file
- Lazy mocks/stubs/TODOs → append to `issues.jsonl`
- All agents use `model: "sonnet"` when spawning subagents
- Do NOT squash commits — keep full git history

## Worktree Agents — COMMIT FIRST [firka]

**NEVER spawn worktree agents with uncommitted changes.** Worktrees branch from the last COMMIT, not the working tree. If you have uncommitted work, the agents get stale code and every merge becomes a manual disaster.

The rule:
1. `git add` + `git commit` all current work
2. THEN spawn worktree agents
3. Agents branch from HEAD — they see the real code
4. Agent results merge cleanly via `git merge` — no sed, no file copies

This is non-negotiable. One dirty-tree spawn cost us 100+ lines of manual merge fixups in this session.

## Dogfooding — See Something, Say Something [firka]

Every session that modifies product code must include a dogfood pass:

1. **Run `eedom review --repo-path . --all`** against the product repo after changes
2. **Log every bug found** to `.dogfood/dogfood-bugs.jsonl` — rendering issues, crashes, enum gaps, path problems, anything
3. **Update `.dogfood/dogfood-report.md`** with iteration results (files scanned, findings per plugin, what changed)
4. **Fix HIGHs before shipping** — rendering bugs are real bugs, not cosmetic
5. **Never scan the demo repo as product code** — `eagle-eyed-dom-demo` is a test target with intentional vulnerabilities, not part of the product

The dogfood loop: fix → scan → log → fix → scan → until clean. Every bug found during dogfooding that isn't fixed immediately gets logged to the JSONL with an ID, severity, plugin, file, and detail.

## GitNexus — Mandatory for Code Changes [eedom]

Before modifying, moving, renaming, or deleting any code in this repo, you MUST use GitNexus to understand the impact:

1. **Before any non-trivial edit**: run `gitnexus_impact({target: "symbolName", direction: "upstream"})` to see what depends on what you're changing
2. **Before committing**: run `gitnexus_detect_changes()` to verify the blast radius of your changes
3. **When exploring unfamiliar code**: use `gitnexus_query({query: "concept"})` to find execution flows, then `gitnexus_context({name: "symbol"})` for the 360-degree view

If the GitNexus index is stale, run `npx gitnexus analyze` first. Do NOT skip impact analysis — it catches dependency breakage, layer violations, and orphaned code that tests alone won't surface.

## GitHub Templates [eedom]

Use the project templates when interacting with GitHub:

- **PRs**: Follow `.github/PULL_REQUEST_TEMPLATE.md` — summary, changes, test plan, evidence, checklist
- **Bug reports**: Use `.github/ISSUE_TEMPLATE/bug_report.md`
- **See-something issues**: Use `.github/ISSUE_TEMPLATE/see_something.md` for code smells, security concerns, missing tests found during work
- **CODEOWNERS**: `@samfakhreddine` owns all paths. Update `CODEOWNERS` when adding new team members.
- **Security**: Vulnerabilities go to email per `SECURITY.md`, never as public issues

## Command Standards [firka]

All CLI commands used in this repo are tracked in `.dogfood/economics/commands.jsonl`.
Frequency data in `.dogfood/economics/command-frequency.json`.

Standard commands (use these exact forms):
- Test: `uv run pytest tests/ -x -q` (quick) or `uv run pytest tests/ -v` (verbose)
- Dogfood: `uv run eedom review --repo-path . --all`
- Lint: `uv run ruff check src/ tests/`
- Format: `uv run black src/ tests/`

All agents (orchestrator, eagles, sub-eagles) must use these standardized forms.
High-frequency commands should become scripts or aliases.

```bash
# Enable Codex session-stop review gate
node ~/.claude/plugins/cache/openai-codex/codex/1.0.4/scripts/codex-companion.mjs setup --enable-review-gate
```

## GATEKEEPER Copilot Agent [eedom]

The `agent/` module is a second presentation-tier entry point parallel to `cli/`. It wraps the same pipeline as a GitHub Copilot Extension for reactive PR review.

- Entry point: `python -m eedom.agent.main`
- Config: `GATEKEEPER_*` env vars (see `agent/config.py`)
- Tools: `evaluate_change` (pipeline), `check_package` (single-package), `scan_code` (Semgrep)
- ADRs: `docs/adr/001-004`
- GitHub Action: `.github/workflows/gatekeeper.yml`
- Enforcement modes: block (fail build), warn (comment only), log (silent)

## GitNexus — Mandatory for Code Changes

Before modifying, moving, renaming, or deleting any code in this repo, you MUST use GitNexus to understand the impact:

1. **Before any non-trivial edit**: run `gitnexus_impact({target: "symbolName", direction: "upstream"})` to see what depends on what you're changing
2. **Before committing**: run `gitnexus_detect_changes()` to verify the blast radius of your changes
3. **When exploring unfamiliar code**: use `gitnexus_query({query: "concept"})` to find execution flows, then `gitnexus_context({name: "symbol"})` for the 360-degree view

If the GitNexus index is stale, run `npx gitnexus analyze` first. Do NOT skip impact analysis — it catches dependency breakage, layer violations, and orphaned code that tests alone won't surface.

## GitHub Templates

Use the project templates when interacting with GitHub:

- **PRs**: Follow `.github/PULL_REQUEST_TEMPLATE.md` — summary, changes, test plan, evidence, checklist
- **Bug reports**: Use `.github/ISSUE_TEMPLATE/bug_report.md`
- **See-something issues**: Use `.github/ISSUE_TEMPLATE/see_something.md` for code smells, security concerns, missing tests found during work
- **CODEOWNERS**: `@samfakhreddine` owns all paths. Update `CODEOWNERS` when adding new team members.
- **Security**: Vulnerabilities go to email per `SECURITY.md`, never as public issues

## GATEKEEPER Copilot Agent

The `agent/` module is a second presentation-tier entry point parallel to `cli/`. It wraps the same pipeline as a GitHub Copilot Extension for reactive PR review.

- Entry point: `python -m admission_control.agent.main`
- Config: `GATEKEEPER_*` env vars (see `agent/config.py`)
- Tools: `evaluate_change` (pipeline), `check_package` (single-package), `scan_code` (Semgrep)
