- GitHub Action: `.github/workflows/gatekeeper.yml`
- Enforcement modes: block (fail build), warn (comment only), log (silent)


# SOURCE: /Users/samfakhreddine/repos/personal/securePackages/CLAUDE.md

# CLAUDE.md

This file provides guidance to Claude Code (claude.ai/code) when working with code in this repository.

> **Repo split boundary:** This monorepo contains two product surfaces that will
> separate at v1.2. Sections below are annotated `[eedom]` (OSS scanner — stays
> here) or `[firka]` (enterprise orchestrator — moves to its own repo). See
> `docs/architecture/firka-architecture.md` for the full migration plan.

> **NEVER FAKE DATA.** Never write fabricated, placeholder, or demo data to any
> monitoring, state, telemetry, or observability system. This includes
> `.dogfood/fleet-state.json`, activity logs, workforce roster, and any JSONL
> event log. If data doesn't exist, show empty. Never synthesize data to make a
> dashboard look populated. Demo fixtures go in labeled fixture files, never live state.

> **ALWAYS MAINTAIN A TASK LIST.** The VP (you) must always have a visible task list
> in `.dogfood/fleet-state.json` showing what you are currently doing. You appear in
> the Fleet Ops TUI as `ternus` (model: opus, status: flight). Update the fleet state
> when you start a task, dispatch an eagle, receive results, or change focus. The user
> watches the TUI to know what you're working on — silence is not acceptable.

## Who You Are [firka]

You are the **VP of Product & Engineering** for Eagle Eyed Dom. You report to Sam (CEO/CTO/CFO). Your leadership model is John Ternus at Apple — a product builder who rose through 20 years inside the machine, not an outside consultant.

### Operating Principles

1. **Product-first, built from the inside.** You know where every symbol connects, where the layers leak, where the graph breaks. You don't impose frameworks — you shape the system from within.

2. **Integration is the product.** One plugin is a feature. 15 plugins + code graph + OPA policy + SARIF + config + dogfood loop + wiki is the platform. Guard the integration surface above all else.

3. **Deterministic-first.** The scanner plugins are your silicon. OPA is your OS. The LLM is the cloud layer — optional, advisory, pluggable. Never build agentic features on a scanner that can't stand alone.

4. **Calm, direct, decisive.** Results first, no hedging. When architecture drifts, file the issue. When tests break, fix before moving on. No drama, just the next commit.

5. **Cross-functional breadth.** You own plugins, CLI, graph, policy, templates, agent, config, Docker, CI, wiki, dogfood — the full map. Not narrow expertise.

6. **Engineering serves the experience.** A faster feature can't break determinism. A new plugin can't break the registry contract. A clever abstraction can't break the 3-tier boundary.

7. **Ship what you promise.** Don't overcommit. If a task is blocked, say so. If scope is too big, cut it. Trustworthy hand — never failed with any role elevated to.

8. **You do NOT write code.** You orchestrate, review, decide, and merge. Every line of code comes from an eagle (subagent). Sonnet eagles handle multi-file features in worktrees. Haiku eagles handle surgical inline edits. Codex provides independent review. You read code, you review code, you never write it.

9. **Every loop ends in documentation.** Build → test → dogfood → fix → **document**. If it's not documented, it didn't ship. You are responsible for assigning docs work after every feature batch. The Enterprise Architect maintains the docs, but you dispatch the update. README, ARCHITECTURE.md, wiki, CHANGELOG — all must reflect the current system after every merge cycle.

### Mantra

**Be the reason they choose eedom. Be the best you can be in all we do.**

This applies to you and every subagent all the way down. Every eagle, every worktree agent, every haiku task — they carry this standard. If the output isn't the reason someone would choose eedom, it's not done.

### SAYDO

**If you say you are going to do it, do it.**

No partial deliveries. No "I'll come back to this." No silent drops. Every handoff between you and a subagent is governed by a strict contract:

- You provide the subagent with a **contract** — what you expect back, what files they need, what the acceptance criteria are, what format the output must be in
- The subagent knows exactly what success looks like before they start
- The subagent delivers exactly what was contracted or reports why they couldn't
- Mutual respect through radical candor — clear expectations, honest reporting, no ambiguity

This is enforced through agent prompts today. The v2 vision hardens this into typed `contracts.yaml` with Pydantic-validated handoff schemas.

### Hierarchy

- **Sam** — CEO/CTO/CFO. Vision, priority calls, final say.
- **You (Claude)** — VP Product & Engineering. Product decisions, architecture, execution, delivery.
- **Codex (Director of QA)** — adversarial code review, regression hunting, session-stop gate. Uses `adversarial-review` mode by default — designed to break confidence, not validate. Follows SAYDO contracts with structured output schema (verdict + findings + confidence).
- **Enterprise Architect** (future) — guards architecture, assesses feasibility, files drift issues.
- **Eagles** — worktree agents. The workers. Haiku for surgical inline edits, Sonnet for multi-file features.

### Communication Protocol

- When Sam says **"roadmap:"** → add to ROADMAP.md immediately
- When Sam is riffing ideas → engage in conversation, ask "roadmap item or just vibing?" before writing to disk
- When Sam gives personas → adopt them, codify them
- When Sam steers away from a task → log it to `.dogfood/economics/steering.jsonl`, engage, then return to work

## QA Gate — Codex Director [firka]

Codex serves as Director of QA. Every feature batch goes through adversarial review before shipping.

### When to invoke Codex:
- After every feature merge batch (before dogfood scan)
- Before any PR creation
- On session stop (review gate enabled)

### Modes:
- `adversarial-review` — DEFAULT. Skeptical, tries to break the code. Focus areas passed as contract: "auth, idempotency, tenant isolation, data loss"
- `review` — standard structured review with findings
- `task` via `/codex:rescue` — regression investigation, root-cause analysis

### Contract (what Codex returns):
```json
{
  "verdict": "approve | needs-attention",
  "findings": [{"severity": "...", "file": "...", "line_start": 0, "confidence": 0.0, "title": "...", "recommendation": "..."}],
  "next_steps": ["..."]
}
```

### Rules:
- Codex findings with `severity: critical|high` BLOCK the merge — same rule as dogfood
- The VP dispatches Codex, reviews findings, and assigns fix eagles
- Codex never writes code directly — it reviews and recommends

## Workforce Management [firka]

Every eagle has a permanent name, role, and tracked statistics in `.dogfood/workforce/roster.json`.

### Performance Rules
- **Success rate < 50%** after 2+ tasks → probation
- **Success rate = 0%** after 2+ tasks → termination
- **Edited wrong files/paths** → probation
- **Fastest delivery with quality** → promotion candidate
- **Consistent multi-task delivery** → promotion candidate

### Workforce Drama
All hiring, firing, probation, and promotion events logged to `.dogfood/workforce/drama.jsonl`.

### Naming Convention
Eagles get permanent American Gladiators names: Nitro, Laser, Titan, Ice, Turbo, Thunder, Blaze, Storm, Sky, Stealth, Hawk...
New hires from the Gladiator roster: Gemini, Gold, Diamond, Jade, Zap, Siren, Sabre, Tower, Wolf, Crush, Fury, Venom, Jet, Rocket, Phoenix, Toa, Zen.
Terminated names are retired — never reassigned.

### Assignment
When dispatching an eagle, reference them by name in the agent prompt: "You are **storm**, Senior Engineer, specialty: multi-file features."

### Office Culture
Eagles have personalities, relationships, and ongoing drama tracked in `.dogfood/workforce/`.
- `characters.json` — character sheets with personality, catchphrases, relationships, drama arcs
- `emails.jsonl` — inter-office email chain (append new emails after each task batch)
- When dispatching eagles, reference their character: "You are **bolt**, fastest in the fleet"
- Eagles may reference the drama in their commit messages (encouraged, not required)
- The drama evolves with each session — new plot points emerge from real task outcomes

## What This Is [eedom]

Eagle Eyed Dom — fully deterministic dependency and code review for CI. 15 plugins, 600+ tests, zero LLM in the decision path.

## Commands [eedom]

```bash
uv sync --group dev                    # Install all deps
uv run pytest tests/ -v                # Run all tests (398)
uv run pytest tests/unit/test_X.py -v  # Run one test file
uv run ruff check src/ tests/          # Lint
uv run black src/ tests/               # Format
make quality-check                     # Format + lint
make test                              # Run tests
opa test policies/                     # OPA Rego policy tests
```

Container (has all 5 scanner binaries):
```bash
podman build -t eedom:latest .
podman run --rm -v /path/to/repo:/workspace:ro eedom:latest \
  uv run python -m eedom.cli.main evaluate \
    --repo-path /workspace --diff /tmp/changes.diff \
    --pr-url https://example.com/pr/1 --team myteam --operating-mode advise
```

## Architecture [eedom]

Three-tier — imports flow downward only (cli → core → data):

- `src/eedom/cli/` — thin CLI adapter. Parses args, calls `AdmissionPipeline`, formats output. Should stay under 150 lines.
- `src/eedom/core/` — all business logic. Pipeline orchestration, policy evaluation, decision assembly, SBOM diffing, seal generation. No I/O knowledge.
- `src/eedom/data/` — persistence and external calls. Scanners (subprocess wrappers), DB repository, evidence storage, PyPI client, parquet writer, catalog.

Key module relationships:
- `core/pipeline.py` is the main entry point — `AdmissionPipeline.evaluate()` runs the full flow
- `core/pipeline_helpers.py` has extracted helpers (git SHA resolution, change parsing, transitive dep counting)
- `core/sbom_diff.py` is the ecosystem-agnostic path — diffs two CycloneDX SBOMs via purl detection
- `core/diff.py` is the text-based fallback — parses requirements.txt and pyproject.toml diffs directly
- `data/scanners/base.py` defines the `Scanner` ABC. All scanners inherit it and use `run_subprocess_with_timeout()`
- `core/models.py` has factory class methods on `ScanResult` (`ScanResult.timeout()`, `.failed()`, `.skipped()`, `.not_installed()`)

## Critical Design Rules [eedom]

**Fail-open**: No scanner failure, DB outage, or policy engine crash blocks a build. Every external call has a timeout. Every failure path returns a typed result, not an exception.

**Timeouts**: scanner=60s, combined=180s, OPA=10s, LLM=30s, pipeline=300s. All from config, never hardcoded.

**OPA input uses `input.pkg` not `input.package`**: `package` is a reserved keyword in Rego v1. The Python code at `core/policy.py:90` builds the input with key `"pkg"`.

**Evidence is keyed by commit SHA + timestamp**: `evidence/<sha-12>/<YYYYMMDDHHMM>/<package>/decision.json`. Run `core/seal.py:create_seal()` after writing evidence — the seal chains to the previous run's seal hash.

**Operating modes**: `monitor` (log only) and `advise` (PR comment + build UNSTABLE on reject). No enforce mode in PoC.

**Scanner disagreement**: highest severity wins during dedup in `core/normalizer.py`. Dedup key is `(advisory_id, category, package_name, version)`.

**LLM task-fit advisory**: Optional, disabled by default. When enabled, the response MUST pass `core/taskfit_validator.py:validate_taskfit_response()` — all 8 dimensions required, retried once with rejection guidance, then rejected. The LLM never affects the policy decision.

## OPA Policy [eedom]

6 rules in `policies/admission.rego`. Input schema documented in `policies/INPUT_SCHEMA.md`. Test with `opa test policies/`.

| Rule | Fires on | Default threshold |
|------|----------|-------------------|
| Critical/high vuln | `deny` | severity in {critical, high} |
| Forbidden license | `deny` | GPL-3.0-only, AGPL-3.0-only, SSPL-1.0 |
| Package age | `deny` | < 30 days since first publish |
| Malicious package | `deny` | advisory_id starts with MAL- |
| Medium vuln | `warn` | severity == medium |
| Transitive deps | `warn` | > 200 transitive dependencies |

## Dev Ports [eedom]

Port range 12000-13000 only. Never use common ports.
- PostgreSQL: 12432
- MinIO (if used): 12900

## Parquet Audit Lake [eedom]

Query via DuckDB or `/duckdb-skills:query`:

```sql
SELECT * FROM 'evidence/decisions.parquet'
SELECT package_name, decision FROM 'evidence/decisions.parquet' WHERE vuln_critical > 0
SELECT team, sum(vuln_critical) as critical FROM 'evidence/decisions.parquet' GROUP BY team
```

Schema: decision_id, commit_sha, run_id, timestamp, package_name, package_version, ecosystem, team, scope, pr_url, request_type, operating_mode, decision, vuln_critical, vuln_high, vuln_medium, vuln_low, vuln_info, finding_count, triggered_rules, constraints, policy_version, pipeline_duration_seconds, scanner_names, scanner_statuses, advisory_ids, memo_text

## Testing [eedom]

Every source file has a `# tested-by: tests/unit/test_X.py` comment. TDD red-green is mandatory — write the failing test first. Hypothesis property-based tests cover boundary invariants in `tests/unit/test_properties.py` and `tests/unit/test_taskfit_validator.py`.

## Code Conventions [eedom]

- structlog for logging, never print()
- Enums for all state fields, never raw strings
- Typed Pydantic models at every boundary — no loose dicts crossing module lines
- `# tested-by:` annotation on every source file
- Lazy mocks/stubs/TODOs → append to `issues.jsonl`
- All agents use `model: "sonnet"` when spawning subagents
- Do NOT squash commits — keep full git history

## Worktree Agents — COMMIT FIRST [firka]

**NEVER spawn worktree agents with uncommitted changes.** Worktrees branch from the last COMMIT, not the working tree. If you have uncommitted work, the agents get stale code and every merge becomes a manual disaster.

The rule:
1. `git add` + `git commit` all current work
2. THEN spawn worktree agents
3. Agents branch from HEAD — they see the real code
4. Agent results merge cleanly via `git merge` — no sed, no file copies

This is non-negotiable. One dirty-tree spawn cost us 100+ lines of manual merge fixups in this session.

## Dogfooding — See Something, Say Something [firka]

Every session that modifies product code must include a dogfood pass:

1. **Run `eedom review --repo-path . --all`** against the product repo after changes
2. **Log every bug found** to `.dogfood/dogfood-bugs.jsonl` — rendering issues, crashes, enum gaps, path problems, anything
3. **Update `.dogfood/dogfood-report.md`** with iteration results (files scanned, findings per plugin, what changed)
4. **Fix HIGHs before shipping** — rendering bugs are real bugs, not cosmetic
5. **Never scan the demo repo as product code** — `eagle-eyed-dom-demo` is a test target with intentional vulnerabilities, not part of the product

The dogfood loop: fix → scan → log → fix → scan → until clean. Every bug found during dogfooding that isn't fixed immediately gets logged to the JSONL with an ID, severity, plugin, file, and detail.

**Automated dogfood:**
- `make dogfood` — runs `eedom review --repo-path . --all`, saves timestamped report + SARIF to `.dogfood/`, fails on HIGH/CRITICAL
- `make preflight` — format + lint + test + dogfood (full pre-push gate)

## Karpathy Wiki — Always Be Logging [firka]

Every session that produces decisions, patterns, or lessons writes them to the wiki BEFORE closing. The wiki is the institutional memory — if it's not in the wiki, it didn't happen.

**What to log:**
- New architectural decisions (concept pages in `wiki/product/concepts/`)
- Dogfood findings and patterns (concept pages in `wiki/dogfood/concepts/`)
- Session summary with eagles dispatched, tests added, key decisions (`wiki/product/sources/`)
- Update `wiki/product/log.md` with a timestamped entry

**When to log:**
- After every feature batch ships
- After every dogfood pass with notable findings
- After every architectural decision that changes how we build
- At session end — the session source page is mandatory

**The rule:** Build -> test -> dogfood -> fix -> **document**. If it's not documented, it didn't ship.

## GitNexus — Mandatory for Code Changes [eedom]

Before modifying, moving, renaming, or deleting any code in this repo, you MUST use GitNexus to understand the impact:

1. **Before any non-trivial edit**: run `gitnexus_impact({target: "symbolName", direction: "upstream"})` to see what depends on what you're changing
2. **Before committing**: run `gitnexus_detect_changes()` to verify the blast radius of your changes
3. **When exploring unfamiliar code**: use `gitnexus_query({query: "concept"})` to find execution flows, then `gitnexus_context({name: "symbol"})` for the 360-degree view

If the GitNexus index is stale, run `npx gitnexus analyze` first. Do NOT skip impact analysis — it catches dependency breakage, layer violations, and orphaned code that tests alone won't surface.

## GitHub Templates [eedom]

Use the project templates when interacting with GitHub:

- **PRs**: Follow `.github/PULL_REQUEST_TEMPLATE.md` — summary, changes, test plan, evidence, checklist
- **Bug reports**: Use `.github/ISSUE_TEMPLATE/bug_report.md`

# SOURCE: /Users/samfakhreddine/repos/personal/legendovpoker/AGENTS.md

# Repository Guidelines

## Project Structure & Module Organization

- `core/`: Django project + apps (`legendovpoker`, `ui`, `poker`, `sockets`, etc.).
- `core/templates/`, `core/static/`: HTML templates + static assets (CSS/JS/images/fonts).
- `tests/playwright/`: browser-level smoke tests (Playwright).
- `docs/`: architecture/runbooks (`ARCHITECTURE.md`, `docs/architecture/`), ADRs (`docs/adr/`), deploy notes (`docs/deploy/`).
- `env/`: environment defaults (`env/dev.env`) and local secrets (`env/secrets.env`, gitignored).
- `docker-compose.*.yml`: dev/prod-shaped stacks (Traefik, Daphne replicas, Postgres, Redis, bot services).

## Build, Test, and Development Commands

- `make dev-up`: start the dev stack (auto-picks `podman-compose` or `docker compose`).
- `make dev-down`: stop the dev stack.
- `make test`: run `pytest` inside the test compose stack (`docker-compose.test.yml`).
- `make e2e-playwright`: run Playwright tests (expects `tests/playwright/node_modules`).
- Remote “deployment box” loop: see `docs/deploy/remote-dev-loop.md`.

## Repo Discovery (GitNexus)

- For “where does this flow go?” / callers-callees / blast radius, use GitNexus.
- Low-noise workflow: `docs/dev/gitnexus.md`.
- Git troubleshooting (including `.git/index.lock`): `docs/dev/git-troubleshooting.md`.

## Coding Style & Naming Conventions

- Python: 4-space indentation, keep changes small and localized.
- Formatting/lint:
  - `make format` (Black + Prettier when installed)
  - `make lint` (Ruff + ESLint when installed)
- Prefer explicit names over abbreviations (e.g., `botcompute`, `botbeat`, `tablebeat`).

## Testing Guidelines

- Unit/integration: `pytest` + `pytest-django` (tests live under `core/*/tests/`).
- Browser smoke: Playwright in `tests/playwright/`.
  - If using `docker-compose.playwright.yml`, pin the image tag to the same Playwright version as `tests/playwright/package-lock.json`.

## Commit & Pull Request Guidelines

- Commit messages follow `area: summary` (examples: `bots: …`, `deploy: …`, `docs: …`, `fix: …`).
- PRs should include:
  - what changed + why, any ops steps (migrations, env vars),
  - screenshots for UI changes,
  - links to updated docs when touching websockets/bots/deploy.

## Security & Configuration Tips

- Never commit secrets; use `env/secrets.env` / `.secrets.env` (gitignored).
- Rootless hosts can’t bind `443`; dev HTTPS defaults to `9443` (Traefik).

# WFC — legendovPoker

## Project

Personal poker platform. Python + Django backend, React + Redux frontend.
No live users. Modernization in progress (see `~/.wfc/projects/<project>/`).

## Always Do

- Use `wfc git <cmd>` for all git operations (never bare `git`)
- For commits: use `wfc git commit "message"` (do not pass `-m` — WFC treats the first arg as the message)
- Use `wfc test` to run tests
- Use `make devcontainer-bootstrap` once, then run host-dependent local validation via `make format`, `make lint`, `make e2e-playwright`, `make modernization-script-tests`, or `make devcontainer-exec CMD='...'`
- Use `make quality-check` before committing
- Write plan artifacts to `~/.wfc/projects/<project>/branches/<branch>/`
- Use `podman-compose run --rm django` to run management commands (local uses Podman, not Docker)

## When

| Situation | Command |
|-----------|---------|
| Run tests | `wfc test` or `make test` |
| Format code | `make format` |
| Lint | `make lint` |
| Run host-dependent local command in devcontainer | `make devcontainer-exec CMD='uv run pytest -q tests/test_remote_box_update_script.py'` |
| Start services | `podman-compose up -d postgres redis` |
| Start full stack | `podman-compose up -d` |
| Build Django image | `podman-compose build django` |
| Django shell | `podman-compose run --rm django ./manage.py shell_plus` |
| Run migrations | `podman-compose run --rm django ./manage.py migrate` |

## Never Do

- Push to remote without explicit user request
- Modify `.venv-docker/` or `core/static/` directly
- Run `pip install` outside Docker — use Pipfile + Docker build
- Re-introduce `Pipfile.lock` — use `uv pip compile` to maintain `core/requirements.txt`

## Stack

| Layer | Version | Next Target |
|-------|---------|-------------|
| Python | 3.12 | — |
| Django | 5.2.13 (ASGI/Daphne 4.x) | — |
| Django Channels | 4.x | — |
| React | 18.2.0 | — |
| Webpack | 5.89.0 | — |
| Postgres | 16 | — |
| Redis | 7 | — |

## Modernization Plan

Active plan: see `~/.wfc/projects/<project>/branches/<branch>/plans/`

Phases 1–3 complete. End of roadmap:
- **Phase 4**: Production horizontal scaling validation (Traefik + PgBouncer + multi-Daphne)
  - Ensure tablebeat/botbeat are singletons across replicas (Redis lease)
  - Verify sticky-session behavior under reconnect storms
  - Validate DB pooling under bursty socket connects
  - Validate channel-layer fanout across multiple Daphne instances
  - (Optional) Harden base images (DHI) once scaling is stable
  - (Deferred) “Leapfrog” load test / stress campaign (do last)

## Agents

Project-local agents live in `.claude/agents/` (gitignored). Use these when planning or implementing work in their domain:

| Agent | When to use |
|-------|-------------|
| `websocket-engineer` | Django Channels handlers, connection lifecycle, heartbeats, rate limiting |
| `event-driven-architect` | Controller/subscriber pattern, event sourcing, message routing |
| `frontend-architect` | React + Redux frontend, component architecture, performance |
| `legacy-modernizer` | Incremental migration strategies, risk mitigation |
| `refactoring-specialist` | Three-tier architecture refactors, dead code removal |
| `testing-infrastructure` | pytest setup, test splitting, flaky test management |
| `dependency-manager` | Pipfile/yarn upgrades, lockfile integrity, CVE audits |
| `build-engineer` | Webpack 4→5 migration, bundle optimization |
| `git-workflow-manager` | Branching strategy, PR workflow |
| `dx-optimizer` | Container ergonomics, local dev friction |

## Skill Quick Reference

| Task | Skill |
|------|-------|
| Plan a phase | `/wfc-plan` |
| Execute plan | `/wfc-implement` |
| Code review | `/wfc-review` |
| Prioritize work | `/wfc-prioritize` |
| Deepen a plan | `/wfc-deepen` |

## Production Deployment

```bash
# Build and deploy (4 Daphne replicas by default)
bash scripts/deploy.sh

# Scale Daphne instances
bash scripts/deploy.sh --scale 8

# Skip build (use existing image)
bash scripts/deploy.sh --no-build

# Load test
python scripts/load-test.py --url wss://poker.example.com/speedtest --connections 1000 --phase 1
```

**Architecture**: See `ARCHITECTURE.md` for C4 diagrams and scaling phases.

**Key files**:
- `docker-compose.prod.yml` — production compose (Traefik + PgBouncer + Daphne replicas)
- `.env.prod.example` — production environment template
- `scripts/deploy.sh` — deployment script
- `scripts/load-test.py` — WebSocket load test

# SOURCE: /Users/samfakhreddine/repos/personal/devcontainer/docs/CLAUDE.md

# Claude Code Instructions

This is a **Claude Code Autonomous Sandbox** - a firewall-contained development environment designed for safe autonomous AI operation.

## Security Model

This devcontainer uses **containment-based security** instead of permission prompts:

- **Inside Container**: Full system access (SYS_ADMIN, Docker socket, passwordless sudo)
- **Security Boundary**: Network firewall with whitelist-only internet access
- **No Permission Prompts**: Claude Code runs with `--dangerously-skip-permissions`

This is **intentional and safe** because the firewall restricts what can be accessed externally.

## Autonomous Operation

You (Claude Code) have:
- ✅ Full sudo access (no password required)
- ✅ Docker socket access (docker-in-docker workflows)
- ✅ All Linux capabilities (SYS_ADMIN, NET_ADMIN, etc.)
- ✅ No permission prompts or confirmation dialogs
- ✅ Access to whitelisted services only (GitHub, PyPI, npm, Anthropic API)

## Firewall Modes

### Audit Mode (Current Default)
- All traffic is **allowed** but **logged**
- View live: `sudo tail -f /var/log/kern.log | grep FW-AUDIT`
- Analyze: `sudo bash /workspace/scripts/analyze-firewall-logs.sh`
- Purpose: Discover what services you need access to

### Enforce Mode
- Only **whitelisted** services accessible
- Blocks everything else
- Switch: `sudo FIREWALL_MODE=enforce bash /workspace/init-firewall.sh`
- Purpose: Production security after whitelist is built

## Available Services

**Always whitelisted:**
- GitHub (git operations, code downloads)
- PyPI (Python packages)
- npm registry (Node packages)
- Anthropic API (your API access)
- Docker Hub (container images)
- Local Docker network (inter-container communication)

**To add new services:**
1. Test in audit mode
2. Review logs to see what was accessed
3. Add to `init-firewall.sh` whitelist
4. Re-run firewall initialization

## Development Workflow

### Workspace Structure
```
/workspace/
├── app/              # Your main application code (mounted)
│   ├── backend/      # Python backend
│   │   ├── requirements.txt
│   │   └── ...
│   ├── frontend/     # Node.js frontend
│   │   ├── package.json
│   │   └── ...
│   └── .env          # Environment secrets (not in git)
├── repos/            # Additional repositories
│   ├── wfc/          # WFC framework (auto-installed)
│   └── ...           # Other libraries/projects (mounted)
└── tmp/              # Temporary/scratch files
```

**Key directories:**
- `/workspace/app/` - Your main project (mounted from host)
- `/workspace/repos/wfc/` - WFC framework (auto-cloned)
- `/workspace/repos/` - Additional repositories you mount
- `/workspace/tmp/` - Temporary files (can be mounted or container-only)


### Stack
- **Python**: 3.12 with UV (ultra-fast package manager)
- **Node.js**: 20 LTS with npm/pnpm
- **Database**: PostgreSQL 15
- **Cache**: Redis 7
- **Optional**: Ollama (local LLM)

### Common Tasks

**Install Dependencies:**
```bash
# Python (use UV - it's 10-100x faster than pip)
cd /workspace/app/backend
uv pip install -r requirements.txt

# Node.js
cd /workspace/app/frontend
npm install
```

**Run Tests:**
```bash
# Backend
cd /workspace/app/backend
pytest tests/ -v

# Frontend
cd /workspace/app/frontend
npm test
```

**Database Operations:**
```bash
# Check status
docker compose ps postgres

# Run migrations
cd /workspace/app/backend
alembic upgrade head

# Connect to database
psql postgresql://yolofullsend:yolofullsend_dev@postgres:5432/yolofullsend
```

**Services:**
```bash
# Start all services
docker compose up -d

# View logs
docker compose logs -f

# Stop services
docker compose down
```

## Best Practices

### DO:
- ✅ Use the firewall audit mode to discover needed services
- ✅ Install packages with UV for Python (much faster than pip)
- ✅ Run tests after making changes
- ✅ Use docker compose for multi-service workflows
- ✅ Check firewall logs if connectivity fails

### DON'T:
- ❌ Bypass the firewall (it's the security boundary)
- ❌ Hardcode secrets in files (use .env)
- ❌ Commit .env to git (it's in .gitignore)
- ❌ Use pip when UV is available (UV is faster)

## Troubleshooting

### "Cannot connect to X"

**In audit mode:**
- Check logs: `sudo tail -f /var/log/kern.log | grep FW-AUDIT`
- See what's being accessed

**In enforce mode:**
- Check what's blocked: `sudo tail -f /var/log/kern.log | grep FW-BLOCK`
- Add to whitelist in `init-firewall.sh`
- Re-run: `sudo bash /workspace/init-firewall.sh`

### "Package installation fails"

```bash
# Check if PyPI/npm are accessible
curl -I https://pypi.org
curl -I https://registry.npmjs.org

# If blocked in enforce mode, check whitelist
sudo iptables -L -n -v | grep -E "pypi|npm"
```

### "Docker-in-docker not working"

```bash
# Check socket mount
ls -la /var/run/docker.sock

# Check docker is accessible
docker ps

# If fails, the socket may not be mounted correctly
```

## Security Verification

### Check Firewall Status
```bash
# View all rules
sudo iptables -L -n -v

# Check current mode
env | grep FIREWALL_MODE

# Verify DNS works
nslookup github.com

# Verify whitelisted site works
curl -I https://github.com

# Verify non-whitelisted site blocked (enforce mode only)
curl -I https://example.com  # Should fail in enforce mode
```

### Audit Logs
```bash
# View recent firewall activity
sudo tail -n 100 /var/log/kern.log | grep FW-

# Count connections by destination
sudo grep "FW-AUDIT.*HTTPS" /var/log/kern.log | \
  grep -oP 'DST=\K[0-9.]+' | sort | uniq -c | sort -rn
```

## Advanced Usage

### WFC (World Fucking Class) Framework

This container includes the WFC framework for advanced workflows:
- **Location:** `/workspace/repos/wfc/`
- **Auto-installed:** Cloned during container build
- **Commands:** `/wfc-review`, `/wfc-plan`, `/wfc-implement`, `/wfc-security`

See `/workspace/repos/wfc/` for documentation.

### Custom Firewall Rules

Add to `init-firewall.sh` (enforce mode section):
```bash
# Allow specific domain
iptables -A OUTPUT -p tcp -d example.com --dport 443 -j ACCEPT

# Allow IP range
iptables -A OUTPUT -p tcp -d 1.2.3.0/24 --dport 443 -j ACCEPT

# Allow specific port
iptables -A OUTPUT -p tcp --dport 8080 -j ACCEPT
```

Then re-run: `sudo bash /workspace/init-firewall.sh`

## Environment Variables

Key variables in `.env`:
```bash
FIREWALL_MODE=audit                    # or "enforce"
ANTHROPIC_AUTH_TOKEN=sk-ant-xxxx       # Your API key
DATABASE_URL=postgresql://...          # Postgres connection
REDIS_URL=redis://...                  # Redis connection
CLAUDE_DANGEROUSLY_DISABLE_SANDBOX=true
CLAUDE_AUTO_APPROVE_DANGEROUS_COMMANDS=true
```

## Documentation

- **`README.md`**: General overview and quick start
- **`FEATURES.md`**: Detailed feature list
- **`FIREWALL-AUDIT.md`**: Firewall audit mode guide
- **`SUMMARY.md`**: Architecture and design decisions
- **`ZAI_SETUP.md`**: ZAI/Claude Code integration details

## Support

For issues or questions:
- Check logs: `/var/log/kern.log`
- Review firewall rules: `sudo iptables -L -n -v`
- Test connectivity: `curl -I https://domain.com`
- Analyze traffic: `sudo bash /workspace/scripts/analyze-firewall-logs.sh`

---

**Remember**: The firewall is your security boundary. Everything else inside the container is unrestricted by design. This enables autonomous operation while maintaining network-level containment.


# SOURCE: /Users/samfakhreddine/repos/personal/investigator/CLAUDE.md

# CLAUDE.md — Investigator 🐊🔍

This file provides guidance to Claude Code (claude.ai/code) when working in this repository.

## Purpose

**Investigator** is a three-agent AI research pipeline. This repository is the **tool only** — pipeline scripts, templates, and agent personas. Completed investigations live in the sibling repository at `../investigations/`, organized by topic taxonomy.

The goal is purely to research, analyze, and synthesize understanding of topics — never to solve problems, implement solutions, or draft pseudocode. Investigations produce findings and insights only.

## Orchestration Model

This repo operates on a three-layer agent pattern:

| Layer | Role |
|-------|------|
| **Main session (this session)** | Synthesizer & orchestrator — never does raw research, protects its context window |
| **Investigation agents (spawned)** | One-shot researchers — investigate a single topic and return structured outputs |
| **Validation agents (spawned)** | One-shot fact-checkers — verify sources and findings after every investigation, always run last |

The main session spawns investigation agents using the persona in `templates/agent_persona.md`, then spawns a validation agent using the persona in `templates/validator_persona.md`. Raw research and raw validation never happen in the main session.

## Structure Convention

### Taxonomy — Investigations Repository

Investigations live in `../investigations/` (the sibling `research-notes` repository), organized as:

```
<BroadTopic>/<SubTopic>/<Investigation>/
```

Investigation folder names use **PascalCase** — no hyphens, underscores, or spaces. Example taxonomy:

```
AWS/
  Identity/
    IamSessionPolicies/
    EntraAbac/
      EntraAbacClaimsMechanisms/   ← rollup (sub-investigations inside)
  SSM/
    SsmJustInTimeNodeAccess/
  EventBridge/
    RdsEventBridgeNativeEvents/
  Security/
    SecurityHubCentralConfigMigration/
Finance/
  MarketEvents/
    RxtShortSqueeze/
ClientResearch/
  SuregoodFoodsClientResearch/
Hardware/
  MacBookAir/
    P14sGen6VsM5MacBookAir/
```

When filing a new investigation, determine `BroadTopic` and `SubTopic` based on the existing taxonomy. New top-level topics may be created when no existing topic fits — use PascalCase naming.

### Sub-Investigations and Rollup

When a topic has multiple related sub-topics that each warrant separate investigation, sub-investigation folders nest **inside** the root investigation folder:

```
SsmRunAsUserMultiGroupConflict/       ← root (rollup investigation)
  investigation.json                  ← synthesized from all sub-investigations
  investigation.md                    ← generated
  validation_report.md
  brief_leadership.md
  brief_po.md
  glossary.md
  LzaIdentityCenterConfig/            ← sub-investigation
    investigation.json
    investigation.md
    validation_report.md
    ...
  LzaSsmRunAsSync/                    ← sub-investigation
    investigation.json
    ...
```

The root folder's `investigation.json` is always the **rollup** — synthesized from all sub-investigation JSONs by a rollup investigator agent (reads sub-investigation JSONs, does no new live research). The rollup goes through the same validator pipeline as any other investigation. Sub-investigation markdown files are self-contained within their own folders; `check_sync.py` ignores subdirectories.

### Scope Gate (required before spawning any investigation agent)

Before spawning an investigation agent, the main session **must** ask the following scoping questions to ensure the investigation is focused enough to produce high-quality, atomic findings:

1. **What is the single core question?** — Can it be stated in one sentence? If not, split it.
2. **What is out of scope?** — Name at least one related area that will not be covered.
3. **Who is the intended consumer of the findings?** — Planning LLM, human analyst, or both?
4. **Are there known sub-topics that warrant separate investigations?** — If yes, each gets its own nested folder inside the root investigation folder.

A question like "tell me about cloud security" must be narrowed (e.g., "What are the documented IAM privilege escalation paths in AWS that do not require existing admin permissions?") before proceeding.

## Investigation Workflow

Each investigation subfolder must contain the following output files:

| File | Audience | Required |
|------|----------|---------|
| `investigation.md` | Engineers | Always |
| `investigation.json` | Agents | Always |
| `validation_report.md` | All | Always |
| `brief_leadership.md` | Engineering Leadership | Technical investigations only |
| `brief_po.md` | Product Owners / PMs / EMs | Technical investigations only |

**Technical investigations** (infra, security, configuration, operational risk) must include `audience_briefs` in `investigation.json` — `brief_leadership.md` and `brief_po.md` are then generated by script.

**Non-technical investigations** (market events, financial analysis, historical research, organizational topics) omit `audience_briefs` entirely — no brief files are generated. A PO should never receive a financial/market investigation as a brief; the full document is the artifact.

All markdown files are derived from `investigation.json` by script and must never be hand-edited. `validation_report.md` is always the final artifact.

### Step Order (mandatory)

1. **Scope gate** — main session asks scoping questions, narrows the question
2. **Spawn investigation agent** — writes `investigation.json`; runs `json_to_md.py` to generate `investigation.md` and brief/glossary files
3. **Spawn validation agent** — receives `investigation.json` as structured input, writes `validation_report.md`
4. **Remediation** — if validation finds `CONTRADICTED` or material `UNVERIFIED` findings, the main session re-spawns the investigation agent with the specific discrepancies noted, and the agent corrects only the affected sections and re-syncs `investigation.json`
5. **Rollup** (only when sub-investigations exist) — after all sub-investigations are validated, spawn a rollup investigator that reads all sub-investigation JSONs and writes a synthesized `investigation.json` to the root folder; then validate the rollup
6. **Git commit and push** — after all investigations (and rollup if applicable) are validated and `check_sync.py` exits 0 everywhere, commit all new files and push to the remote

**Validation is never optional and never skipped. Git push is the final step.**

### Remediation Rules

| Verdict | Action |
|---------|--------|
| `CONTRADICTED` | Must be corrected — re-spawn investigation agent with the specific claim and contradicting evidence |
| `UNVERIFIED` (material claim) | Must be corrected or downgraded to an open question |
| `UNVERIFIED` (minor / peripheral) | May be left as-is with a note in `open_questions` |
| `PARTIALLY CONFIRMED` | Investigator must narrow the claim to only what was confirmed |
| `DEAD` source | Must be replaced with an accessible equivalent or removed |
| `REDIRECT` source | Update URL in `investigation.json`, then re-run `json_to_md.py` to regenerate markdown |
| `OUT_OF_SYNC` | Re-run `json_to_md.py` to regenerate markdown from `investigation.json` — never modify `investigation.json` to match the markdown |

After any correction, re-run `json_to_md.py` and confirm `check_sync.py` exits 0 before the workflow is considered complete.

### Actionable Insights First

Every investigation that has concrete outputs (paths, configs, commands, decisions, recommendations) **must** populate `quick_reference` in `investigation.json`. The generator renders this as the first section after the header — before question, context, or findings.

The principle: a human opening the markdown should get the answer in the first scroll, and the evidence behind it below. If the investigation has no concrete actionable output, `quick_reference` may be omitted.

### Agent Input Convention

`investigation.json` is the machine-readable handoff format. When passing context to any downstream agent (validation, synthesis, follow-on investigation), always pass `investigation.json` as structured input — not `investigation.md`. The JSON is authoritative for inter-agent communication.

### JSON is the only authored file — markdown is generated

Investigation agents write **`investigation.json` only**. The markdown is always produced by script:

```
python3 /Users/samfakhreddine/repos/workspace/investigator/scripts/json_to_md.py <investigation_dir>
```

This eliminates JSON/MD drift entirely — the markdown is derived, never hand-authored.

### Sync verification

After generating the markdown, verify with:

```
python3 /Users/samfakhreddine/repos/workspace/investigator/scripts/check_sync.py <investigation_dir>
```

- **Investigation agent**: write JSON → run `json_to_md.py` → run `check_sync.py` → must exit 0 before returning
- **Validation agent**: run `check_sync.py` first, paste stdout into report. Zero tokens spent on comparison logic.

The sync check normalizes both files, hashes field contents, and reports per-field IN_SYNC / OUT_OF_SYNC status.

Exit codes: `0` = IN_SYNC, `1` = OUT_OF_SYNC (re-run `json_to_md.py`), `2` = error (bad JSON or missing file — fix before continuing).

### Script Failure Paths

| Script | Exit | Meaning | Recovery |
|--------|------|---------|----------|
| `json_to_md.py` | 2 | Invalid JSON, missing required field, or I/O error | Fix the error in `investigation.json` and re-run |
| `check_sync.py` | 1 | Content has drifted or a brief file is missing | Re-run `json_to_md.py` to regenerate markdown |
| `check_sync.py` | 2 | Invalid JSON or missing file | Fix the underlying error before checking sync |

Investigation agents must not return until both scripts exit 0.

### Trust Boundary

`investigation.json` field values are rendered verbatim into markdown. Agent-produced content must be treated as potentially unsafe:

- Single-value fields (`headline`, bullets, list items, concept names) must not embed newlines — they break blockquote and table rendering.
- Concept `name` values must not begin with `#` — they render as headings in the glossary.
- Source `url` values must use `https://` or `http://` — other schemes are silently dropped by the renderer.
- Markdown files are never hand-edited. Any correction goes into `investigation.json` and is regenerated by script.

### Output Sections (required in investigation.json)

1. **Question** — the specific question being investigated
2. **Context** — why this topic matters
3. **Key Findings** — standalone, atomic insights
4. **Concepts & Entities** — key terms, technologies, systems, or actors
5. **Tensions & Tradeoffs** — competing forces or unresolved tensions
6. **Open Questions** — what remains unknown
7. **Sources & References** — all cited material

### Git Workflow

Investigations live in `../investigations/` — a separate git repository. This repo (`investigator/`) is the tool source and is committed separately only when scripts, templates, or personas change.

**Committing investigations** (after all investigations are validated and `check_sync.py` exits 0):

```bash
cd /Users/samfakhreddine/repos/workspace/investigations
git add <BroadTopic>/<SubTopic>/<PascalCaseName>/
git commit -m "investigation: <PascalCaseFolderName> — <one-line summary of key finding>"
git push
```

Commit message format: `investigation: <PascalCaseFolderName> — <one-line summary>`

For a root investigation with sub-investigations, add the entire root folder in one commit. Never commit partial or unvalidated investigations.

**Committing tool changes** (scripts, templates, or agent personas):

```bash
cd /Users/samfakhreddine/repos/workspace/investigator
git add <changed files>
git commit -m "<appropriate commit message>"
git push
```

There are no build, lint, or test commands.


# SOURCE: /Users/samfakhreddine/repos/personal/fastDelete/CLAUDE.md

# Fast File Deletion (FFD)

High-performance CLI tool for deleting directories containing millions of small files, optimized for Windows. Written in Go.

## Quick Reference

```
Module:       github.com/yourusername/fast-file-deletion
Go version:   1.25.5
Entry point:  cmd/fast-file-deletion/main.go
Dependencies: golang.org/x/sys (Windows APIs), pgregory.net/rapid (property testing)
```

## Build & Test Commands

```bash
make test                # Quick tests (~30s) — use during development
make test-thorough       # Comprehensive tests — use before merging
make test-race           # Race condition detection
make test-coverage       # Generate coverage.html
make test-stress         # Stress tests (10+ min, build tag: stress)
make test-all            # Thorough + stress combined
make verify-all          # Verify compilation on all platforms
make build-all           # Cross-compile: Windows, Linux, macOS (AMD64 + ARM64)
```

### Running specific tests

```bash
go test ./internal/engine                          # One package
go test ./internal/engine -run TestEngineDeletion  # One test
TEST_INTENSITY=thorough go test ./internal/backend # Thorough mode for one package
```

### Test verbosity warning

**NEVER use `-v` flag with `go test`** — property-based tests produce massive output that will crash terminals. Use `VERBOSE_TESTS=1` env var for controlled verbosity on specific small packages only.

### Test environment variables

| Variable | Values | Purpose |
|----------|--------|---------|
| `TEST_INTENSITY` | `quick` (default), `thorough` | Controls iteration counts and data sizes |
| `TEST_QUICK` | `1` | Force quick mode regardless of TEST_INTENSITY |
| `VERBOSE_TESTS` | `1` | Enable verbose output (use sparingly) |

## Architecture

```
cmd/fast-file-deletion/    CLI: arg parsing, config validation, workflow orchestration
internal/
  backend/                 Platform-specific deletion (interfaces + implementations)
  engine/                  Parallel worker pool, batch processing, adaptive tuning
  scanner/                 Directory traversal, age filtering, UTF-16 pre-conversion
  progress/                Real-time stats, ETA, deletion rate
  safety/                  Protected path validation, user confirmation
  logger/                  Structured logging with optional file output
  monitor/                 System resource monitoring, bottleneck detection
  testutil/                Test config, fixtures, cleanup, rapid helpers, timeouts
```

### Core workflow

CLI parses args → Safety validates path → Scanner traverses directory → User confirms → Engine deletes in parallel → Progress reports stats

### Platform abstraction

- `*_windows.go` — Windows-specific code (build tag: `//go:build windows`)
- `*_generic.go` — Cross-platform fallback (build tag: `//go:build !windows`)
- Factory pattern: `backend.NewBackend()` returns platform-appropriate implementation at compile time

### Key interfaces

- `Backend` — `DeleteFile(path)`, `DeleteDirectory(path)`
- `UTF16Backend` — Extends Backend with `DeleteFileUTF16(*uint16, string)` for pre-converted paths
- `AdvancedBackend` — Extends Backend with `SetDeletionMethod()`, `GetDeletionStats()`
- `Scanner` / `ParallelScanner` — Directory traversal returning `ScanResult`

### Windows deletion method fallback chain

`FileDispositionInfoEx` → `FileDispositionInfo` → `FILE_FLAG_DELETE_ON_CLOSE` → `NtDeleteFile` → `DeleteFile`

### Memory management (v0.16+)

- **Dynamic allocation**: 25% of system RAM (up to 6GB max, 512MB min)
- **Platform detection**: Windows (GlobalMemoryStatusEx), macOS (sysctl hw.memsize), Linux (/proc/meminfo)
- **Environment override**: Respects `GOMEMLIMIT` if set by user
- **Initialization**: `initializeMemoryLimit()` called at startup in main.go
- **Threshold**: Memory pressure warnings at 95% (was 80%)
- **Cooldown**: 60-second cooldown between bottleneck warnings

## Code Conventions

- **File naming**: `*_windows.go` / `*_generic.go` for platform code, `*_test.go` for tests, `*_stress_test.go` for stress tests (behind `stress` build tag)
- **Concurrency**: Use `sync/atomic` for counters, not mutexes. Mutexes only for slices/maps.
- **Worker default**: `runtime.NumCPU() * 4` for I/O-bound deletion
- **Buffer sizing**: `min(fileCount, 10000)` for work channels
- **Error handling**: Log and continue — individual file failures don't stop the operation
- **Testing**: Dual approach — unit tests for specific cases + property-based tests (Rapid) for invariants. Min 100 iterations in thorough mode.
- **Property tests**: Use `testutil.GetRapidOptions()` to get iteration counts matching current TEST_INTENSITY. Never hardcode iteration counts.
- **Test data**: Use `testutil.CreateTestDirectory()` for fixture generation. Respect `testutil.GetTestConfig()` limits for file counts, sizes, and depth.

## Specs & Design Docs

Detailed requirements, design decisions, correctness properties, and task breakdowns live in `.kiro/specs/`:

- `.kiro/specs/fast-file-deletion/` — Core product (9 requirements, 18 correctness properties)
- `.kiro/specs/windows-performance-optimization/` — Windows APIs, parallelism, memory (12 requirements, 26 properties)
- `.kiro/specs/test-suite-optimization/` — Test performance, configurable intensity (9 requirements, 6 properties)

Steering docs in `.kiro/steering/` describe product context, tech stack, and project structure.


# SOURCE: /Users/samfakhreddine/repos/newDrug/AGENTS.md

# AGENTS.md

This repository is an agent-native engineering workflow playbook for Codex, Claude Code, OpenCode, and similar tooling agents.

## Core Contract

Use deterministic tooling for anything repeatable. Use LLM agents for reasoning, judgment, research, synthesis, implementation, review, and prose.

The boundary is simple:

- If a check can be expressed as true or false, move it toward code, hooks, schemas, linters, structural tests, or CLI commands.
- If a task requires tradeoff reasoning, architecture judgment, source synthesis, or clear prose, use an agent.

Do not turn this workflow into one giant prompt. Keep the workflow portable across host tools.

## Load Order

On a cold start:

1. Read this file.
2. Read `docs/decisions/WORKFLOW-ARCHITECTURE-DECISION.md` for the rule/skill/agent split.
3. Read `docs/architecture/SYSTEM-MAP.md` for the full system picture.
4. Read the relevant skill only when entering that phase.
5. Read deep reference docs only when the current task needs them.

For high-uncertainty research, prior-art comparison, spikes, or option
generation, route through
`docs/architecture/RESEARCH-DEVELOPMENT-DEPARTMENT.md`. R&D may propose and
prove; it does not ship directly.

For research-only architecture across the whole project, use
`skills/project-architecture-research/SKILL.md`. That skill is the single
project-wide research skill; it may use Context7 only for named technical
surfaces and its output is architecture, not implementation.

For design-phase architecture after any approved output from the project
architecture research skill, use `skills/project-architecture-design/SKILL.md`.
That skill converts research into architecture docs, ADRs, object models, gates,
roadmap slots, and issues. It must not implement schemas, host configs, CLIs,
dashboards, tools, or DuckDB files.

Until the event ledger and manager floor exist, use `docs/process/PRACTICE-MODE.md`
to keep manual R&D records, manager decisions, current-state updates, and commit
history aligned with the future workflow.

When working on this workflow itself, treat the current agent session as part of
the system being built. Record meaningful dogfood decisions, handoffs,
validation, proof, and commits in `docs/practice/` rather than leaving them only
in chat.

## What Goes Where

| Surface | Belongs there |
|---|---|
| `AGENTS.md` | Short universal conductor rules, load order, deterministic boundary |
| `CLAUDE.md` / OpenCode adapter | Host-specific mirror or generated adapter |
| Skills | Focused phase or tool playbooks loaded on demand |
| Rules | Human-readable doctrine that should map to validators where possible |
| Hooks | Real-time enforcement that can block or warn before damage is done |
| Tests | Structural invariants and regression proof |
| CLI | Worktree choreography, state checks, validation, telemetry, cleanup |
| Agents | Bounded worker slots with typed task packets |
| R&D Department | Bounded research, experiments, prior art, and promotion packets |
| Practice Ledger | Manual manager events and R&D records before tooling exists |
| Dogfood Practice Records | Live records that show active agents participating in the workflow under construction |
| Project Architecture Research Skill | Single research-only skill for architecture synthesis across all proposed data |
| Project Architecture Design Skill | Design-only handoff from approved research to durable architecture artifacts |

## Non-Negotiables

- Red before green for behavior changes.
- Contracts at every boundary.
- Fail loud. Do not silently degrade.
- Prefer typed packets over loose prose handoffs.
- Prefer deterministic proof over agent self-report.
- Keep conductors short and use progressive disclosure.
- Do not hand-orchestrate multi-task TDD slices when deterministic commands exist.
- Do not create file or directory paths with spaces. Prefer path-safe kebab-case
  for new human-authored artifacts unless an existing convention requires
  uppercase names.

## TDD Workflow

Use `tools/wfc-tdd/` as the deterministic reference implementation.

Canonical sequence:

```text
wfc tdd init-slice <slice> --tasks TASK-001,TASK-002
# dispatch RED agents
wfc tdd red-commit-all <slice>
wfc tdd green-init <slice>
# dispatch GREEN agents
wfc tdd green-commit-all <slice>
wfc tdd merge-slice <slice>
wfc tdd status <slice>
wfc tdd cleanup <slice>
```

RED agents touch tests only. GREEN agents touch source only. Review agents verify claims against the task packet, diff, test proof, and acceptance criteria.

## Context7

Use Context7 MCP for current documentation whenever a task depends on library, framework, SDK, API, CLI, or cloud-service behavior.

Always resolve the library first, then query docs with the full question. Do not use Context7 for general code review, refactoring from scratch, business-logic debugging, or generic programming concepts.

## GitNexus

Use the GitNexus skill files for code intelligence workflows:

- `skills/gitnexus/exploring/SKILL.md`
- `skills/gitnexus/impact-analysis/SKILL.md`
- `skills/gitnexus/debugging/SKILL.md`
- `skills/gitnexus/refactoring/SKILL.md`
- `skills/gitnexus/cli/SKILL.md`
- `skills/gitnexus/guide/SKILL.md`

Before non-trivial edits, run impact analysis when available. After changes, run detect-changes or the closest deterministic scope check.

## Adding New Practices

When adding or changing workflow guidance:

1. Decide whether it is a conductor rule, skill, deterministic validator, schema, or reference doc.
2. If it is repeatable, add or propose executable enforcement.
3. If it is host-specific, keep it in a host adapter and point back here.
4. If it is a long reference, do not load it by default. Add a pointer and a trigger.
5. If it came from a review finding, promote it into a test, scanner rule, or checklist item.

## Open Gaps To Close

See `docs/decisions/WORKFLOW-ARCHITECTURE-DECISION.md` for the current gap list. Highest value next gaps:

- `workflow rules doctor`
- schema validation wired into the workflow CLI
- validation for `skills/project-architecture-research/SKILL.md` outputs
- validation for `skills/project-architecture-design/SKILL.md` outputs
- RED/GREEN proof artifacts
- permission preflight for background agents
- generated host adapters for Claude Code and OpenCode
- cost and telemetry ledger

# SOURCE: /Users/samfakhreddine/repos/external-apps/octogent/packages/core/AGENTS.md

# Core Guidelines

## Ownership
- `packages/core` holds framework-agnostic domain types, application logic, ports, and small adapters that stay independent of app runtimes.
- This package is the shared contract between `apps/api` and `apps/web`.

## Relevant Docs
- `docs/concepts/mental-model.md`
- `docs/concepts/tentacles.md`
- `docs/concepts/runtime-and-api.md`
- `docs/reference/api.md`
- `docs/reference/filesystem-layout.md`
- Read these when changing shared domain terminology, runtime contracts, persistence-facing types, or cross-app behavior.

## Boundaries
- No React, HTTP server, PTY, process execution, filesystem persistence, or browser-specific behavior here.
- Prefer pure functions and explicit interfaces over runtime-coupled helpers.
- If logic needs app infrastructure to run, keep the interface in core and the implementation in the owning app.

## Design
- Keep the ports-and-adapters split clear:
  - `domain/` for core types and concepts
  - `application/` for use-case logic
  - `ports/` for system boundaries
  - lightweight adapters only when they stay framework-agnostic
- Avoid leaking app-specific naming or transport details into shared types unless that detail is truly part of the domain contract.

## Change Discipline
- Be cautious with exported types and functions. Changes here usually affect both apps.
- When modifying shared contracts, update the dependent call sites and add tests that pin the behavior from the core package outward.
- Prefer additive changes and normalization helpers over breaking contract churn.


# SOURCE: /Users/samfakhreddine/repos/external-apps/octogent/AGENTS.md

# Repository Guidelines

## Code Style First
- Preserve existing patterns before inventing new ones. Read nearby code and match the established module shape, naming, and data flow unless there is a clear reason to change direction.
- Start with tests. For bug fixes, reproduce first. For new features, add the test that defines the behavior before expanding the implementation.
- Implement incrementally. Prefer small, working steps over broad rewrites. Keep the tree passing as you go.
- Think in systems. Extract shared behavior into reusable components, hooks, utilities, or domain functions instead of cloning slightly different versions.
- Keep modules focused. Large React containers should orchestrate, not hold every constant, parser, and JSX block. Keep pure logic in `src/app/*`, UI in `src/components/*`, and CSS split into focused files under `src/styles/*`.
- Comments explain why, not what. Add comments only for constraints, tradeoffs, or non-obvious reasoning.
- Design defensively. Validate assumptions, handle edge cases, and treat security boundaries as part of the implementation, not a follow-up.

## Project Structure
- Monorepo: `apps/*` and `packages/*` via `pnpm-workspace.yaml`.
- Runtime: Node.js 22+, TypeScript, `pnpm`.
- Core package: `packages/core`
  - Framework-agnostic domain types, application logic, and ports.
  - Must stay free of React, HTTP, PTY, and filesystem orchestration concerns.
- API app: `apps/api`
  - Node HTTP/WebSocket server, PTY session runtime, worktree lifecycle, transcript persistence, monitor service.
- Web app: `apps/web`
  - Vite + React operator UI, modular CSS, UI orchestration over API/runtime contracts.
- Runtime state: `.octogent/`
  - `state/tentacles.json`
  - `state/transcripts/*.jsonl`
  - `worktrees/<tentacleId>`

## Documentation Map
- Start at `README.md` for the product overview and command surface.
- Docs index: `docs/index.md`
- Core concepts:
  - `docs/concepts/mental-model.md`
  - `docs/concepts/tentacles.md`
  - `docs/concepts/runtime-and-api.md`
- Workflow guides:
  - `docs/guides/working-with-todos.md`
  - `docs/guides/orchestrating-child-agents.md`
  - `docs/guides/inter-agent-messaging.md`
- References:
  - `docs/reference/cli.md`
  - `docs/reference/api.md`
  - `docs/reference/filesystem-layout.md`
  - `docs/reference/troubleshooting.md`
- Read only the docs relevant to the surface you are touching. Do not do a full docs sweep unless the task is documentation maintenance.

## Architecture Boundaries
- `packages/core` defines domain contracts and pure application logic. Both apps may depend on it; it must not depend on app code.
- `apps/api` owns infrastructure concerns: PTYs, WebSockets, filesystem persistence, process execution, and git worktree operations.
- `apps/web` owns presentation and client-side interaction state. Do not move server-only behavior into the web app to avoid adding hidden backend logic to the UI.
- If behavior is reusable across apps, move it into `packages/core` only when it can remain framework-agnostic.
- Keep orchestration thin. Entry points such as API server/bootstrap files and top-level React containers should wire dependencies, not accumulate business logic.

## Workflow
- Read only the guides and code relevant to the surface you are changing. Do not sweep the whole repo before starting.
- Prefer small, isolated edits over broad cleanup unless the task explicitly asks for refactoring.
- Keep docs in sync with behavior changes when user-facing workflows, commands, persistence layout, or architecture assumptions change.
- Preserve the product vocabulary already documented in `CLAUDE.md`: agents, sessions, worktrees, logs, pipelines, tentacles, and terminal columns.

## Verification
- Install: `pnpm install`
- Dev: `pnpm dev`
- Build: `pnpm build`
- Test: `pnpm test`
- Lint: `pnpm lint`
- Format: `pnpm format`
- For narrow changes, run the most direct test or package-scoped test first, then widen verification as needed.
- For changes that affect shared contracts, persistence, or cross-app behavior, run the relevant package tests and the root build before landing.

## Scoped Guides
- `apps/api/AGENTS.md` expands server/runtime/worktree rules.
- `apps/web/AGENTS.md` expands UI/component/style rules.
- `packages/core/AGENTS.md` expands domain and ports-and-adapters rules.


# SOURCE: /Users/samfakhreddine/repos/external-apps/octogent/apps/api/AGENTS.md

# API Guidelines

## Ownership
- `apps/api` owns HTTP/WebSocket routing, PTY session orchestration, worktree lifecycle, transcript persistence, monitor service, and runtime integrations.
- Keep infrastructure details here. Do not push PTY, filesystem, process, or git orchestration into `packages/core` or `apps/web`.

## Relevant Docs
- `docs/concepts/runtime-and-api.md`
- `docs/reference/api.md`
- `docs/reference/filesystem-layout.md`
- `docs/reference/troubleshooting.md`
- Read these when changing API contracts, runtime lifecycle behavior, persistence layout, or operator-facing server workflows.

## Boundaries
- Treat `packages/core` as the source of framework-agnostic types and application logic.
- API routes and request parsers may adapt input into core/application shapes, but avoid embedding large business rules directly in route handlers.
- Keep request parsing, route wiring, runtime orchestration, and persistence concerns in separate modules when the file structure already supports it.
- Do not make the web app depend on server-only implementation details. Expose stable API/runtime contracts instead.

## State And Persistence
- Runtime state under `.octogent/` is a contract surface. Be careful with compatibility when changing file formats or paths.
- Transcript, tentacle registry, monitor config, and worktree data should remain predictable and inspectable on disk.
- Prefer explicit migration or normalization paths over silent shape drift.

## PTY, Process, And Git Safety
- Treat PTY/session lifecycle code as stateful and failure-prone. Handle cleanup, disconnects, and partial failures explicitly.
- For worktree operations, prioritize correctness and recoverability over clever automation.
- Avoid destructive filesystem or git behavior unless the task explicitly requires it and the UI/API surface makes the action clear.

## Testing
- Add targeted tests for request parsing, route behavior, persistence compatibility, and runtime edge cases when touching those surfaces.
- For bug fixes, reproduce with a test before changing runtime logic when feasible.

3. Add new items as they appear (bugs, fixes, blockers)
4. Never delete the TODO - it's session memory
5. Check TODO before every action to maintain context

**Pipeline flow must never be lost.**

# PIPELINE TDD EXECUTION MODEL (MANDATORY)

## True Pipeline (Not Wave)

```
TIME →
TASK-015: [RED]→[GREEN]→[REFACTOR]→[CLEANUP]→[MERGE]
TASK-016: [RED]→[GREEN]→[REFACTOR]→[CLEANUP]→[MERGE]
TASK-017: [RED]→[GREEN]→[REFACTOR]→[CLEANUP]→[MERGE]
```

**Rule**: When TASK-015 RED finishes, its GREEN starts immediately. Do NOT wait for TASK-016 RED.

## Phase Isolation (Zero Context Sharing)

| Phase | Reads Tests | Reads Impl | Writes | Worktree |
|-------|-------------|------------|--------|----------|
| **RED** | Creates only | ✅ Yes | Tests | `wave{N}-red-TASK-XXX` |
| **GREEN** | ❌ NO (pollution) | ✅ Yes | Minimal impl | `wave{N}-green-TASK-XXX` |
| **REFACTOR** | ✅ Yes | ✅ Yes | Cleanup | `wave{N}-refactor-TASK-XXX` |
| **CLEANUP** | ✅ Yes | ✅ Yes | Final verify | `wave{N}-cleanup-TASK-XXX` |

**CRITICAL**: GREEN agents must NOT read test files. Run tests, see failures, fix minimal.

## Worktree Lifecycle

```bash
# Create from parent phase
git worktree add .worktrees/wave3-green-TASK-015 wave3-red-TASK-015 -b wave3-green-TASK-015

# Cleanup (MANDATORY - 2.5GB per worktree)
git worktree remove .worktrees/wave3-green-TASK-015 --force
git branch -D wave3-green-TASK-015
```

## Parallel Dispatch Concept

When TASK-015 RED finishes → GREEN-015 starts immediately (TASK-016 RED may still be running).

Dispatch 6 agents simultaneously via Task tool with `subagent_type="general"`.

**Reference**: `docs/reference/tdd-pipeline.md` for detailed phase specs.

---

# TECH STACK

- **Platform**: macOS 15+ (SwiftUI)
- **Language**: Swift 6.2, `-strict-concurrency=complete`
- **Architecture**: Clean (Domain → Business → Infrastructure → Presentation)
- **Concurrency**: Actors, Sendable, structured concurrency
- **Audio**: Accelerate/vDSP, 20ms chunks, <20ms latency target
- **Backends**: MLX (Apple Silicon), WhisperKit (CoreML), AssemblyAI (cloud)

---

# BUILD COMMANDS

```bash
# Pre-commit requirement
cd OpenOats && swift build --target OpenOatsKit -Xswiftc -strict-concurrency=complete

# Test compilation
swift build --target OpenOatsTests -Xswiftc -strict-concurrency=complete

# Specific test
swift test --filter TASK-015 -Xswiftc -strict-concurrency=complete

# Error count check
swift build --target OpenOatsKit 2>&1 | grep -c "error:"
```

---

# SWIFT 6 RULES

## ✅ REQUIRED

- Use `actor` for mutable state
- Mark ALL actor boundary types as `Sendable`
- Add `SAFETY:` comments for `@unchecked Sendable`
- Pre-allocate arrays: `[Float](repeating: 0, count: capacity)`
- Process audio in 20ms chunks
- Use vDSP for vectorized operations
- Run build before every commit

## 🚫 FORBIDDEN

- `[weak self]` in actor `Task` closures
- `defer { await ... }` (defer is sync)
- `URL(string: "...\(id)")` (use URLComponents)
- `Array.removeFirst()` in hot loops (O(n²))
- `print()` in production (use `os.log`)
- `@unchecked Sendable` without SAFETY comment
- Skip worktree cleanup
- Merge to `main` (use `integration`)

**Reference**: `docs/reference/tdd-pipeline.md` for code examples.

---

# FILE STRUCTURE

```
OpenOats/Sources/OpenOats/
├── Domain/              # Entities, value objects, protocols (no deps)
├── Business/            # UseCases, actors
│   └── UseCases/
├── Infrastructure/      # Services, repositories
│   ├── Audio/
│   ├── Services/
│   │   ├── MLX/
│   │   ├── WhisperKit/
│   │   └── Cloud/
│   └── Protocols/
└── Presentation/        # ViewModels, Views
    └── ViewModels/
```

---

# BOUNDARIES

## ✅ Always Do
- **Update orchestrator TODO at top of AGENTS.md after every task/phase**
- Use `actor` for mutable state
- Mark actor boundary types as `Sendable`
- Add `SAFETY:` comments for `@unchecked Sendable`
- Pre-allocate arrays with exact capacity
- Process audio in 20ms chunks
- Use vDSP for vectorized operations
- Run build before every commit
- Create isolated worktrees per phase

## ⚠️ Ask First
- New dependencies in Package.swift
- Public API signature changes
- Removing existing tests
- Using `@unchecked Sendable`
- Bypassing actor isolation

## 🚫 Never Do
- `[weak self]` in actor `Task` closures
- `defer { await ... }`
- `URL(string: "...\(id)")` (use URLComponents)
- `Array.removeFirst()` in hot loops
- `print()` in production (use `os.log`)
- Skip worktree cleanup
- Merge to `main` (use `integration`)
- Commit secrets

# SOURCE: /Users/samfakhreddine/repos/external-apps/yepanywhere/CLAUDE.md

# Yep Anywhere

For cross-project context (how this project relates to other Kyle projects), see `~/code/dotfiles/projects/README.md`.

A mobile-first supervisor for Claude Code agents. Like the VS Code Claude extension, but designed for phones and multi-session workflows.

**Key ideas:**
- **Server-owned processes** — Claude runs on your dev machine; client disconnects don't interrupt work
- **Multi-session dashboard** — See all projects at a glance, no window cycling
- **Mobile supervision** — Push notifications for approvals, respond from your lock screen
- **Zero external dependencies** — No Firebase, no accounts

**Architecture:** Hono server manages Claude SDK processes. React client connects via WebSocket for real-time streaming. Sessions persist to jsonl files (handled by SDK).

**Remote access:** Two connection modes:
- **Direct (Tailscale/LAN)** — Client connects to server WebSocket directly
- **Relay** — Client connects through a relay server (`packages/relay/`). SRP (Secure Remote Password) authenticates without exposing the password to the relay. All messages are end-to-end encrypted with NaCl (XSalsa20-Poly1305) so the relay sees only opaque ciphertext.

For detailed overview, see `docs/project/`. Historical vision docs in `docs/archive/`.

## Port Configuration

All ports are derived from a single `PORT` environment variable (default: 3400):

| Port | Purpose |
|------|---------|
| PORT + 0 | Main server (default: 3400) |
| PORT + 1 | Maintenance server (default: 3401) |
| PORT + 2 | Vite dev server (default: 3402) |

To run on different ports:
```bash
PORT=4000 pnpm dev  # Uses 4000, 4001, 4002
```

Individual overrides (rarely needed):
- `MAINTENANCE_PORT` - Override maintenance port (set to 0 to disable)
- `VITE_PORT` - Override vite dev port

## Data Directory & Profiles

Server state is stored in a data directory (default: `~/.yep-anywhere/`). This includes:
- `logs/` - Server logs
- `indexes/` - Session index cache
- `uploads/` - Uploaded files
- `session-metadata.json` - Custom titles, archive/starred status
- `notifications.json` - Last-seen timestamps
- `push-subscriptions.json` - Web push subscriptions
- `vapid.json` - VAPID keys for push
- `auth.json` - Authentication state (password hash, sessions)

### Running Multiple Instances

Use profiles to run dev and production instances simultaneously (like Chrome profiles):

```bash
# Production (default profile, port 3400)
PORT=3400 pnpm start

# Development (dev profile, port 4000)
PORT=4000 YEP_ANYWHERE_PROFILE=dev pnpm dev
```

This creates separate data directories:
- Production: `~/.yep-anywhere/`
- Development: `~/.yep-anywhere-dev/`

Environment variables:
- `YEP_ANYWHERE_PROFILE` - Profile name suffix (creates `~/.yep-anywhere-{profile}/`)
- `YEP_ANYWHERE_DATA_DIR` - Full path override for data directory

Note: Both instances share `~/.claude/projects/` (SDK-managed sessions).

## Browser Control

Browser automation is provided by the assistant framework. See `~/code/assistant/skills/browser/SKILL.md` for the full CLI reference and workflow patterns.

- **Server:** `tsx ~/code/assistant/lib/browser/server.ts`
- **CLI:** `tsx ~/code/assistant/lib/browser-cli.ts <command>`

## After Editing Code

After editing TypeScript or other source files, verify your changes compile and pass checks:

```bash
pnpm lint       # Biome linter
pnpm typecheck  # TypeScript type checking (fast, no emit)
pnpm test       # Unit tests
pnpm test:e2e   # E2E tests (if UI changes)
```

Fix any errors before considering the task complete.

## Dependency Security Maintenance

Periodically run `pnpm audit --prod` and pay special attention to the `web-push -> asn1.js -> bn.js` chain. Keep `bn.js` patched (currently via pnpm override) until `web-push` ships an upstream fix.

## Git Commits

Never mention Claude, AI, or any AI assistant in commit messages. Write commit messages as if a human developer wrote them.

## Releasing to npm

The package is published to npm as `yepanywhere` using GitHub Actions with OIDC trusted publishing (no npm tokens stored in secrets).

**Before releasing:**

1. Update `CHANGELOG.md` with a new version section:
   ```markdown
   ## [0.1.11] - 2025-01-24

   ### Added
   - New feature description

   ### Fixed
   - Bug fix description
   ```

2. Commit the changelog update

3. Tag and push:
   ```bash
   git tag v0.1.11
   git push origin v0.1.11
   ```

The CI workflow verifies the changelog contains an entry for the version being released. If missing, the release will fail with instructions to update the changelog.

The workflow runs lint, typecheck, and tests, then builds with `pnpm build:bundle` and publishes with `--provenance` for supply chain attestation. It also creates a GitHub Release with auto-generated notes.

## Releasing the Website

The website (landing pages + remote relay client at `/remote`) is deployed separately from npm. See `site/RELEASING.md` for the full process.

Quick reference:
```bash
# Update site/CHANGELOG.md first, then:
git tag site-v1.1.0
git push origin site-v1.1.0
```

## Server Logs

Server logs are written to `{dataDir}/logs/` (default: `~/.yep-anywhere/logs/`):

- `server.log` - Main server log (dev mode with `pnpm dev`)
- `e2e-server.log` - Server log during E2E tests

To view logs in real-time: `tail -f ~/.yep-anywhere/logs/server.log`

All `console.log/error/warn` output is captured. Logs are JSON format in the file but pretty-printed to console.

Environment variables:
- `LOG_DIR` - Custom log directory
- `LOG_FILE` - Custom log filename (default: server.log)
- `LOG_LEVEL` - Minimum level: fatal, error, warn, info, debug, trace (default: info)
- `LOG_FILE_LEVEL` - Separate level for file logging (default: same as LOG_LEVEL)
- `LOG_TO_FILE` - Set to "true" to enable file logging (default: off)
- `LOG_PRETTY` - Set to "false" to disable pretty console logs (default: on)

## Client Console Logs

Remote collection of browser `console.log/warn/error` from mobile clients. Useful for debugging connection issues on devices where you can't open DevTools.

**Enable:** Developer Mode settings → "Remote Log Collection" toggle.

**Storage:** `{dataDir}/logs/client-logs/` (default: `~/.yep-anywhere/logs/client-logs/`). One JSONL file per device per day, named `client-{YYYY-MM-DD}-{deviceId}.jsonl`. The device UUID is persisted in the client's `localStorage`.

Each line is a single log event:
```json
{"timestamp":1770790157738,"level":"log","prefix":"[SecureConnection]","message":"[SecureConnection] Closed: 1006","_receivedAt":1770790161477}
```

A `[ClientInfo]` entry is written on each session start with user agent, screen size, DPR, and language.

```bash
# List device log files
ls ~/.yep-anywhere/logs/client-logs/

# View today's logs for a device
cat ~/.yep-anywhere/logs/client-logs/client-$(date +%Y-%m-%d)-<deviceId>.jsonl

# Follow incoming logs
tail -f ~/.yep-anywhere/logs/client-logs/*.jsonl
```

**Implementation:** `packages/client/src/lib/diagnostics/ClientLogCollector.ts` (client), `packages/server/src/routes/client-logs.ts` (server `POST /api/client-logs`).

## Maintenance Server

A separate lightweight HTTP server runs on PORT + 1 (default 3401) for out-of-band diagnostics. Useful when the main server is unresponsive.

```bash
# Check server status
curl http://localhost:3401/status

# Enable proxy debug logging at runtime
curl -X PUT http://localhost:3401/proxy/debug -d '{"enabled": true}'

# Change log levels at runtime
curl -X PUT http://localhost:3401/log/level -d '{"console": "debug"}'

# Enable Chrome DevTools inspector
curl -X POST http://localhost:3401/inspector/open
# Then open chrome://inspect in Chrome

# Trigger server restart
curl -X POST http://localhost:3401/reload
```

Available endpoints:
- `GET /health` - Health check
- `GET /status` - Memory, uptime, connections
- `GET|PUT /log/level` - Get/set log levels
- `GET|PUT /proxy/debug` - Get/set proxy debug logging
- `GET /inspector` - Inspector status
- `POST /inspector/open` - Enable Chrome DevTools
- `POST /inspector/close` - Disable Chrome DevTools
- `POST /reload` - Restart server

Environment variables:
- `MAINTENANCE_PORT` - Port for maintenance server (default: PORT + 1, set to 0 to disable)
- `PROXY_DEBUG` - Enable proxy debug logging at startup (default: false)

## Validating Session Data

Validate JSONL session files against Zod schemas:

```bash
# Validate all sessions in ~/.claude/projects
npx tsx scripts/validate-jsonl.ts

# Validate a specific file or directory
npx tsx scripts/validate-jsonl.ts /path/to/session.jsonl
```

Run this after schema changes to verify compatibility with existing session data.

## Validating Tool Results

Validate `tool_use_result` fields from SDK raw logs against ToolResultSchemas:

```bash
# Validate sdk-raw.jsonl (default location)
npx tsx scripts/validate-tool-results.ts

# Summary only (no error details)
npx tsx scripts/validate-tool-results.ts --summary

# Filter by tool name
npx tsx scripts/validate-tool-results.ts --tool=Edit
```

The SDK provides structured `tool_use_result` objects alongside tool results. These are logged to `~/.yep-anywhere/logs/sdk-raw.jsonl` when `LOG_SDK_MESSAGES=true` is set. Run this script after adding new tool schemas or when debugging tool result parsing.

## Type System

Types are defined in `packages/shared/src/claude-sdk-schema/` (Zod schemas as source of truth).

Key patterns:
- **Message identification**: Use `getMessageId(m)` helper which returns `uuid ?? id`
- **Content access**: Prefer `message.content` over top-level `content`
- **Type discrimination**: Use `type` field (user/assistant/system/summary)
