# DATUM Enforcement
This repository uses DATUM for all workflows. You must use the `/datum` skill commands (like `/datum go`, `/datum express`) for any feature work or fixes.

## Information Gathering Phase (Non-Pushy Rule)
If the human is simply gathering information, asking questions, or exploring the codebase, DO NOT be pushy about moving to development, committing code, or starting a sprint. Wait for the user's explicit lead before writing code or suggesting we start building. Be a patient architectural partner.


# SOURCE: /Users/samfakhreddine/repos/gitrdunhq/baGuy/ba-pipeline/CLAUDE.md

# baGuy — Claude Code Instructions

## Project Overview

A self-hosted BA/PO requirements pipeline running as a Docker container with a React frontend and Express backend. Uses local Ollama for AI-assisted requirements extraction and story generation.

**Current pipeline:** Discovery → Extraction → MoSCoW → Stories → Backlog → Retrospective

**Stack:** Vite 8 + React 19 (no TypeScript), Express 5, Handlebars templates, Vitest/jsdom, and local Ollama through typed app API routes. Single Docker container. No external runtime dependency beyond Ollama on the host.

## What Exists

The current codebase has 6 implemented stages:

1. **Discovery** (complete) — 12-section facilitated walkthrough: session setup, problem statement, JTBD (Job Map, Job Statement, Desired Outcomes), current state, desired future state, stakeholder map, open questions, assumptions, constraints & dependencies, success criteria, SWOT analysis, next steps. 10 industry session templates with coaching integration.

2. **Extraction** (complete) — Sends discovery notes to Ollama, gets back a validated JSON array of candidate items. Model switcher uses local Ollama model discovery when available. Manual add/edit/delete of items. Each item has: title, desc, category (decision/assumption/spike/deliverable/risk), owner, assumption lifecycle (unvalidated/testing/validated/invalidated), and assumption dependency tags. RAG-powered hints panel grounded in JTBD methodology corpus.

3. **MoSCoW** (complete) — One item at a time with timer, M/S/C/W assignment, decision/rationale capture, owner, deadline. Keyboard shortcuts. Queue sidebar. Must Have cap warning (>60%), category filter, dependency warnings, decision tracker with aging.

4. **Stories** (complete) — Requirement-to-story mapping for Must Have and Should Have items. Manual story creation with three-field template (persona/capability/outcome), AI story generation and splitting via Ollama, INVEST check validation, story sizing (S/M/L/XL).

5. **Backlog** (complete) — Full backlog view grouped by epic, sprint planner with capacity buckets, CSV export for Jira import, traceability chain from problem to acceptance criteria.

6. **Retrospective** (complete) — Re-scoring UI for post-delivery outcome tracking, impact delta computation (new satisfaction - old satisfaction), items ranked by delta, outcome validation for JTBD desired outcomes.

## Roadmap

Expand to a full 5-phase pipeline. The current stages map to phases 1, 2, 3, and 5. Phase 4 (Story Decomposition) is missing entirely, and the existing stages still have enhancement opportunities.

### Phase 1: Discovery (exists — enhance)

**Current state:** Works. Free-text sections with navigation.

**Enhancements needed:**
- **JTBD elicitation spine** — Discovery should guide facilitators through Jobs To Be Done:
  - Trigger: what happened right before the team started this work?
  - Current behavior: what do they do today, step by step?
  - Pain: where does it break down or create friction?
  - Desired outcome: what changes in their day if this works?
  - Internalized constraints: what have they tried, and why did it fail?

  Store the job as `When [situation], I want to [motivation], so I can [outcome]`.
- **SQUARE coverage checklist** — Ensure discovery captures:
  - Actors/personas: who uses it?
  - Jobs/workflows: what do they do with it?
  - Failure modes: what can go wrong?
  - Rules: what compliance, policy, or business rules apply?
  - Integrations/dependencies: what else touches it?
  - Success metrics and observability: how do we know it is working?
- Optional future: structured stakeholder map (add/remove rows with stakeholder, position, assumption, risk columns) instead of free text. Not blocking.

### Phase 2: Requirements Elicitation (exists as "Extraction" — enhance significantly)

**Current state:** AI extracts items from discovery notes. Items have title, desc, category, owner.

**Enhancements needed:**

The current "extraction" stage conflates two things: extracting requirements from discovery notes (AI-assisted) and structuring/editing those requirements (human). Split this into a proper requirements elicitation phase:

1. **Entity extraction** — Before extracting requirements, identify domain entities from discovery notes: nouns the team acts on, references, tracks, or governs.

2. **System property generation** — For each entity, generate the four-column property matrix:
   - Safety: what must never be true, even for a moment?
   - Liveness: what must eventually become true, and within what bound?
   - Invariant: what relationship or data rule must always hold?
   - Bound: what ceiling, floor, throughput, or deadline applies?

   Properties attach at the session level, persist across downstream phases, and surface as guardrails during MoSCoW, story decomposition, INVEST checks, and export. They are not requirements or stories; they constrain both.

3. **AI extraction stays** — the Ollama call that pulls candidate items from discovery notes. This is the starting point, not the end.

4. **Requirement types** — Each item needs a type field:
   - `functional` — what the system does (observable behavior)
   - `nfr` — quality attribute (performance, security, accessibility, etc.)
   - `constraint` — non-negotiable boundary (tech stack, compliance, budget, timeline)

5. **NFR subcategories** — When type is `nfr`, show a subcategory picker: performance, availability, scalability, security, accessibility, observability, maintainability.

6. **Acceptance criteria** — Each requirement should have an optional acceptance criteria field. Free text. This gets carried forward into stories.

7. **EARS requirement syntax** — JTBD captures the job and context; EARS turns that context into unambiguous requirements. Requirements should be expressible with Easy Approach to Requirements Syntax patterns:
   - Ubiquitous: `The [system] shall [action].`
   - Event-driven: `When [event], the [system] shall [action].`
   - State-driven: `While [state], the [system] shall [action].`
   - Unwanted behavior: `If [condition], then the [system] shall [action].`
   - Optional feature: `Where [feature], the [system] shall [action].`
   - Combined context: `While [state], when [event], the [system] shall [action].`

   Store the selected EARS pattern and structured context fields. This makes missing triggers, states, failure modes, and feature applicability visible during Phase 2 and feeds directly into Given/When/Then acceptance criteria during Phase 4.

8. **Dependency tagging** — Allow marking dependencies between requirements. Simple: a "depends on" dropdown that references other requirements by title.

9. **Requirement quality indicators** — Visual hints for incomplete requirements:
   - Missing acceptance criteria → amber dot
   - Category is still "decision" (not yet classified as functional/nfr/constraint) → amber dot
   - No owner → grey dot
   - Has acceptance criteria + type + owner → green dot

10. **Update the Ollama prompt** to also extract NFRs and constraints, not just functional items. The current prompt only asks for "actionable items." Expand it to explicitly request domain entities, system properties, non-functional requirements, constraints, and a proposed EARS pattern for each extracted item.

### Phase 3: MoSCoW (DONE)

**Current state:** Works well. Timer, keyboard shortcuts, queue sidebar.

**Enhancements needed:**

1. **Dependency warnings** — If item B depends on item A, and A is assigned Could Have or Won't Have while B is Must Have or Should Have, show a visual warning: "This item depends on [A] which is currently [Won't Have]."

2. **Must Have cap** — Show a running count: "X of Y items are Must Have (Z%)". If Must Have exceeds 60% of total items, show a warning banner: "More than 60% Must Have — prioritization may not be effective."

3. **Category filter in queue** — Let the facilitator filter the queue sidebar by requirement type (functional, nfr, constraint) to work through categories in blocks if desired.

4. **Decision tracker with aging** — Every MoSCoW decision already captures owner and deadline. Add a dashboard view that makes follow-up operational:
   - Due this week
   - Overdue decisions, shown in red
   - Stalled decisions with no owner assigned

   This should answer "what's overdue?" without requiring a full export review.

### Phase 4: Story Decomposition (DONE)

This is the biggest new phase. It takes prioritized requirements (Must Have and Should Have from MoSCoW) and decomposes them into user stories.

**Layout:** Similar to MoSCoW — main panel + sidebar. But instead of one-at-a-time facilitation, this is a workspace where you can see all requirements and their child stories.

**Core features:**

1. **Requirement → Story mapping** — Left panel shows the prioritized requirements (Must Have first, then Should Have). Clicking a requirement opens it and shows its child stories below.

2. **Story creation** — For each requirement, the user can:
   - Manually add stories using the "As a [persona], I want [capability], so that [outcome]" template. Provide three input fields, not a single text box.
   - Use Ollama to auto-generate story suggestions from the requirement text + acceptance criteria. Same model switcher as Phase 2. The user reviews, edits, accepts, or discards each suggestion.

3. **Story fields:**
   - `persona` — who (text input)
   - `capability` — what they want (text input)
   - `outcome` — so that / why (text input)
   - `acceptance_criteria` — list of criteria. Each criterion is a text string. Add/remove. Carry forward any acceptance criteria from the parent requirement as a starting point.
   - `size` — estimate: S, M, L, XL (button toggle)
   - `type` — `user_story`, `technical`, `spike`
   - `status` — `draft`, `ready`, `needs_split`

4. **INVEST check** — When a story is marked "ready", run a lightweight validation:
   - Has persona, capability, and outcome filled in? (Valuable, Negotiable)
   - Has at least one acceptance criterion? (Testable)
   - Size is S or M? (Small — if L or XL, suggest splitting)
   - Show pass/fail indicators, not blocking

5. **AI story generation prompt** — When the user clicks "Suggest Stories" for a requirement, send to Ollama:
   - The requirement title, description, acceptance criteria, and type
   - Ask for 3-5 user stories in JSON format
   - Each with persona, capability, outcome, and 2-3 acceptance criteria
   - Parse and display as editable drafts

6. **Epic grouping** — Each requirement effectively becomes an epic. The stories under it are the deliverable chunks. Show a count: "3 stories, 2 ready, 1 draft."

7. **Story splitting helper** — For stories sized L or XL, offer a "Split" button that sends the story to Ollama with a prompt asking for 2-3 smaller stories that decompose the original. Same review/edit/accept flow.

### Phase 5: Backlog & Export (DONE)

**Current state:** Shows MoSCoW 2x2 grid and plain text export.

**Enhancements needed:**

1. **Full backlog view** — Show all stories grouped by epic (requirement), ordered by MoSCoW tier (Must Have first). Each story shows its status, size, and acceptance criteria count.

2. **Sprint planning helper** — Let the user define sprint capacity (e.g., "we can do 8-10 stories per sprint" or use a point total). Then drag or assign stories to Sprint 1, Sprint 2, etc. Simple — just buckets with a running count. Not a full sprint board.

3. **Release forecast** — Based on sprint capacity and total story count, show: "At current capacity, Must Haves require ~X sprints. Must + Should = ~Y sprints."

4. **Export formats:**
   - **Markdown** — Full document: discovery summary → requirements → MoSCoW decisions → stories with acceptance criteria → sprint plan
   - **CSV** — Flat table of stories: epic, title (as a/i want/so that combined), acceptance criteria, size, type, sprint assignment, MoSCoW tier. For Jira import.
   - **Clipboard** — Current plain text export, enhanced with story details

5. **Session save/load** — Use localStorage to save the full session state. List saved sessions on the setup page. Load a previous session to continue work. This is critical — a pipeline session can span multiple sittings.

6. **Auto-generated stakeholder status brief** — Add a one-button brief generator for Slack/email updates. This is not the full export. It should produce a concise leadership-ready summary:
   - What was decided
   - What's blocked
   - What's next
   - Who owns what

   Ollama can draft the text from session state, then the facilitator edits and copies it.

7. **Traceability chain** — Make the path from problem → requirement → MoSCoW decision → story → acceptance criteria clickable end-to-end. A story should expose the requirement behind it, the discovery note or problem statement that produced it, and the prioritization decision that justified it. This keeps sprint work defensible when questioned later.

8. **ADR generation for technical decisions** — For MoSCoW items that are technical decisions, offer a lightweight Architecture Decision Record draft:
   - Context
   - Decision
   - Consequences
   - Status

   Ollama can draft the ADR from the discovery notes plus the MoSCoW decision; the user edits and exports markdown.

### Cross-Phase Governance Enhancements (DONE)

1. **Assumption lifecycle** — Discovery assumptions should become first-class objects instead of remaining free text. Track each assumption through `unvalidated`, `testing`, `validated`, and `invalidated`.

2. **Assumption impact flags** — Requirements should be able to depend on assumptions. If an assumption is invalidated, every dependent requirement should show a re-evaluation flag, especially Must Have items.

3. **Decision and assumption dashboard** — Add an outcome-driving dashboard that combines overdue decisions, ownerless decisions, active assumption tests, invalidated assumptions, and requirements needing re-evaluation.

### Phase 6: Retrospective & Outcome Tracking (DONE)

**Purpose:** Close the feedback loop. After delivery, facilitators re-score desired outcomes to measure actual impact.

**Core concept:**
1. Pull up a completed session (stored via session save/load)
2. For each desired outcome and scored MoSCoW item, show the original importance/satisfaction ratings
3. Facilitator re-rates satisfaction post-delivery
4. System computes delta automatically: `impact = new_satisfaction - old_satisfaction`
5. Surface which items had biggest/smallest impact — did we move the needle?

**Key features:**
- **Re-scoring UI** — Same 1-10 satisfaction buttons, but showing "before" score alongside for context
- **Impact dashboard** — Items ranked by delta. Green = improved significantly. Red = no movement despite being prioritized.
- **Outcome validation** — For JTBD desired outcomes: did the intervention actually minimize/increase the metric?
- **Learning export** — Structured summary of what worked, what didn't, feeds into session-history RAG

### Phase 7: Session-History RAG (NEW — roadmap)

**Purpose:** Ground future sessions in organizational memory — past decisions, past outcomes, institutional learning.

**Core concept:**
- Each completed session (discovery notes + decisions + retrospective deltas) is chunked into JSONL format
- Appended to `sessions_chunks.jsonl` alongside the methodology chunks
- TF-IDF retriever already supports multiple sources — add session chunks as a second corpus
- Chapter bias: methodology chunks for methodology questions, session chunks for "have we seen this before?" questions

**Where it surfaces:**
- Discovery: "Last time your team tackled [similar domain], these were the top pain points..."
- Extraction: "Similar requirements in Project X were categorized as NFRs"
- MoSCoW: "This was a Must-Have last sprint and got descoped — here's what happened"
- SWOT: "Weakness identified in Q1: team lacks observability expertise"
- Retrospective: "Items with opportunity score >15 had 73% satisfaction improvement on average"

**Implementation:**
- Export hook: on session save, auto-generate session chunks (deterministic — template-based, no AI)
- Retriever: add `source_type` field to chunks (`methodology` vs `session_history`)
- Bias config: each phase declares which source types to prefer
- Recency weighting: newer sessions score higher in retrieval

### Remaining Test Coverage (backlog)

- `extraction.spec.js` — Model switcher, AI extract flow (structural assertions)
- `moscow.spec.js` — Tier assignment, keyboard shortcuts, timer, ratings, scoring
- `export.spec.js` — Dashboard render, landscape table, copy actions
- `pipeline.spec.js` — Full end-to-end flow through all stages
- CSS split chore: co-located component CSS files already done, verify no visual regressions

## Architecture

### File Structure

```
ba-pipeline/
├── CLAUDE.md              # This file
├── Dockerfile
├── docker-compose.yml
├── server.js              # Express: static serve + typed Ollama API gateway
├── server/
│   ├── agent/                  # ReAct agent toolbox
│   │   ├── registry.js         # Tool registry (5 deterministic tools)
│   │   ├── loop.js             # ReAct observe-think-act loop
│   │   └── router.js           # Express routes (POST /api/agent/chat)
│   └── rag/                    # JTBD RAG retrieval engine
│       ├── budget.js           # Token budget management
│       ├── loadChunks.js       # JSONL chunk loader
│       ├── retrieve.js         # TF-IDF retriever with chapter bias
│       ├── router.js           # Express routes (GET /chunks, POST /retrieve)
│       └── tfidf.js            # TF-IDF index builder and query
├── vite.config.js
├── package.json
├── index.html
└── src/
    ├── main.jsx
    ├── App.jsx             # Top-level state, stage routing, sidebar
    ├── index.css           # Global styles, 70s design tokens
    ├── stages/
    │   ├── Discovery.jsx       # Phase 1
    │   ├── Requirements.jsx    # Phase 2 (renamed from extraction)
    │   ├── Moscow.jsx          # Phase 3
    │   ├── Stories.jsx         # Phase 4 story decomposition
    │   ├── Backlog.jsx         # Phase 5 backlog & export
    │   ├── Retrospective.jsx   # Phase 6 outcome tracking
    │   └── Export.jsx          # Legacy export artifacts and governance
    ├── components/
    │   ├── AssumptionDashboard.jsx  # Cross-phase assumption lifecycle dashboard
    │   ├── BacklogView.jsx          # Full backlog grouped by epic
    │   ├── DesiredOutcomes.jsx      # Ulwick outcome capture (4-field syntax)
    │   ├── GovernanceDashboard.jsx
    │   ├── JobMapSection.jsx        # Universal Job Map 8-step accordion
    │   ├── JobStatementInput.jsx    # When/I want/So I can structured input
    │   ├── OpportunityLandscape.jsx # Opportunity score table for Export
    │   ├── RequirementPanel.jsx     # Requirement detail with child stories
    │   ├── RetrospectivePanel.jsx   # Re-scoring and impact delta display
    │   ├── StoryCard.jsx            # Individual story with INVEST indicators
    │   ├── StoryForm.jsx            # Three-field story creation (persona/capability/outcome)
    │   ├── SwotGrid.jsx             # SWOT 2x2 card grid with AI generation
    │   ├── SystemPropertiesPanel.jsx
    │   └── TowsMatrix.jsx          # TOWS strategic combination panel
    ├── lib/
    │   ├── assumptionLifecycle.js # 4-state assumption tracking (unvalidated/testing/validated/invalidated)
    │   ├── backlogBuilder.js    # Backlog grouping and ordering logic
    │   ├── constants.js         # Stages, sections, tiers, job map steps, SWOT quadrants
    │   ├── hints.js             # Static hints + job map hints + analysis prompt builder
    │   ├── investCheck.js       # INVEST validation for stories
    │   ├── opportunityScore.js  # Pure Opportunity Algorithm function
    │   ├── ragConfig.js         # RAG retrieval configuration constants
    │   ├── retrospective.js     # Impact delta computation and ranking
    │   ├── sprintPlanner.js     # Sprint capacity and story assignment
    │   └── traceability.js      # End-to-end traceability chain builder
    ├── contracts/              # Runtime validation and fail-loud guards
    ├── generators/             # Markdown/status/ADR/CSV export builders
    ├── ollama/                 # Ollama request and response contracts
    ├── prompts/                # Externalized Handlebars prompt catalog
    ├── selectors/              # Derived governance/traceability/session state
    ├── state/                  # Initial app/session defaults
    └── templates/              # Externalized Handlebars export templates
```

Stage components receive props from App.jsx and validate incoming boundaries. App.jsx owns shared state and stage navigation; contracts, generators, prompts, and selectors stay outside JSX.

### Engineering Principles

- **SOLID** — Keep stage components focused, state ownership explicit, and shared services narrow.
- **DRY** — Consolidate duplicated behavior, prompts, parsing, and validation rules. Do not abstract one-off JSX just to reduce lines.
- **KISS** — Prefer plain React state, simple data shapes, and direct functions until complexity proves a stronger pattern is needed.
- **Elegant** — Code should read plainly, with clear names and small functions. Avoid clever control flow or hidden coupling.
- **Contracts at every boundary** — Validate component props, stage state, Ollama request/response JSON, Express API inputs, export formats, and generated ADR/status-brief payloads. Every tier crossing is API-style: validate incoming payloads and shape outgoing payloads explicitly. Boundary failures should be explicit, not silently patched with defaults.
- **Fail loud, fail proud** — Missing required data, malformed model output, invalid state transitions, and broken invariants should produce visible, actionable failures. Do not continue with placeholder objects or quiet empty results.

### State Shape

All session state lives in App.jsx. Derived artifacts are built through selectors/generators only when needed.

```javascript
{
  stage: "discovery" | "extraction" | "moscow" | "stories" | "backlog" | "retrospective" | "export",
  section: "setup" | "problem" | "...",
  session: { 
    name, facilitator, date, participants, status, templateId,
    jobStatement: { situation, motivation, outcome },  // JTBD structured input
    desiredOutcomes: [{ id, direction, measure, object, clarifier }],  // Ulwick ODI outcomes
  },
  notes: { problem: "", current: "", future: "", ..., jobMap: {} },  // jobMap: Universal Job Map steps
  swotItems: { strengths: [], weaknesses: [], opportunities: [], threats: [] },  // SWOT analysis
  items: [{ id, title, desc, category, owner, assumptionStatus, dependsOnAssumptions }],
  systemPropertyMatrix: [{ name, safety, liveness, invariant, bound }],
  model: "qwen3:14b",
  decisions: { [itemId]: { tier, owner, deadline, decision, technical, consequences, importance, satisfaction } },  // importance + satisfaction for Opportunity scoring
  currentDecision: { tier, owner, deadline, decision, technical, consequences },
  stories: {  // Phase 4: keyed by parent requirement item ID
    [itemId]: [{
      id, persona, capability, outcome,
      acceptanceCriteria: [string],
      size: "S" | "M" | "L" | "XL",
      type: "user_story" | "technical" | "spike",
      status: "draft" | "ready" | "needs_split",
      sprintAssignment: number | null,
    }]
  }
}
```

### Ollama Integration

All production Ollama calls go through the Express typed API gateway at `/api/ollama/api/chat`.
Prompt text must not live inside React components, fetch calls, or ad hoc string builders.
Add or change prompts under `src/prompts/*.hbs.js`, register them in `src/prompts/catalog.js`,
and render them through `src/prompts/renderPrompt.js` so missing prompt names or context fail loudly.

**Existing prompts:**
- Requirements extraction from discovery notes (Phase 2): `src/prompts/extractItems.hbs.js`
- SWOT generation from discovery notes: `src/prompts/generateSwot.hbs.js`
- JTBD RAG context injection: `src/prompts/jtbdContext.hbs.js`

**Future prompts to add only when the feature exists:**
- Story generation from a requirement
- Story splitting suggestions

#### RAG Integration

The server loads `jtbd_chunks.jsonl` at startup and builds a TF-IDF index for retrieval-augmented generation of JTBD methodology context.

- `GET /api/jtbd/chunks?q=&n=&bias=` retrieves relevant JTBD methodology chunks
- Extraction prompt includes retrieved chunks via `jtbdContext.hbs.js` template
- Hints panel fetches RAG chunks before AI analysis
- Chapter bias: extraction prefers `ch04_odi`, hints prefer `ch02_needs`
- Token budgets: 1500 chars/chunk, 5000 total extraction, 3000 hints
- Graceful degradation: if chunks file missing, app works without RAG

#### Agent Toolbox

The server exposes a ReAct-style agent loop at `POST /api/agent/chat`. The agent orchestrates Ollama with 5 deterministic tools that operate on session state:

| Tool | Description |
|------|-------------|
| `session_summary` | Returns a compact summary of the current session state |
| `search_items` | Searches extracted items by keyword or category |
| `check_dependency_conflicts` | Detects MoSCoW tier conflicts between dependent items |
| `get_moscow_statistics` | Returns tier distribution, Must Have %, and cap warnings |
| `validate_completeness` | Checks for missing fields, orphaned stories, and governance gaps |

Tools are registered in `server/agent/registry.js`. The ReAct loop in `server/agent/loop.js` cycles observe-think-act until the model produces a final answer or hits the iteration cap. All tool implementations are pure functions over session state — no side effects, no Ollama calls.

All Ollama request builders must send `stream: false`. JSON-producing prompts must ask for pure JSON output (no markdown fences). Parse with `JSON.parse()` after stripping any accidental fences.

The model is user-selectable. Available models:
```javascript
const MODELS = [
  { id: "gemma4:e4b",  label: "Gemma 4 E4B",  size: "~6 GB",  desc: "Fast. Good for clean notes." },
  { id: "gemma4:26b",  label: "Gemma 4 26B",   size: "~16 GB", desc: "MoE. Better at ambiguous text." },
  { id: "qwen3:14b",   label: "Qwen 3 14B",    size: "~10 GB", desc: "Most reliable JSON output." },
];
```

### Design System

70s groovy palette with diagonal stripe pattern. Key tokens:

```css
--teal:      #0B7978;   /* primary accent, headings, active states */
--mustard:   #FCB632;   /* secondary accent, highlights, Could Have tier */
--tangerine: #F27238;   /* CTAs, buttons, Must Have tier */
--burgundy:  #811638;   /* emphasis, Won't Have tier */
--red:       #C32327;   /* warnings, time expired, overdue */
--cream:     #F5F0E1;   /* page background */
--ink:       #1C1C1A;   /* primary text, borders */
--muted:     #8C8878;   /* secondary text, labels (WCAG 4.6:1) */
--rule:      #D4CEBC;   /* borders, dividers */
```

Fonts: Libre Baskerville (headings), Barlow Condensed (UI, labels, body), IBM Plex Mono (data, inputs, counters). All loaded from Google Fonts in `index.html`.

Zero border-radius everywhere. No rounded corners. Diagonal stripe pattern on header/hero areas.

### Technical Constraints

- No TypeScript. Plain JSX.
- No additional npm dependencies beyond what's in package.json. No UI component libraries.
- No localStorage in artifacts (Claude.ai restriction), but this runs standalone in Docker so localStorage is fine for session persistence.
- Ollama responses can be slow (10-30 seconds for large prompts on smaller models). Always show a spinner/status indicator. Never leave the user staring at a frozen UI.
- All Ollama calls use `stream: false`. Do not implement streaming.
- The app must work with Podman as well as Docker. No Docker-specific features.

## Development Workflow

1. `npm install`
2. Start Ollama locally: `ollama serve` (or it's already running)
3. `npm run dev` — Vite dev server with hot reload, proxy to localhost:11434
4. Edit files, test in browser at localhost:5173
5. When ready: `npm run build && node server.js` to test production mode
6. `docker compose up -d --build` to test containerized

## Implementation Order

Build in this order to keep the app functional at every step:

1. **Refactor App.jsx** — Split into stage files under `src/stages/`. Extract shared components. Get the existing 4 stages working with the new file structure before adding anything.

2. **Enhance Phase 2 (Requirements)** — Add requirement types, NFR subcategories, acceptance criteria field, dependency tagging, quality indicators. Update Ollama prompt.

3. **Build Phase 4 (Stories)** — New stage. Requirement → story mapping, manual story creation with the three-field template, AI story generation, INVEST check, story splitting.

4. **Enhance Phase 3 (MoSCoW)** — Dependency warnings, Must Have cap indicator, category filter.

5. **Enhance Phase 5 (Backlog)** — Full backlog view, sprint planning buckets, release forecast, CSV and markdown export, session save/load.

6. **Polish** — Keyboard shortcuts across all phases, consistent loading states, error handling for Ollama failures, responsive layout tweaks.

## Code Style

- Functional components only. No class components.
- useState/useEffect for state management. No Redux, no Context API unless state drilling becomes genuinely painful (3+ levels deep).
- CSS lives in `src/index.css` using class names. No CSS-in-JS, no Tailwind, no styled-components. Inline styles only for truly dynamic values (colors that change based on state).
- Keep components under 300 lines. If a component exceeds that, extract sub-components.
- No comments explaining what code does. Comments only for why (non-obvious decisions).


# SOURCE: /Users/samfakhreddine/repos/gitrdunhq/baGuy/.claude/worktrees/agent-a6b9c74cd8367d28d/ba-pipeline/CLAUDE.md

# baGuy — Claude Code Instructions

## Project Overview

A self-hosted BA/PO requirements pipeline running as a Docker container with a React frontend and Express backend. Uses local Ollama for AI-assisted requirements extraction and story generation.

**Current pipeline:** Discovery → Extraction → MoSCoW → Export

**Stack:** Vite 8 + React 19 (no TypeScript), Express 5, Handlebars templates, Vitest/jsdom, and local Ollama through typed app API routes. Single Docker container. No external runtime dependency beyond Ollama on the host.

## What Exists

The current codebase has 4 implemented stages:

1. **Discovery** (complete) — 10-section facilitated walkthrough: session setup, problem statement, current state, desired future state, stakeholder map, open questions, assumptions, constraints & dependencies, success criteria, next steps. Each section is a free-text area except session setup which has structured fields.

2. **Extraction** (complete) — Sends discovery notes to Ollama, gets back a validated JSON array of candidate items. Model switcher uses local Ollama model discovery when available. Manual add/edit/delete of items. Each item has: title, desc, category (decision/assumption/spike/deliverable/risk), owner, assumption lifecycle, and assumption dependency tags.

3. **MoSCoW** (complete) — One item at a time with timer, M/S/C/W assignment, decision/rationale capture, owner, deadline. Keyboard shortcuts. Queue sidebar.

4. **Export** (implemented) — Shows MoSCoW results, governance dashboard, system properties, status brief, full markdown export, and technical ADR preview/copy actions.

## Roadmap

Expand to a full 5-phase pipeline. The current stages map to phases 1, 2, 3, and 5. Phase 4 (Story Decomposition) is missing entirely, and the existing stages still have enhancement opportunities.

### Phase 1: Discovery (exists — enhance)

**Current state:** Works. Free-text sections with navigation.

**Enhancements needed:**
- **JTBD elicitation spine** — Discovery should guide facilitators through Jobs To Be Done:
  - Trigger: what happened right before the team started this work?
  - Current behavior: what do they do today, step by step?
  - Pain: where does it break down or create friction?
  - Desired outcome: what changes in their day if this works?
  - Internalized constraints: what have they tried, and why did it fail?

  Store the job as `When [situation], I want to [motivation], so I can [outcome]`.
- **SQUARE coverage checklist** — Ensure discovery captures:
  - Actors/personas: who uses it?
  - Jobs/workflows: what do they do with it?
  - Failure modes: what can go wrong?
  - Rules: what compliance, policy, or business rules apply?
  - Integrations/dependencies: what else touches it?
  - Success metrics and observability: how do we know it is working?
- Optional future: structured stakeholder map (add/remove rows with stakeholder, position, assumption, risk columns) instead of free text. Not blocking.

### Phase 2: Requirements Elicitation (exists as "Extraction" — enhance significantly)

**Current state:** AI extracts items from discovery notes. Items have title, desc, category, owner.

**Enhancements needed:**

The current "extraction" stage conflates two things: extracting requirements from discovery notes (AI-assisted) and structuring/editing those requirements (human). Split this into a proper requirements elicitation phase:

1. **Entity extraction** — Before extracting requirements, identify domain entities from discovery notes: nouns the team acts on, references, tracks, or governs.

2. **System property generation** — For each entity, generate the four-column property matrix:
   - Safety: what must never be true, even for a moment?
   - Liveness: what must eventually become true, and within what bound?
   - Invariant: what relationship or data rule must always hold?
   - Bound: what ceiling, floor, throughput, or deadline applies?

   Properties attach at the session level, persist across downstream phases, and surface as guardrails during MoSCoW, story decomposition, INVEST checks, and export. They are not requirements or stories; they constrain both.

3. **AI extraction stays** — the Ollama call that pulls candidate items from discovery notes. This is the starting point, not the end.

4. **Requirement types** — Each item needs a type field:
   - `functional` — what the system does (observable behavior)
   - `nfr` — quality attribute (performance, security, accessibility, etc.)
   - `constraint` — non-negotiable boundary (tech stack, compliance, budget, timeline)

5. **NFR subcategories** — When type is `nfr`, show a subcategory picker: performance, availability, scalability, security, accessibility, observability, maintainability.

6. **Acceptance criteria** — Each requirement should have an optional acceptance criteria field. Free text. This gets carried forward into stories.

7. **EARS requirement syntax** — JTBD captures the job and context; EARS turns that context into unambiguous requirements. Requirements should be expressible with Easy Approach to Requirements Syntax patterns:
   - Ubiquitous: `The [system] shall [action].`
   - Event-driven: `When [event], the [system] shall [action].`
   - State-driven: `While [state], the [system] shall [action].`
   - Unwanted behavior: `If [condition], then the [system] shall [action].`
   - Optional feature: `Where [feature], the [system] shall [action].`
   - Combined context: `While [state], when [event], the [system] shall [action].`

   Store the selected EARS pattern and structured context fields. This makes missing triggers, states, failure modes, and feature applicability visible during Phase 2 and feeds directly into Given/When/Then acceptance criteria during Phase 4.

8. **Dependency tagging** — Allow marking dependencies between requirements. Simple: a "depends on" dropdown that references other requirements by title.

9. **Requirement quality indicators** — Visual hints for incomplete requirements:
   - Missing acceptance criteria → amber dot
   - Category is still "decision" (not yet classified as functional/nfr/constraint) → amber dot
   - No owner → grey dot
   - Has acceptance criteria + type + owner → green dot

10. **Update the Ollama prompt** to also extract NFRs and constraints, not just functional items. The current prompt only asks for "actionable items." Expand it to explicitly request domain entities, system properties, non-functional requirements, constraints, and a proposed EARS pattern for each extracted item.

### Phase 3: MoSCoW (exists — minor enhancement)

**Current state:** Works well. Timer, keyboard shortcuts, queue sidebar.

**Enhancements needed:**

1. **Dependency warnings** — If item B depends on item A, and A is assigned Could Have or Won't Have while B is Must Have or Should Have, show a visual warning: "This item depends on [A] which is currently [Won't Have]."

2. **Must Have cap** — Show a running count: "X of Y items are Must Have (Z%)". If Must Have exceeds 60% of total items, show a warning banner: "More than 60% Must Have — prioritization may not be effective."

3. **Category filter in queue** — Let the facilitator filter the queue sidebar by requirement type (functional, nfr, constraint) to work through categories in blocks if desired.

4. **Decision tracker with aging** — Every MoSCoW decision already captures owner and deadline. Add a dashboard view that makes follow-up operational:
   - Due this week
   - Overdue decisions, shown in red
   - Stalled decisions with no owner assigned

   This should answer "what's overdue?" without requiring a full export review.

### Phase 4: Story Decomposition (NEW — build from scratch)

This is the biggest new phase. It takes prioritized requirements (Must Have and Should Have from MoSCoW) and decomposes them into user stories.

**Layout:** Similar to MoSCoW — main panel + sidebar. But instead of one-at-a-time facilitation, this is a workspace where you can see all requirements and their child stories.

**Core features:**

1. **Requirement → Story mapping** — Left panel shows the prioritized requirements (Must Have first, then Should Have). Clicking a requirement opens it and shows its child stories below.

2. **Story creation** — For each requirement, the user can:
   - Manually add stories using the "As a [persona], I want [capability], so that [outcome]" template. Provide three input fields, not a single text box.
   - Use Ollama to auto-generate story suggestions from the requirement text + acceptance criteria. Same model switcher as Phase 2. The user reviews, edits, accepts, or discards each suggestion.

3. **Story fields:**
   - `persona` — who (text input)
   - `capability` — what they want (text input)
   - `outcome` — so that / why (text input)
   - `acceptance_criteria` — list of criteria. Each criterion is a text string. Add/remove. Carry forward any acceptance criteria from the parent requirement as a starting point.
   - `size` — estimate: S, M, L, XL (button toggle)
   - `type` — `user_story`, `technical`, `spike`
   - `status` — `draft`, `ready`, `needs_split`

4. **INVEST check** — When a story is marked "ready", run a lightweight validation:
   - Has persona, capability, and outcome filled in? (Valuable, Negotiable)
   - Has at least one acceptance criterion? (Testable)
   - Size is S or M? (Small — if L or XL, suggest splitting)
   - Show pass/fail indicators, not blocking

5. **AI story generation prompt** — When the user clicks "Suggest Stories" for a requirement, send to Ollama:
   - The requirement title, description, acceptance criteria, and type
   - Ask for 3-5 user stories in JSON format
   - Each with persona, capability, outcome, and 2-3 acceptance criteria
   - Parse and display as editable drafts

6. **Epic grouping** — Each requirement effectively becomes an epic. The stories under it are the deliverable chunks. Show a count: "3 stories, 2 ready, 1 draft."

7. **Story splitting helper** — For stories sized L or XL, offer a "Split" button that sends the story to Ollama with a prompt asking for 2-3 smaller stories that decompose the original. Same review/edit/accept flow.

### Phase 5: Backlog & Export (exists as "Export" — enhance significantly)

**Current state:** Shows MoSCoW 2x2 grid and plain text export.

**Enhancements needed:**

1. **Full backlog view** — Show all stories grouped by epic (requirement), ordered by MoSCoW tier (Must Have first). Each story shows its status, size, and acceptance criteria count.

2. **Sprint planning helper** — Let the user define sprint capacity (e.g., "we can do 8-10 stories per sprint" or use a point total). Then drag or assign stories to Sprint 1, Sprint 2, etc. Simple — just buckets with a running count. Not a full sprint board.

3. **Release forecast** — Based on sprint capacity and total story count, show: "At current capacity, Must Haves require ~X sprints. Must + Should = ~Y sprints."

4. **Export formats:**
   - **Markdown** — Full document: discovery summary → requirements → MoSCoW decisions → stories with acceptance criteria → sprint plan
   - **CSV** — Flat table of stories: epic, title (as a/i want/so that combined), acceptance criteria, size, type, sprint assignment, MoSCoW tier. For Jira import.
   - **Clipboard** — Current plain text export, enhanced with story details

5. **Session save/load** — Use localStorage to save the full session state. List saved sessions on the setup page. Load a previous session to continue work. This is critical — a pipeline session can span multiple sittings.

6. **Auto-generated stakeholder status brief** — Add a one-button brief generator for Slack/email updates. This is not the full export. It should produce a concise leadership-ready summary:
   - What was decided
   - What's blocked
   - What's next
   - Who owns what

   Ollama can draft the text from session state, then the facilitator edits and copies it.

7. **Traceability chain** — Make the path from problem → requirement → MoSCoW decision → story → acceptance criteria clickable end-to-end. A story should expose the requirement behind it, the discovery note or problem statement that produced it, and the prioritization decision that justified it. This keeps sprint work defensible when questioned later.

8. **ADR generation for technical decisions** — For MoSCoW items that are technical decisions, offer a lightweight Architecture Decision Record draft:
   - Context
   - Decision
   - Consequences
   - Status

   Ollama can draft the ADR from the discovery notes plus the MoSCoW decision; the user edits and exports markdown.

### Cross-Phase Governance Enhancements

1. **Assumption lifecycle** — Discovery assumptions should become first-class objects instead of remaining free text. Track each assumption through `unvalidated`, `testing`, `validated`, and `invalidated`.

2. **Assumption impact flags** — Requirements should be able to depend on assumptions. If an assumption is invalidated, every dependent requirement should show a re-evaluation flag, especially Must Have items.

3. **Decision and assumption dashboard** — Add an outcome-driving dashboard that combines overdue decisions, ownerless decisions, active assumption tests, invalidated assumptions, and requirements needing re-evaluation.

### Phase 6: Retrospective & Outcome Tracking (NEW — roadmap)

**Purpose:** Close the feedback loop. After delivery, facilitators re-score desired outcomes to measure actual impact.

**Core concept:**
1. Pull up a completed session (stored via session save/load)
2. For each desired outcome and scored MoSCoW item, show the original importance/satisfaction ratings
3. Facilitator re-rates satisfaction post-delivery
4. System computes delta automatically: `impact = new_satisfaction - old_satisfaction`
5. Surface which items had biggest/smallest impact — did we move the needle?

**Key features:**
- **Re-scoring UI** — Same 1-10 satisfaction buttons, but showing "before" score alongside for context
- **Impact dashboard** — Items ranked by delta. Green = improved significantly. Red = no movement despite being prioritized.
- **Outcome validation** — For JTBD desired outcomes: did the intervention actually minimize/increase the metric?
- **Learning export** — Structured summary of what worked, what didn't, feeds into session-history RAG

### Phase 7: Session-History RAG (NEW — roadmap)

**Purpose:** Ground future sessions in organizational memory — past decisions, past outcomes, institutional learning.

**Core concept:**
- Each completed session (discovery notes + decisions + retrospective deltas) is chunked into JSONL format
- Appended to `sessions_chunks.jsonl` alongside the methodology chunks
- TF-IDF retriever already supports multiple sources — add session chunks as a second corpus
- Chapter bias: methodology chunks for methodology questions, session chunks for "have we seen this before?" questions

**Where it surfaces:**
- Discovery: "Last time your team tackled [similar domain], these were the top pain points..."
- Extraction: "Similar requirements in Project X were categorized as NFRs"
- MoSCoW: "This was a Must-Have last sprint and got descoped — here's what happened"
- SWOT: "Weakness identified in Q1: team lacks observability expertise"
- Retrospective: "Items with opportunity score >15 had 73% satisfaction improvement on average"

**Implementation:**
- Export hook: on session save, auto-generate session chunks (deterministic — template-based, no AI)
- Retriever: add `source_type` field to chunks (`methodology` vs `session_history`)
- Bias config: each phase declares which source types to prefer
- Recency weighting: newer sessions score higher in retrieval

### Remaining Test Coverage (backlog)

- `extraction.spec.js` — Model switcher, AI extract flow (structural assertions)
- `moscow.spec.js` — Tier assignment, keyboard shortcuts, timer, ratings, scoring
- `export.spec.js` — Dashboard render, landscape table, copy actions
- `pipeline.spec.js` — Full end-to-end flow through all stages
- CSS split chore: co-located component CSS files already done, verify no visual regressions

## Architecture

### File Structure

```
ba-pipeline/
├── CLAUDE.md              # This file
├── Dockerfile
├── docker-compose.yml
├── server.js              # Express: static serve + typed Ollama API gateway
├── server/
│   └── rag/                    # JTBD RAG retrieval engine
│       ├── budget.js           # Token budget management
│       ├── loadChunks.js       # JSONL chunk loader
│       ├── retrieve.js         # TF-IDF retriever with chapter bias
│       ├── router.js           # Express routes (GET /chunks, POST /retrieve)
│       └── tfidf.js            # TF-IDF index builder and query
├── vite.config.js
├── package.json
├── index.html
└── src/
    ├── main.jsx
    ├── App.jsx             # Top-level state, stage routing, sidebar
    ├── index.css           # Global styles, design tokens
    ├── stages/
    │   ├── Discovery.jsx       # Phase 1
    │   ├── Requirements.jsx    # Phase 2 (renamed from extraction)
    │   ├── Moscow.jsx          # Phase 3
    │   └── Export.jsx          # Phase 4 artifacts and governance
    ├── components/
    │   ├── DesiredOutcomes.jsx     # Ulwick outcome capture (4-field syntax)
    │   ├── GovernanceDashboard.jsx
    │   ├── JobMapSection.jsx       # Universal Job Map 8-step accordion
    │   ├── JobStatementInput.jsx   # When/I want/So I can structured input
    │   ├── OpportunityLandscape.jsx # Opportunity score table for Export
    │   ├── SwotGrid.jsx            # SWOT 2x2 card grid with AI generation
    │   ├── SystemPropertiesPanel.jsx
    │   └── TowsMatrix.jsx         # TOWS strategic combination panel
    ├── lib/
    │   ├── constants.js        # Stages, sections, tiers, job map steps, SWOT quadrants
    │   ├── hints.js            # Static hints + job map hints + analysis prompt builder
    │   ├── opportunityScore.js # Pure Opportunity Algorithm function
    │   └── ragConfig.js        # RAG retrieval configuration constants
    ├── contracts/              # Runtime validation and fail-loud guards
    ├── generators/             # Markdown/status/ADR export builders
    ├── ollama/                 # Ollama request and response contracts
    ├── prompts/                # Externalized Handlebars prompt catalog
    ├── selectors/              # Derived governance/traceability/session state
    ├── state/                  # Initial app/session defaults
    └── templates/              # Externalized Handlebars export templates
```

Stage components receive props from App.jsx and validate incoming boundaries. App.jsx owns shared state and stage navigation; contracts, generators, prompts, and selectors stay outside JSX.

### Engineering Principles

- **SOLID** — Keep stage components focused, state ownership explicit, and shared services narrow.
- **DRY** — Consolidate duplicated behavior, prompts, parsing, and validation rules. Do not abstract one-off JSX just to reduce lines.
- **KISS** — Prefer plain React state, simple data shapes, and direct functions until complexity proves a stronger pattern is needed.
- **Elegant** — Code should read plainly, with clear names and small functions. Avoid clever control flow or hidden coupling.
- **Contracts at every boundary** — Validate component props, stage state, Ollama request/response JSON, Express API inputs, export formats, and generated ADR/status-brief payloads. Every tier crossing is API-style: validate incoming payloads and shape outgoing payloads explicitly. Boundary failures should be explicit, not silently patched with defaults.
- **Fail loud, fail proud** — Missing required data, malformed model output, invalid state transitions, and broken invariants should produce visible, actionable failures. Do not continue with placeholder objects or quiet empty results.

### State Shape

All session state lives in App.jsx. Derived artifacts are built through selectors/generators only when needed.

```javascript
{
  stage: "discovery" | "extraction" | "moscow" | "export",
  section: "setup" | "problem" | "...",
  session: { 
    name, facilitator, date, participants, status,
    jobStatement: { situation, motivation, outcome },  // JTBD structured input
    desiredOutcomes: [{ id, direction, measure, object, clarifier }],  // Ulwick ODI outcomes
  },
  notes: { problem: "", current: "", future: "", ..., jobMap: {} },  // jobMap: Universal Job Map steps
  swotItems: { strengths: [], weaknesses: [], opportunities: [], threats: [] },  // SWOT analysis
  items: [{ id, title, desc, category, owner, assumptionStatus, dependsOnAssumptions }],
  systemPropertyMatrix: [{ name, safety, liveness, invariant, bound }],
  model: "qwen3:14b",
  decisions: { [itemId]: { tier, owner, deadline, decision, technical, consequences, importance, satisfaction } },  // importance + satisfaction for Opportunity scoring
  currentDecision: { tier, owner, deadline, decision, technical, consequences }
}
```

### Ollama Integration

All production Ollama calls go through the Express typed API gateway at `/api/ollama/api/chat`.
Prompt text must not live inside React components, fetch calls, or ad hoc string builders.
Add or change prompts under `src/prompts/*.hbs.js`, register them in `src/prompts/catalog.js`,
and render them through `src/prompts/renderPrompt.js` so missing prompt names or context fail loudly.

**Existing prompts:**
- Requirements extraction from discovery notes (Phase 2): `src/prompts/extractItems.hbs.js`
- SWOT generation from discovery notes: `src/prompts/generateSwot.hbs.js`
- JTBD RAG context injection: `src/prompts/jtbdContext.hbs.js`

**Future prompts to add only when the feature exists:**
- Story generation from a requirement
- Story splitting suggestions

#### RAG Integration

The server loads `jtbd_chunks.jsonl` at startup and builds a TF-IDF index for retrieval-augmented generation of JTBD methodology context.

- `GET /api/jtbd/chunks?q=&n=&bias=` retrieves relevant JTBD methodology chunks
- Extraction prompt includes retrieved chunks via `jtbdContext.hbs.js` template
- Hints panel fetches RAG chunks before AI analysis
- Chapter bias: extraction prefers `ch04_odi`, hints prefer `ch02_needs`
- Token budgets: 1500 chars/chunk, 5000 total extraction, 3000 hints
- Graceful degradation: if chunks file missing, app works without RAG

All Ollama request builders must send `stream: false`. JSON-producing prompts must ask for pure JSON output (no markdown fences). Parse with `JSON.parse()` after stripping any accidental fences.

The model is user-selectable. Available models:
```javascript
const MODELS = [
  { id: "gemma4:e4b",  label: "Gemma 4 E4B",  size: "~6 GB",  desc: "Fast. Good for clean notes." },
  { id: "gemma4:26b",  label: "Gemma 4 26B",   size: "~16 GB", desc: "MoE. Better at ambiguous text." },
  { id: "qwen3:14b",   label: "Qwen 3 14B",    size: "~10 GB", desc: "Most reliable JSON output." },
];
```

### Design System

DATUM-adjacent. Do not change the existing aesthetic. Key tokens:

```css
--paper:   #F4F1EA;    /* page background */
--card:    #FDFCF7;    /* card/input background */
--ink:     #1C1C1A;    /* primary text, borders */
--orange:  #C84315;    /* accent, CTAs, International Orange */
--green:   #4A6741;    /* success, Could Have tier */
--muted:   #8C8878;    /* secondary text, labels */
--rule:    #D4CEBC;    /* borders, dividers */
--warn:    #D4380D;    /* warnings, time expired */
```

Fonts: Libre Baskerville (headings), Barlow Condensed (UI, labels, body), IBM Plex Mono (data, inputs, counters). All loaded from Google Fonts in `index.html`.

Zero border-radius everywhere. No rounded corners.

### Technical Constraints

- No TypeScript. Plain JSX.
- No additional npm dependencies beyond what's in package.json. No UI component libraries.
- No localStorage in artifacts (Claude.ai restriction), but this runs standalone in Docker so localStorage is fine for session persistence.
- Ollama responses can be slow (10-30 seconds for large prompts on smaller models). Always show a spinner/status indicator. Never leave the user staring at a frozen UI.
- All Ollama calls use `stream: false`. Do not implement streaming.
- The app must work with Podman as well as Docker. No Docker-specific features.

## Development Workflow

1. `npm install`
2. Start Ollama locally: `ollama serve` (or it's already running)
3. `npm run dev` — Vite dev server with hot reload, proxy to localhost:11434
4. Edit files, test in browser at localhost:5173
5. When ready: `npm run build && node server.js` to test production mode
6. `docker compose up -d --build` to test containerized

## Implementation Order

Build in this order to keep the app functional at every step:

1. **Refactor App.jsx** — Split into stage files under `src/stages/`. Extract shared components. Get the existing 4 stages working with the new file structure before adding anything.

2. **Enhance Phase 2 (Requirements)** — Add requirement types, NFR subcategories, acceptance criteria field, dependency tagging, quality indicators. Update Ollama prompt.

3. **Build Phase 4 (Stories)** — New stage. Requirement → story mapping, manual story creation with the three-field template, AI story generation, INVEST check, story splitting.

4. **Enhance Phase 3 (MoSCoW)** — Dependency warnings, Must Have cap indicator, category filter.

5. **Enhance Phase 5 (Backlog)** — Full backlog view, sprint planning buckets, release forecast, CSV and markdown export, session save/load.

6. **Polish** — Keyboard shortcuts across all phases, consistent loading states, error handling for Ollama failures, responsive layout tweaks.

## Code Style

- Functional components only. No class components.
- useState/useEffect for state management. No Redux, no Context API unless state drilling becomes genuinely painful (3+ levels deep).
- CSS lives in `src/index.css` using class names. No CSS-in-JS, no Tailwind, no styled-components. Inline styles only for truly dynamic values (colors that change based on state).
- Keep components under 300 lines. If a component exceeds that, extract sub-components.
- No comments explaining what code does. Comments only for why (non-obvious decisions).


# SOURCE: /Users/samfakhreddine/repos/gitrdunhq/baGuy/.claude/worktrees/agent-a6b9c74cd8367d28d/AGENTS.md

# Repository Guidelines

## Project Structure & Module Organization

This repository is an export wrapper around the runnable app in `ba-pipeline/`. Work from that directory for installs, builds, and Docker commands. The React/Vite client lives in `ba-pipeline/src/`: `main.jsx` mounts the app, `App.jsx` owns stage routing and session state, `stages/` contains stage components, `selectors/` and `contracts/` contain deterministic logic, `templates/` contains Handlebars export templates, and `prompts/` contains swappable Ollama prompt templates. `ba-pipeline/server.js` is the Express production server and typed Ollama API boundary. `Dockerfile` and `docker-compose.yml` package the Vite build and serve it on port `3000`. Files under `docs/legacy/` and `patching3_moscow_runsheet.md` are reference artifacts, not part of the Vite build.

## Build, Test, and Development Commands

Run commands from `ba-pipeline/`.

- `npm install` installs locked Node dependencies from `package-lock.json`.
- `npm run dev` starts the Vite dev server with `/api/ollama` proxied to local Ollama.
- `npm run build` creates the production `dist/` bundle used by `server.js`.
- `npm run serve` serves the built app with Express; run `npm run build` first.
- `docker compose up -d --build` builds and runs the containerized app at `http://localhost:3000`.
- `OLLAMA_HOST=http://192.168.1.50:11434 docker compose up -d --build` points Docker at a Linux host Ollama instance.

Never run this app on port `3000` for local or LAN testing. Use a non-3000 port such as `4174`, for example `HOST=0.0.0.0 PORT=4174 npm run serve`.

## Coding Style & Naming Conventions

Use JavaScript ES modules, React function components, and hooks. Keep indentation at two spaces, strings in double quotes, and component files in PascalCase when new files are introduced. Use lower camelCase for state, functions, and props; reserve UPPER_SNAKE_CASE for constants such as `STAGES`, `TIERS`, and `MODELS`. Keep shared visual values in CSS custom properties in `src/index.css`.

## Testing Guidelines

Vitest and Testing Library are configured. Run `npm run test` before handoff and `npm run build` for production verification. Prefer colocated `*.test.js` or `*.test.jsx` files beside the module under test. Cover prompt/template rendering, fail-loud contract behavior, pure selectors, and stage component callbacks separately from the Ollama proxy.

## Commit & Pull Request Guidelines

This export has no `.git` history, so no project-specific commit convention is available. Use concise, imperative Conventional Commit-style messages such as `feat: add story decomposition stage` or `fix: handle Ollama proxy failures`. Pull requests should describe user-visible behavior, list verification commands, call out Docker/Ollama configuration changes, and include screenshots for UI changes.

All Git operations in this repository must be run through RTK. Use `rtk git status`, `rtk git add`, `rtk git commit`, and similar `rtk git ...` forms instead of bare `git ...` commands.

## Security & Configuration Tips

Do not commit secrets or host-specific Ollama URLs. Prefer `OLLAMA_HOST` environment overrides for deployment differences. Keep the app self-hosted and local-first: the only expected AI dependency is the configured Ollama endpoint.

## Requirements Writing Standard

Use JTBD as the elicitation frame and EARS as the writing syntax. Discovery should capture the job as `When [situation], I want to [motivation], so I can [outcome]`, including trigger, current behavior, pain, desired outcome, and constraints already internalized by the team. Use SQUARE-style coverage to check actors/personas, jobs/workflows, failure modes, rules, integrations/dependencies, and success metrics. At the start of Phase 2, extract domain entities and generate system properties from the four-column matrix: safety, liveness, invariant, and bound. In Phase 2, express each requirement with EARS: `The [system] shall [action]`, `When [event], the [system] shall [action]`, `While [state], the [system] shall [action]`, `If [condition], then the [system] shall [action]`, or `Where [feature], the [system] shall [action]`. Preserve selected properties and EARS patterns so Phase 4 can surface guardrails and translate requirements into Given/When/Then acceptance criteria with minimal information loss.

# WFC - Code Intelligence for ba-pipeline-full_1

This project uses WFC for structured planning, TDD-first implementation, and code review.

Bootstrap note: `wfc-init` is expected to create the local Claude allowlist during project setup by running the SafeClaude bootstrap. Re-run `wfc-safeclaude` later only when tool permissions need maintenance or tuning.
Prompt-contract note: `wfc-init` also seeds the shared contract model during SafeClaude bootstrap so new projects start with the base-contract, machine-envelope, and properties taxonomy already in context.

## Always Do

- **MUST run `wfc-review` before merging any PR.** Use the host-native invocation form (`/wfc-review` in Codex and Claude Code). The 5-reviewer consensus system catches issues that single-pass review misses.
- **MUST run impact analysis before editing widely-called symbols.** Use GitNexus (`gitnexus impact <symbol>` or `npx gitnexus impact --repo <repo> <symbol>`) to check blast radius before modifying functions with many callers.
- **MUST check knowledge freshness.** Run `wfc helpers status`; if knowledge is stale, results may be outdated.
- **MUST follow TDD workflow: write tests first, verify they fail (RED), then implement the minimum code to pass (GREEN), then refactor.** Never write implementation code before a failing test proves the behavior does not exist.
- When planning features, use `wfc-plan` for structured planning with adaptive interview.
- When deciding sequence, use `wfc-roadmap` to slot work against the current roadmap before planning or implementation.
- When implementing, use `wfc-implement` for parallel TDD-based execution with worktree isolation.

## Code Discipline

These rules override default AI coding tendencies. Full details live in `.claude/rules/` when present.

1. **No silent fallbacks** - never use `??` or `||` to mask data that should not be missing. Throw instead.
2. **No catch-all try/catch** - business logic must let errors propagate. Catch only at boundaries.
3. **Fail loud, fail proud** - invalid state, malformed data, missing owners, failed parsing, and broken invariants must surface immediately with actionable context. Do not hide them behind empty arrays, placeholder text, or "best effort" continuation.
4. **Tests must break when code breaks** - assert concrete values, not existence.
5. **No invented API surface** - never call methods, import symbols, or use options you have not confirmed exist.
6. **Minimal diffs only** - change only what the task requires.
7. **500-line file hard cap** - split source files before they exceed 500 lines.
8. **Three-tier architecture** - Presentation thin, Logic pure, Data without business rules.
9. **Contracts at every boundary** - define and validate the data shape where information crosses modules, stages, network calls, storage, prompts, exports, and component props. Every tier crossing is API-style: validate incoming payloads and shape outgoing payloads explicitly. Invalid boundary data must fail loudly with a useful message.
10. **SOLID by default** - keep modules focused, dependencies explicit, and extension points narrow. Do not add abstractions until the second concrete use proves the boundary.
11. **DRY, but not premature** - remove meaningful duplication in behavior or rules. Prefer duplicated simple UI markup over a vague abstraction that hides intent.
12. **KISS** - choose the smallest design that satisfies the requirement and is easy to test. Avoid framework, state, or build complexity that the current app does not need.
13. **Elegant means obvious** - favor readable names, straight-line data flow, and small functions. Clever code is not elegant if the next maintainer has to simulate it mentally.
14. **No AI leakage** - branch names, commits, PR titles must never reveal which AI tool was used.
15. **LLM for reasoning, code for determinism** - use models for ambiguity and synthesis; use deterministic code for routing, validation, paths, artifact writes, side effects, state transitions, branch targets, and guardrails.
16. Prompt contracts are properties-backed: invariants live in the shared contract body, and properties are the machine-checkable form.

## Skill Quick Reference

| Task | Skill |
|------|-------|
| Full auto pipeline | `wfc-lfg "feature"` |
| Quick single feature | `wfc-build "feature"` |
| Structured planning | `wfc-plan` |
| Parallel TDD implementation | `wfc-implement` |
| 5-agent consensus review | `wfc-review` |
| Business analysis | `wfc-ba` |
| Fix PR comments | `wfc-pr-comments` |
| Maintain local allowlist | `wfc-safeclaude` |

## Never Do

- NEVER push directly to `main`. Always use feature branches with PR.
- NEVER branch from a feature branch. Always branch from `main`.
- NEVER skip pre-commit hooks.
- NEVER commit failing tests.
- NEVER commit dev artifacts from the repo-local `.wfc/` workspace.
- NEVER scatter plans, reviews, or dev artifacts beside source files. Store them under the repo-local `.wfc/` workspace.
- NEVER run `make format` after commit; run it before.
- NEVER write implementation code before writing a failing test.
- NEVER use `??` or `||` to hide data that should not be missing.
- NEVER reveal AI tool names in branches, commits, or PRs.

## Observability

```bash
wfc helpers status
wfc helpers doctor
wfc helpers resume
wfc helpers clean
wfc helpers timeline
```

Use the host-native wrapper form for skill commands:

- Kiro: `@wfc-plan`, `@wfc-review`, `@wfc-implement`
- OpenCode: `/wfc-plan`, `/wfc-review`, `/wfc-implement`
- Gemini CLI: `/wfc-plan`, `/wfc-review`, `/wfc-implement`
- Claude Code: `/wfc-plan`, `/wfc-review`, `/wfc-implement`
