# SOURCE: /Users/samfakhreddine/repos/gitrdunhq/baGuy/.claude/worktrees/agent-a9487092eef3c02ad/ba-pipeline/CLAUDE.md

# baGuy — Claude Code Instructions

## Project Overview

A self-hosted BA/PO requirements pipeline running as a Docker container with a React frontend and Express backend. Uses local Ollama for AI-assisted requirements extraction and story generation.

**Current pipeline:** Discovery → Extraction → MoSCoW → Export

**Stack:** Vite 8 + React 19 (no TypeScript), Express 5, Handlebars templates, Vitest/jsdom, and local Ollama through typed app API routes. Single Docker container. No external runtime dependency beyond Ollama on the host.

## What Exists

The current codebase has 4 implemented stages:

1. **Discovery** (complete) — 10-section facilitated walkthrough: session setup, problem statement, current state, desired future state, stakeholder map, open questions, assumptions, constraints & dependencies, success criteria, next steps. Each section is a free-text area except session setup which has structured fields.

2. **Extraction** (complete) — Sends discovery notes to Ollama, gets back a validated JSON array of candidate items. Model switcher uses local Ollama model discovery when available. Manual add/edit/delete of items. Each item has: title, desc, category (decision/assumption/spike/deliverable/risk), owner, assumption lifecycle, and assumption dependency tags.

3. **MoSCoW** (complete) — One item at a time with timer, M/S/C/W assignment, decision/rationale capture, owner, deadline. Keyboard shortcuts. Queue sidebar.

4. **Export** (implemented) — Shows MoSCoW results, governance dashboard, system properties, status brief, full markdown export, and technical ADR preview/copy actions.

## Roadmap

Expand to a full 5-phase pipeline. The current stages map to phases 1, 2, 3, and 5. Phase 4 (Story Decomposition) is missing entirely, and the existing stages still have enhancement opportunities.

### Phase 1: Discovery (exists — enhance)

**Current state:** Works. Free-text sections with navigation.

**Enhancements needed:**
- **JTBD elicitation spine** — Discovery should guide facilitators through Jobs To Be Done:
  - Trigger: what happened right before the team started this work?
  - Current behavior: what do they do today, step by step?
  - Pain: where does it break down or create friction?
  - Desired outcome: what changes in their day if this works?
  - Internalized constraints: what have they tried, and why did it fail?

  Store the job as `When [situation], I want to [motivation], so I can [outcome]`.
- **SQUARE coverage checklist** — Ensure discovery captures:
  - Actors/personas: who uses it?
  - Jobs/workflows: what do they do with it?
  - Failure modes: what can go wrong?
  - Rules: what compliance, policy, or business rules apply?
  - Integrations/dependencies: what else touches it?
  - Success metrics and observability: how do we know it is working?
- Optional future: structured stakeholder map (add/remove rows with stakeholder, position, assumption, risk columns) instead of free text. Not blocking.

### Phase 2: Requirements Elicitation (exists as "Extraction" — enhance significantly)

**Current state:** AI extracts items from discovery notes. Items have title, desc, category, owner.

**Enhancements needed:**

The current "extraction" stage conflates two things: extracting requirements from discovery notes (AI-assisted) and structuring/editing those requirements (human). Split this into a proper requirements elicitation phase:

1. **Entity extraction** — Before extracting requirements, identify domain entities from discovery notes: nouns the team acts on, references, tracks, or governs.

2. **System property generation** — For each entity, generate the four-column property matrix:
   - Safety: what must never be true, even for a moment?
   - Liveness: what must eventually become true, and within what bound?
   - Invariant: what relationship or data rule must always hold?
   - Bound: what ceiling, floor, throughput, or deadline applies?

   Properties attach at the session level, persist across downstream phases, and surface as guardrails during MoSCoW, story decomposition, INVEST checks, and export. They are not requirements or stories; they constrain both.

3. **AI extraction stays** — the Ollama call that pulls candidate items from discovery notes. This is the starting point, not the end.

4. **Requirement types** — Each item needs a type field:
   - `functional` — what the system does (observable behavior)
   - `nfr` — quality attribute (performance, security, accessibility, etc.)
   - `constraint` — non-negotiable boundary (tech stack, compliance, budget, timeline)

5. **NFR subcategories** — When type is `nfr`, show a subcategory picker: performance, availability, scalability, security, accessibility, observability, maintainability.

6. **Acceptance criteria** — Each requirement should have an optional acceptance criteria field. Free text. This gets carried forward into stories.

7. **EARS requirement syntax** — JTBD captures the job and context; EARS turns that context into unambiguous requirements. Requirements should be expressible with Easy Approach to Requirements Syntax patterns:
   - Ubiquitous: `The [system] shall [action].`
   - Event-driven: `When [event], the [system] shall [action].`
   - State-driven: `While [state], the [system] shall [action].`
   - Unwanted behavior: `If [condition], then the [system] shall [action].`
   - Optional feature: `Where [feature], the [system] shall [action].`
   - Combined context: `While [state], when [event], the [system] shall [action].`

   Store the selected EARS pattern and structured context fields. This makes missing triggers, states, failure modes, and feature applicability visible during Phase 2 and feeds directly into Given/When/Then acceptance criteria during Phase 4.

8. **Dependency tagging** — Allow marking dependencies between requirements. Simple: a "depends on" dropdown that references other requirements by title.

9. **Requirement quality indicators** — Visual hints for incomplete requirements:
   - Missing acceptance criteria → amber dot
   - Category is still "decision" (not yet classified as functional/nfr/constraint) → amber dot
   - No owner → grey dot
   - Has acceptance criteria + type + owner → green dot

10. **Update the Ollama prompt** to also extract NFRs and constraints, not just functional items. The current prompt only asks for "actionable items." Expand it to explicitly request domain entities, system properties, non-functional requirements, constraints, and a proposed EARS pattern for each extracted item.

### Phase 3: MoSCoW (exists — minor enhancement)

**Current state:** Works well. Timer, keyboard shortcuts, queue sidebar.

**Enhancements needed:**

1. **Dependency warnings** — If item B depends on item A, and A is assigned Could Have or Won't Have while B is Must Have or Should Have, show a visual warning: "This item depends on [A] which is currently [Won't Have]."

2. **Must Have cap** — Show a running count: "X of Y items are Must Have (Z%)". If Must Have exceeds 60% of total items, show a warning banner: "More than 60% Must Have — prioritization may not be effective."

3. **Category filter in queue** — Let the facilitator filter the queue sidebar by requirement type (functional, nfr, constraint) to work through categories in blocks if desired.

4. **Decision tracker with aging** — Every MoSCoW decision already captures owner and deadline. Add a dashboard view that makes follow-up operational:
   - Due this week
   - Overdue decisions, shown in red
   - Stalled decisions with no owner assigned

   This should answer "what's overdue?" without requiring a full export review.

### Phase 4: Story Decomposition (NEW — build from scratch)

This is the biggest new phase. It takes prioritized requirements (Must Have and Should Have from MoSCoW) and decomposes them into user stories.

**Layout:** Similar to MoSCoW — main panel + sidebar. But instead of one-at-a-time facilitation, this is a workspace where you can see all requirements and their child stories.

**Core features:**

1. **Requirement → Story mapping** — Left panel shows the prioritized requirements (Must Have first, then Should Have). Clicking a requirement opens it and shows its child stories below.

2. **Story creation** — For each requirement, the user can:
   - Manually add stories using the "As a [persona], I want [capability], so that [outcome]" template. Provide three input fields, not a single text box.
   - Use Ollama to auto-generate story suggestions from the requirement text + acceptance criteria. Same model switcher as Phase 2. The user reviews, edits, accepts, or discards each suggestion.

3. **Story fields:**
   - `persona` — who (text input)
   - `capability` — what they want (text input)
   - `outcome` — so that / why (text input)
   - `acceptance_criteria` — list of criteria. Each criterion is a text string. Add/remove. Carry forward any acceptance criteria from the parent requirement as a starting point.
   - `size` — estimate: S, M, L, XL (button toggle)
   - `type` — `user_story`, `technical`, `spike`
   - `status` — `draft`, `ready`, `needs_split`

4. **INVEST check** — When a story is marked "ready", run a lightweight validation:
   - Has persona, capability, and outcome filled in? (Valuable, Negotiable)
   - Has at least one acceptance criterion? (Testable)
   - Size is S or M? (Small — if L or XL, suggest splitting)
   - Show pass/fail indicators, not blocking

5. **AI story generation prompt** — When the user clicks "Suggest Stories" for a requirement, send to Ollama:
   - The requirement title, description, acceptance criteria, and type
   - Ask for 3-5 user stories in JSON format
   - Each with persona, capability, outcome, and 2-3 acceptance criteria
   - Parse and display as editable drafts

6. **Epic grouping** — Each requirement effectively becomes an epic. The stories under it are the deliverable chunks. Show a count: "3 stories, 2 ready, 1 draft."

7. **Story splitting helper** — For stories sized L or XL, offer a "Split" button that sends the story to Ollama with a prompt asking for 2-3 smaller stories that decompose the original. Same review/edit/accept flow.

### Phase 5: Backlog & Export (exists as "Export" — enhance significantly)

**Current state:** Shows MoSCoW 2x2 grid and plain text export.

**Enhancements needed:**

1. **Full backlog view** — Show all stories grouped by epic (requirement), ordered by MoSCoW tier (Must Have first). Each story shows its status, size, and acceptance criteria count.

2. **Sprint planning helper** — Let the user define sprint capacity (e.g., "we can do 8-10 stories per sprint" or use a point total). Then drag or assign stories to Sprint 1, Sprint 2, etc. Simple — just buckets with a running count. Not a full sprint board.

3. **Release forecast** — Based on sprint capacity and total story count, show: "At current capacity, Must Haves require ~X sprints. Must + Should = ~Y sprints."

4. **Export formats:**
   - **Markdown** — Full document: discovery summary → requirements → MoSCoW decisions → stories with acceptance criteria → sprint plan
   - **CSV** — Flat table of stories: epic, title (as a/i want/so that combined), acceptance criteria, size, type, sprint assignment, MoSCoW tier. For Jira import.
   - **Clipboard** — Current plain text export, enhanced with story details

5. **Session save/load** — Use localStorage to save the full session state. List saved sessions on the setup page. Load a previous session to continue work. This is critical — a pipeline session can span multiple sittings.

6. **Auto-generated stakeholder status brief** — Add a one-button brief generator for Slack/email updates. This is not the full export. It should produce a concise leadership-ready summary:
   - What was decided
   - What's blocked
   - What's next
   - Who owns what

   Ollama can draft the text from session state, then the facilitator edits and copies it.

7. **Traceability chain** — Make the path from problem → requirement → MoSCoW decision → story → acceptance criteria clickable end-to-end. A story should expose the requirement behind it, the discovery note or problem statement that produced it, and the prioritization decision that justified it. This keeps sprint work defensible when questioned later.

8. **ADR generation for technical decisions** — For MoSCoW items that are technical decisions, offer a lightweight Architecture Decision Record draft:
   - Context
   - Decision
   - Consequences
   - Status

   Ollama can draft the ADR from the discovery notes plus the MoSCoW decision; the user edits and exports markdown.

### Cross-Phase Governance Enhancements

1. **Assumption lifecycle** — Discovery assumptions should become first-class objects instead of remaining free text. Track each assumption through `unvalidated`, `testing`, `validated`, and `invalidated`.

2. **Assumption impact flags** — Requirements should be able to depend on assumptions. If an assumption is invalidated, every dependent requirement should show a re-evaluation flag, especially Must Have items.

3. **Decision and assumption dashboard** — Add an outcome-driving dashboard that combines overdue decisions, ownerless decisions, active assumption tests, invalidated assumptions, and requirements needing re-evaluation.

## Architecture

### File Structure

```
ba-pipeline/
├── CLAUDE.md              # This file
├── Dockerfile
├── docker-compose.yml
├── server.js              # Express: static serve + typed Ollama API gateway
├── vite.config.js
├── package.json
├── index.html
└── src/
    ├── main.jsx
    ├── App.jsx             # Top-level state, stage routing, sidebar
    ├── index.css           # Global styles, design tokens
    ├── stages/
    │   ├── Discovery.jsx       # Phase 1
    │   ├── Requirements.jsx    # Phase 2 (renamed from extraction)
    │   ├── Moscow.jsx          # Phase 3
    │   └── Export.jsx          # Phase 4 artifacts and governance
    ├── components/
    │   ├── GovernanceDashboard.jsx
    │   └── SystemPropertiesPanel.jsx
    ├── contracts/              # Runtime validation and fail-loud guards
    ├── generators/             # Markdown/status/ADR export builders
    ├── ollama/                 # Ollama request and response contracts
    ├── prompts/                # Externalized Handlebars prompt catalog
    ├── selectors/              # Derived governance/traceability/session state
    ├── state/                  # Initial app/session defaults
    └── templates/              # Externalized Handlebars export templates
```

Stage components receive props from App.jsx and validate incoming boundaries. App.jsx owns shared state and stage navigation; contracts, generators, prompts, and selectors stay outside JSX.

### Engineering Principles

- **SOLID** — Keep stage components focused, state ownership explicit, and shared services narrow.
- **DRY** — Consolidate duplicated behavior, prompts, parsing, and validation rules. Do not abstract one-off JSX just to reduce lines.
- **KISS** — Prefer plain React state, simple data shapes, and direct functions until complexity proves a stronger pattern is needed.
- **Elegant** — Code should read plainly, with clear names and small functions. Avoid clever control flow or hidden coupling.
- **Contracts at every boundary** — Validate component props, stage state, Ollama request/response JSON, Express API inputs, export formats, and generated ADR/status-brief payloads. Every tier crossing is API-style: validate incoming payloads and shape outgoing payloads explicitly. Boundary failures should be explicit, not silently patched with defaults.
- **Fail loud, fail proud** — Missing required data, malformed model output, invalid state transitions, and broken invariants should produce visible, actionable failures. Do not continue with placeholder objects or quiet empty results.

### State Shape

All session state lives in App.jsx. Derived artifacts are built through selectors/generators only when needed.

```javascript
{
  stage: "discovery" | "extraction" | "moscow" | "export",
  section: "setup" | "problem" | "...",
  session: { name, facilitator, date, participants, status },
  notes: { problem: "", current: "", future: "", ... },
  items: [{ id, title, desc, category, owner, assumptionStatus, dependsOnAssumptions }],
  systemPropertyMatrix: [{ name, safety, liveness, invariant, bound }],
  model: "qwen3:14b",
  decisions: { [itemId]: { tier, owner, deadline, decision, technical, consequences } },
  currentDecision: { tier, owner, deadline, decision, technical, consequences }
}
```

### Ollama Integration

All production Ollama calls go through the Express typed API gateway at `/api/ollama/api/chat`.
Prompt text must not live inside React components, fetch calls, or ad hoc string builders.
Add or change prompts under `src/prompts/*.hbs.js`, register them in `src/prompts/catalog.js`,
and render them through `src/prompts/renderPrompt.js` so missing prompt names or context fail loudly.

**Existing prompts:**
- Requirements extraction from discovery notes (Phase 2): `src/prompts/extractItems.hbs.js`

**Future prompts to add only when the feature exists:**
- Story generation from a requirement
- Story splitting suggestions

All Ollama request builders must send `stream: false`. JSON-producing prompts must ask for pure JSON output (no markdown fences). Parse with `JSON.parse()` after stripping any accidental fences.

The model is user-selectable. Available models:
```javascript
const MODELS = [
  { id: "gemma4:e4b",  label: "Gemma 4 E4B",  size: "~6 GB",  desc: "Fast. Good for clean notes." },
  { id: "gemma4:26b",  label: "Gemma 4 26B",   size: "~16 GB", desc: "MoE. Better at ambiguous text." },
  { id: "qwen3:14b",   label: "Qwen 3 14B",    size: "~10 GB", desc: "Most reliable JSON output." },
];
```

### Design System

DATUM-adjacent. Do not change the existing aesthetic. Key tokens:

```css
--paper:   #F4F1EA;    /* page background */
--card:    #FDFCF7;    /* card/input background */
--ink:     #1C1C1A;    /* primary text, borders */
--orange:  #C84315;    /* accent, CTAs, International Orange */
--green:   #4A6741;    /* success, Could Have tier */
--muted:   #8C8878;    /* secondary text, labels */
--rule:    #D4CEBC;    /* borders, dividers */
--warn:    #D4380D;    /* warnings, time expired */
```

Fonts: Libre Baskerville (headings), Barlow Condensed (UI, labels, body), IBM Plex Mono (data, inputs, counters). All loaded from Google Fonts in `index.html`.

Zero border-radius everywhere. No rounded corners.

### Technical Constraints

- No TypeScript. Plain JSX.
- No additional npm dependencies beyond what's in package.json. No UI component libraries.
- No localStorage in artifacts (Claude.ai restriction), but this runs standalone in Docker so localStorage is fine for session persistence.
- Ollama responses can be slow (10-30 seconds for large prompts on smaller models). Always show a spinner/status indicator. Never leave the user staring at a frozen UI.
- All Ollama calls use `stream: false`. Do not implement streaming.
- The app must work with Podman as well as Docker. No Docker-specific features.

## Development Workflow

1. `npm install`
2. Start Ollama locally: `ollama serve` (or it's already running)
3. `npm run dev` — Vite dev server with hot reload, proxy to localhost:11434
4. Edit files, test in browser at localhost:5173
5. When ready: `npm run build && node server.js` to test production mode
6. `docker compose up -d --build` to test containerized

## Implementation Order

Build in this order to keep the app functional at every step:

1. **Refactor App.jsx** — Split into stage files under `src/stages/`. Extract shared components. Get the existing 4 stages working with the new file structure before adding anything.

2. **Enhance Phase 2 (Requirements)** — Add requirement types, NFR subcategories, acceptance criteria field, dependency tagging, quality indicators. Update Ollama prompt.

3. **Build Phase 4 (Stories)** — New stage. Requirement → story mapping, manual story creation with the three-field template, AI story generation, INVEST check, story splitting.

4. **Enhance Phase 3 (MoSCoW)** — Dependency warnings, Must Have cap indicator, category filter.

5. **Enhance Phase 5 (Backlog)** — Full backlog view, sprint planning buckets, release forecast, CSV and markdown export, session save/load.

6. **Polish** — Keyboard shortcuts across all phases, consistent loading states, error handling for Ollama failures, responsive layout tweaks.

## Code Style

- Functional components only. No class components.
- useState/useEffect for state management. No Redux, no Context API unless state drilling becomes genuinely painful (3+ levels deep).
- CSS lives in `src/index.css` using class names. No CSS-in-JS, no Tailwind, no styled-components. Inline styles only for truly dynamic values (colors that change based on state).
- Keep components under 300 lines. If a component exceeds that, extract sub-components.
- No comments explaining what code does. Comments only for why (non-obvious decisions).


# SOURCE: /Users/samfakhreddine/repos/gitrdunhq/baGuy/.claude/worktrees/agent-a6a42898f845d6a59/ba-pipeline/CLAUDE.md

3. **AI extraction stays** — the Ollama call that pulls candidate items from discovery notes. This is the starting point, not the end.

4. **Requirement types** — Each item needs a type field:
   - `functional` — what the system does (observable behavior)
   - `nfr` — quality attribute (performance, security, accessibility, etc.)
   - `constraint` — non-negotiable boundary (tech stack, compliance, budget, timeline)

5. **NFR subcategories** — When type is `nfr`, show a subcategory picker: performance, availability, scalability, security, accessibility, observability, maintainability.

6. **Acceptance criteria** — Each requirement should have an optional acceptance criteria field. Free text. This gets carried forward into stories.

7. **EARS requirement syntax** — JTBD captures the job and context; EARS turns that context into unambiguous requirements. Requirements should be expressible with Easy Approach to Requirements Syntax patterns:
   - Ubiquitous: `The [system] shall [action].`
   - Event-driven: `When [event], the [system] shall [action].`
   - State-driven: `While [state], the [system] shall [action].`
   - Unwanted behavior: `If [condition], then the [system] shall [action].`
   - Optional feature: `Where [feature], the [system] shall [action].`
   - Combined context: `While [state], when [event], the [system] shall [action].`

   Store the selected EARS pattern and structured context fields. This makes missing triggers, states, failure modes, and feature applicability visible during Phase 2 and feeds directly into Given/When/Then acceptance criteria during Phase 4.

8. **Dependency tagging** — Allow marking dependencies between requirements. Simple: a "depends on" dropdown that references other requirements by title.

9. **Requirement quality indicators** — Visual hints for incomplete requirements:
   - Missing acceptance criteria → amber dot
   - Category is still "decision" (not yet classified as functional/nfr/constraint) → amber dot
   - No owner → grey dot
   - Has acceptance criteria + type + owner → green dot

10. **Update the Ollama prompt** to also extract NFRs and constraints, not just functional items. The current prompt only asks for "actionable items." Expand it to explicitly request domain entities, system properties, non-functional requirements, constraints, and a proposed EARS pattern for each extracted item.

### Phase 3: MoSCoW (exists — minor enhancement)

**Current state:** Works well. Timer, keyboard shortcuts, queue sidebar.

**Enhancements needed:**

1. **Dependency warnings** — If item B depends on item A, and A is assigned Could Have or Won't Have while B is Must Have or Should Have, show a visual warning: "This item depends on [A] which is currently [Won't Have]."

2. **Must Have cap** — Show a running count: "X of Y items are Must Have (Z%)". If Must Have exceeds 60% of total items, show a warning banner: "More than 60% Must Have — prioritization may not be effective."

3. **Category filter in queue** — Let the facilitator filter the queue sidebar by requirement type (functional, nfr, constraint) to work through categories in blocks if desired.

4. **Decision tracker with aging** — Every MoSCoW decision already captures owner and deadline. Add a dashboard view that makes follow-up operational:
   - Due this week
   - Overdue decisions, shown in red
   - Stalled decisions with no owner assigned

   This should answer "what's overdue?" without requiring a full export review.

### Phase 4: Story Decomposition (NEW — build from scratch)

This is the biggest new phase. It takes prioritized requirements (Must Have and Should Have from MoSCoW) and decomposes them into user stories.

**Layout:** Similar to MoSCoW — main panel + sidebar. But instead of one-at-a-time facilitation, this is a workspace where you can see all requirements and their child stories.

**Core features:**

1. **Requirement → Story mapping** — Left panel shows the prioritized requirements (Must Have first, then Should Have). Clicking a requirement opens it and shows its child stories below.

2. **Story creation** — For each requirement, the user can:
   - Manually add stories using the "As a [persona], I want [capability], so that [outcome]" template. Provide three input fields, not a single text box.
   - Use Ollama to auto-generate story suggestions from the requirement text + acceptance criteria. Same model switcher as Phase 2. The user reviews, edits, accepts, or discards each suggestion.

3. **Story fields:**
   - `persona` — who (text input)
   - `capability` — what they want (text input)
   - `outcome` — so that / why (text input)
   - `acceptance_criteria` — list of criteria. Each criterion is a text string. Add/remove. Carry forward any acceptance criteria from the parent requirement as a starting point.
   - `size` — estimate: S, M, L, XL (button toggle)
   - `type` — `user_story`, `technical`, `spike`
   - `status` — `draft`, `ready`, `needs_split`

4. **INVEST check** — When a story is marked "ready", run a lightweight validation:
   - Has persona, capability, and outcome filled in? (Valuable, Negotiable)
   - Has at least one acceptance criterion? (Testable)
   - Size is S or M? (Small — if L or XL, suggest splitting)
   - Show pass/fail indicators, not blocking

5. **AI story generation prompt** — When the user clicks "Suggest Stories" for a requirement, send to Ollama:
   - The requirement title, description, acceptance criteria, and type
   - Ask for 3-5 user stories in JSON format
   - Each with persona, capability, outcome, and 2-3 acceptance criteria
   - Parse and display as editable drafts

6. **Epic grouping** — Each requirement effectively becomes an epic. The stories under it are the deliverable chunks. Show a count: "3 stories, 2 ready, 1 draft."

7. **Story splitting helper** — For stories sized L or XL, offer a "Split" button that sends the story to Ollama with a prompt asking for 2-3 smaller stories that decompose the original. Same review/edit/accept flow.

### Phase 5: Backlog & Export (exists as "Export" — enhance significantly)

**Current state:** Shows MoSCoW 2x2 grid and plain text export.

**Enhancements needed:**

1. **Full backlog view** — Show all stories grouped by epic (requirement), ordered by MoSCoW tier (Must Have first). Each story shows its status, size, and acceptance criteria count.

2. **Sprint planning helper** — Let the user define sprint capacity (e.g., "we can do 8-10 stories per sprint" or use a point total). Then drag or assign stories to Sprint 1, Sprint 2, etc. Simple — just buckets with a running count. Not a full sprint board.

3. **Release forecast** — Based on sprint capacity and total story count, show: "At current capacity, Must Haves require ~X sprints. Must + Should = ~Y sprints."

4. **Export formats:**
   - **Markdown** — Full document: discovery summary → requirements → MoSCoW decisions → stories with acceptance criteria → sprint plan
   - **CSV** — Flat table of stories: epic, title (as a/i want/so that combined), acceptance criteria, size, type, sprint assignment, MoSCoW tier. For Jira import.
   - **Clipboard** — Current plain text export, enhanced with story details

5. **Session save/load** — Use localStorage to save the full session state. List saved sessions on the setup page. Load a previous session to continue work. This is critical — a pipeline session can span multiple sittings.

6. **Auto-generated stakeholder status brief** — Add a one-button brief generator for Slack/email updates. This is not the full export. It should produce a concise leadership-ready summary:
   - What was decided
   - What's blocked
   - What's next
   - Who owns what

   Ollama can draft the text from session state, then the facilitator edits and copies it.

7. **Traceability chain** — Make the path from problem → requirement → MoSCoW decision → story → acceptance criteria clickable end-to-end. A story should expose the requirement behind it, the discovery note or problem statement that produced it, and the prioritization decision that justified it. This keeps sprint work defensible when questioned later.

8. **ADR generation for technical decisions** — For MoSCoW items that are technical decisions, offer a lightweight Architecture Decision Record draft:
   - Context
   - Decision
   - Consequences
   - Status

   Ollama can draft the ADR from the discovery notes plus the MoSCoW decision; the user edits and exports markdown.

### Cross-Phase Governance Enhancements

1. **Assumption lifecycle** — Discovery assumptions should become first-class objects instead of remaining free text. Track each assumption through `unvalidated`, `testing`, `validated`, and `invalidated`.

2. **Assumption impact flags** — Requirements should be able to depend on assumptions. If an assumption is invalidated, every dependent requirement should show a re-evaluation flag, especially Must Have items.

3. **Decision and assumption dashboard** — Add an outcome-driving dashboard that combines overdue decisions, ownerless decisions, active assumption tests, invalidated assumptions, and requirements needing re-evaluation.

## Architecture

### File Structure

```
ba-pipeline/
├── CLAUDE.md              # This file
├── Dockerfile
├── docker-compose.yml
├── server.js              # Express: static serve + typed Ollama API gateway
├── server/
│   └── rag/                    # JTBD RAG retrieval engine
│       ├── budget.js           # Token budget management
│       ├── loadChunks.js       # JSONL chunk loader
│       ├── retrieve.js         # TF-IDF retriever with chapter bias
│       ├── router.js           # Express routes (GET /chunks, POST /retrieve)
│       └── tfidf.js            # TF-IDF index builder and query
├── vite.config.js
├── package.json
├── index.html
└── src/
    ├── main.jsx
    ├── App.jsx             # Top-level state, stage routing, sidebar
    ├── index.css           # Global styles, design tokens
    ├── stages/
    │   ├── Discovery.jsx       # Phase 1
    │   ├── Requirements.jsx    # Phase 2 (renamed from extraction)
    │   ├── Moscow.jsx          # Phase 3
    │   └── Export.jsx          # Phase 4 artifacts and governance
    ├── components/
    │   ├── DesiredOutcomes.jsx     # Ulwick outcome capture (4-field syntax)
    │   ├── GovernanceDashboard.jsx
    │   ├── JobMapSection.jsx       # Universal Job Map 8-step accordion
    │   ├── JobStatementInput.jsx   # When/I want/So I can structured input
    │   ├── OpportunityLandscape.jsx # Opportunity score table for Export
    │   ├── SwotGrid.jsx            # SWOT 2x2 card grid with AI generation
    │   ├── SystemPropertiesPanel.jsx
    │   └── TowsMatrix.jsx         # TOWS strategic combination panel
    ├── lib/
    │   ├── constants.js        # Stages, sections, tiers, job map steps, SWOT quadrants
    │   ├── hints.js            # Static hints + job map hints + analysis prompt builder
    │   ├── opportunityScore.js # Pure Opportunity Algorithm function
    │   └── ragConfig.js        # RAG retrieval configuration constants
    ├── contracts/              # Runtime validation and fail-loud guards
    ├── generators/             # Markdown/status/ADR export builders
    ├── ollama/                 # Ollama request and response contracts
    ├── prompts/                # Externalized Handlebars prompt catalog
    ├── selectors/              # Derived governance/traceability/session state
    ├── state/                  # Initial app/session defaults
    └── templates/              # Externalized Handlebars export templates
```

Stage components receive props from App.jsx and validate incoming boundaries. App.jsx owns shared state and stage navigation; contracts, generators, prompts, and selectors stay outside JSX.

### Engineering Principles

- **SOLID** — Keep stage components focused, state ownership explicit, and shared services narrow.
- **DRY** — Consolidate duplicated behavior, prompts, parsing, and validation rules. Do not abstract one-off JSX just to reduce lines.
- **KISS** — Prefer plain React state, simple data shapes, and direct functions until complexity proves a stronger pattern is needed.
- **Elegant** — Code should read plainly, with clear names and small functions. Avoid clever control flow or hidden coupling.
- **Contracts at every boundary** — Validate component props, stage state, Ollama request/response JSON, Express API inputs, export formats, and generated ADR/status-brief payloads. Every tier crossing is API-style: validate incoming payloads and shape outgoing payloads explicitly. Boundary failures should be explicit, not silently patched with defaults.
- **Fail loud, fail proud** — Missing required data, malformed model output, invalid state transitions, and broken invariants should produce visible, actionable failures. Do not continue with placeholder objects or quiet empty results.

### State Shape

All session state lives in App.jsx. Derived artifacts are built through selectors/generators only when needed.

```javascript
{
  stage: "discovery" | "extraction" | "moscow" | "export",
  section: "setup" | "problem" | "...",
  session: { 
    name, facilitator, date, participants, status,
    jobStatement: { situation, motivation, outcome },  // JTBD structured input
    desiredOutcomes: [{ id, direction, measure, object, clarifier }],  // Ulwick ODI outcomes
  },
  notes: { problem: "", current: "", future: "", ..., jobMap: {} },  // jobMap: Universal Job Map steps
  swotItems: { strengths: [], weaknesses: [], opportunities: [], threats: [] },  // SWOT analysis
  items: [{ id, title, desc, category, owner, assumptionStatus, dependsOnAssumptions }],
  systemPropertyMatrix: [{ name, safety, liveness, invariant, bound }],
  model: "qwen3:14b",
  decisions: { [itemId]: { tier, owner, deadline, decision, technical, consequences, importance, satisfaction } },  // importance + satisfaction for Opportunity scoring
  currentDecision: { tier, owner, deadline, decision, technical, consequences }
}
```

### Ollama Integration

All production Ollama calls go through the Express typed API gateway at `/api/ollama/api/chat`.
Prompt text must not live inside React components, fetch calls, or ad hoc string builders.
Add or change prompts under `src/prompts/*.hbs.js`, register them in `src/prompts/catalog.js`,
and render them through `src/prompts/renderPrompt.js` so missing prompt names or context fail loudly.

**Existing prompts:**
- Requirements extraction from discovery notes (Phase 2): `src/prompts/extractItems.hbs.js`
- SWOT generation from discovery notes: `src/prompts/generateSwot.hbs.js`
- JTBD RAG context injection: `src/prompts/jtbdContext.hbs.js`

**Future prompts to add only when the feature exists:**
- Story generation from a requirement
- Story splitting suggestions

#### RAG Integration

The server loads `jtbd_chunks.jsonl` at startup and builds a TF-IDF index for retrieval-augmented generation of JTBD methodology context.

- `GET /api/jtbd/chunks?q=&n=&bias=` retrieves relevant JTBD methodology chunks
- Extraction prompt includes retrieved chunks via `jtbdContext.hbs.js` template
- Hints panel fetches RAG chunks before AI analysis
- Chapter bias: extraction prefers `ch04_odi`, hints prefer `ch02_needs`
- Token budgets: 1500 chars/chunk, 5000 total extraction, 3000 hints
- Graceful degradation: if chunks file missing, app works without RAG

All Ollama request builders must send `stream: false`. JSON-producing prompts must ask for pure JSON output (no markdown fences). Parse with `JSON.parse()` after stripping any accidental fences.

The model is user-selectable. Available models:
```javascript
const MODELS = [
  { id: "gemma4:e4b",  label: "Gemma 4 E4B",  size: "~6 GB",  desc: "Fast. Good for clean notes." },
  { id: "gemma4:26b",  label: "Gemma 4 26B",   size: "~16 GB", desc: "MoE. Better at ambiguous text." },
  { id: "qwen3:14b",   label: "Qwen 3 14B",    size: "~10 GB", desc: "Most reliable JSON output." },
];
```

### Design System

DATUM-adjacent. Do not change the existing aesthetic. Key tokens:

```css
--paper:   #F4F1EA;    /* page background */
--card:    #FDFCF7;    /* card/input background */
--ink:     #1C1C1A;    /* primary text, borders */
--orange:  #C84315;    /* accent, CTAs, International Orange */
--green:   #4A6741;    /* success, Could Have tier */
--muted:   #8C8878;    /* secondary text, labels */
--rule:    #D4CEBC;    /* borders, dividers */
--warn:    #D4380D;    /* warnings, time expired */
```

Fonts: Libre Baskerville (headings), Barlow Condensed (UI, labels, body), IBM Plex Mono (data, inputs, counters). All loaded from Google Fonts in `index.html`.

Zero border-radius everywhere. No rounded corners.

### Technical Constraints

- No TypeScript. Plain JSX.
- No additional npm dependencies beyond what's in package.json. No UI component libraries.
- No localStorage in artifacts (Claude.ai restriction), but this runs standalone in Docker so localStorage is fine for session persistence.
- Ollama responses can be slow (10-30 seconds for large prompts on smaller models). Always show a spinner/status indicator. Never leave the user staring at a frozen UI.
- All Ollama calls use `stream: false`. Do not implement streaming.
- The app must work with Podman as well as Docker. No Docker-specific features.

## Development Workflow

1. `npm install`
2. Start Ollama locally: `ollama serve` (or it's already running)
3. `npm run dev` — Vite dev server with hot reload, proxy to localhost:11434
4. Edit files, test in browser at localhost:5173
5. When ready: `npm run build && node server.js` to test production mode
6. `docker compose up -d --build` to test containerized

## Implementation Order

Build in this order to keep the app functional at every step:

1. **Refactor App.jsx** — Split into stage files under `src/stages/`. Extract shared components. Get the existing 4 stages working with the new file structure before adding anything.

2. **Enhance Phase 2 (Requirements)** — Add requirement types, NFR subcategories, acceptance criteria field, dependency tagging, quality indicators. Update Ollama prompt.

3. **Build Phase 4 (Stories)** — New stage. Requirement → story mapping, manual story creation with the three-field template, AI story generation, INVEST check, story splitting.

4. **Enhance Phase 3 (MoSCoW)** — Dependency warnings, Must Have cap indicator, category filter.

5. **Enhance Phase 5 (Backlog)** — Full backlog view, sprint planning buckets, release forecast, CSV and markdown export, session save/load.

6. **Polish** — Keyboard shortcuts across all phases, consistent loading states, error handling for Ollama failures, responsive layout tweaks.

## Code Style

- Functional components only. No class components.
- useState/useEffect for state management. No Redux, no Context API unless state drilling becomes genuinely painful (3+ levels deep).
- CSS lives in `src/index.css` using class names. No CSS-in-JS, no Tailwind, no styled-components. Inline styles only for truly dynamic values (colors that change based on state).
- Keep components under 300 lines. If a component exceeds that, extract sub-components.
- No comments explaining what code does. Comments only for why (non-obvious decisions).


# SOURCE: /Users/samfakhreddine/repos/ai-code-tools/ee-skills/AGENTS.md

# AGENTS.md

Guidance for AI coding agents working in this repository.

## Commands

```bash
# Install all skills locally (run after git pull too)
bash scripts/install.sh
bash scripts/install.sh ee-mermaid          # install one skill only
bash scripts/install.sh --dry-run           # preview without installing

# Validate all SKILL.md frontmatter
uv run --with pyyaml python scripts/validate.py

# Regenerate README skills table from frontmatter
uv run --with pyyaml python scripts/update_readme.py

# List test cases for a skill
uv run --with pyyaml python scripts/run_skill_tests.py --skill <skillname>
```

All Python scripts must use `uv run` — never bare `python` or `python3`.

## Architecture

Skills live under `skills/<name>/`. Each skill is self-contained:

```
skills/ee-mermaid/
├── SKILL.md          ← frontmatter (name, description, license) + instructions
├── references/       ← loaded on-demand when the skill fires
├── assets/           ← static templates, icons, or other bundled files
├── scripts/          ← utilities the skill instructs the agent to call
└── evals/evals.json  ← test prompts with expected outputs
```

`_template/` is the scaffold — copy it to start a new skill.

### How skills reach agents

`install.sh` syncs each `skills/<name>/` to `~/.ee/<name>/` via rsync, then
symlinks `~/.ee/<name>` into the agent's skills directory. The default target
is `~/.claude/skills/` (Claude Code); set `SKILLS_PATH` to override for other
tools. The `~/.ee/` intermediary allows multiple repo clones without
collisions.

### SKILL.md frontmatter is the primary trigger

The `description:` field is what an agent reads to decide whether to use a
skill. It must describe what users actually say, not what the tool does.
Vague or jargon-heavy descriptions cause undertriggering. Minimum 80 chars.
Required fields: `name`, `description`, `license`.

### Adding a skill

1. Branch `add/ee-<skillname>`, copy `skills/_template/`, fill `SKILL.md`
2. `uv run --with pyyaml python scripts/validate.py` must pass before PR
3. Run `uv run --with pyyaml python scripts/update_readme.py` to update the table
4. Add yourself to `CODEOWNERS` for your skill directory
5. Squash merge — one commit per PR

### Versioning and releases

Releases are automated by Release Please. Use conventional commit prefixes on `main`:

| Prefix | Version bump |
|--------|-------------|
| `feat:` | minor |
| `fix:` | patch |
| `feat!:` or `BREAKING CHANGE:` | major |
| `chore:` `docs:` `ci:` `refactor:` | no bump |

Release Please opens a release PR when it detects bumpable commits. Merging
that PR tags the release and updates `CHANGELOG.md` and `pyproject.toml`
automatically.

### CI

- `validate.yml` — **blocking**: fails PR if any `SKILL.md` has bad frontmatter or README table is stale
- `eval.yml` — **advisory**: posts test case summary as PR step summary
- `release-please.yml` — opens release PRs on every push to `main`
- `sync-skill-creator.yml` — weekly PR to pull upstream skill-creator updates

<!-- rtk-instructions v2 -->
# RTK (Rust Token Killer) - Token-Optimized Commands

## Golden Rule

**Always prefix commands with `rtk`**. If RTK has a dedicated filter, it uses it. If not, it passes through unchanged. This means RTK is always safe to use.

**Important**: Even in command chains with `&&`, use `rtk`:
```bash
# ❌ Wrong
git add . && git commit -m "msg" && git push

# ✅ Correct
rtk git add . && rtk git commit -m "msg" && rtk git push
```

## RTK Commands by Workflow

### Build & Compile (80-90% savings)
```bash
rtk cargo build         # Cargo build output
rtk cargo check         # Cargo check output
rtk cargo clippy        # Clippy warnings grouped by file (80%)
rtk tsc                 # TypeScript errors grouped by file/code (83%)
rtk lint                # ESLint/Biome violations grouped (84%)
rtk prettier --check    # Files needing format only (70%)
rtk next build          # Next.js build with route metrics (87%)
```

### Test (90-99% savings)
```bash
rtk cargo test          # Cargo test failures only (90%)
rtk vitest run          # Vitest failures only (99.5%)
rtk playwright test     # Playwright failures only (94%)
rtk test <cmd>          # Generic test wrapper - failures only
```

### Git (59-80% savings)
```bash
rtk git status          # Compact status
rtk git log             # Compact log (works with all git flags)
rtk git diff            # Compact diff (80%)
rtk git show            # Compact show (80%)
rtk git add             # Ultra-compact confirmations (59%)
rtk git commit          # Ultra-compact confirmations (59%)
rtk git push            # Ultra-compact confirmations
rtk git pull            # Ultra-compact confirmations
rtk git branch          # Compact branch list
rtk git fetch           # Compact fetch
rtk git stash           # Compact stash
rtk git worktree        # Compact worktree
```

Note: Git passthrough works for ALL subcommands, even those not explicitly listed.

### GitHub (26-87% savings)
```bash
rtk gh pr view <num>    # Compact PR view (87%)
rtk gh pr checks        # Compact PR checks (79%)
rtk gh run list         # Compact workflow runs (82%)
rtk gh issue list       # Compact issue list (80%)
rtk gh api              # Compact API responses (26%)
```

### JavaScript/TypeScript Tooling (70-90% savings)
```bash
rtk pnpm list           # Compact dependency tree (70%)
rtk pnpm outdated       # Compact outdated packages (80%)
rtk pnpm install        # Compact install output (90%)
rtk npm run <script>    # Compact npm script output
rtk npx <cmd>           # Compact npx command output
rtk prisma              # Prisma without ASCII art (88%)
```

### Files & Search (60-75% savings)
```bash
rtk ls <path>           # Tree format, compact (65%)
rtk read <file>         # Code reading with filtering (60%)
rtk grep <pattern>      # Search grouped by file (75%)
rtk find <pattern>      # Find grouped by directory (70%)
```

### Analysis & Debug (70-90% savings)
```bash
rtk err <cmd>           # Filter errors only from any command
rtk log <file>          # Deduplicated logs with counts
rtk json <file>         # JSON structure without values
rtk deps                # Dependency overview
rtk env                 # Environment variables compact
rtk summary <cmd>       # Smart summary of command output
rtk diff                # Ultra-compact diffs
```

### Infrastructure (85% savings)
```bash
rtk docker ps           # Compact container list
rtk docker images       # Compact image list
rtk docker logs <c>     # Deduplicated logs
rtk kubectl get         # Compact resource list
rtk kubectl logs        # Deduplicated pod logs
```

### Network (65-70% savings)
```bash
rtk curl <url>          # Compact HTTP responses (70%)
rtk wget <url>          # Compact download output (65%)
```

### Meta Commands
```bash
rtk gain                # View token savings statistics
rtk gain --history      # View command history with savings
rtk discover            # Analyze Claude Code sessions for missed RTK usage
rtk proxy <cmd>         # Run command without filtering (for debugging)
rtk init                # Add RTK instructions to CLAUDE.md
rtk init --global       # Add RTK to ~/.claude/CLAUDE.md
```

## Token Savings Overview

| Category | Commands | Typical Savings |
|----------|----------|-----------------|
| Tests | vitest, playwright, cargo test | 90-99% |
| Build | next, tsc, lint, prettier | 70-87% |
| Git | status, log, diff, add, commit | 59-80% |
| GitHub | gh pr, gh run, gh issue | 26-87% |
| Package Managers | pnpm, npm, npx | 70-90% |
| Files | ls, read, grep, find | 60-75% |
| Infrastructure | docker, kubectl | 85% |
| Network | curl, wget | 65-70% |

Overall average: **60-90% token reduction** on common development operations.

# SOURCE: /Users/samfakhreddine/repos/local-drafts/investigations/CLAUDE.md

# CLAUDE.md — Investigations

This repository stores completed investigations produced by the investigator pipeline at `../investigator/`. It is read-only from the tool's perspective — all content here is generated by agents and scripts, never hand-authored.

## Repository Purpose

Pure research data. No code, no implementations, no solutions. Findings and insights only.

## Taxonomy

Investigations are organized as:

```
<BroadTopic>/<SubTopic>/<Investigation>/
```

All folder names use **PascalCase** — no hyphens, underscores, or spaces.

### Current top-level topics

| Topic | Description |
|-------|-------------|
| `AWS` | All Amazon Web Services investigations — identity, SSM, EventBridge, security, IaC, hybrid identity |
| `Finance` | Market events, financial analysis, trading patterns |
| `ClientResearch` | Research on specific companies or clients |
| `Hardware` | Device comparisons, hardware evaluations |

New top-level topics may be created freely when no existing topic fits. Use PascalCase; aim for 1–2 words that describe the domain clearly (e.g. `Compliance`, `AI`, `Networking`).

### Sub-topic guidance

Within each broad topic, use a sub-topic that narrows the domain. Examples:

```
AWS/
  Identity/        ← IAM, Identity Center, Entra, ABAC, SCIM
  SSM/             ← Session Manager, Run As, Just-in-Time access
  EventBridge/     ← Rules, patterns, native events
  Security/        ← Security Hub, Defender, threat detection
  HybridIdentity/  ← SSSD, on-prem/cloud identity bridging
  InfrastructureAsCode/ ← CDK, Pulumi, Terraform, CloudFormation
Finance/
  MarketEvents/    ← Short squeezes, earnings, macro events
ClientResearch/
  <ClientName>/    ← One sub-folder per client, named after them
Hardware/
  MacBookAir/
  ThinkPad/
```

When a new sub-topic is needed, name it descriptively in PascalCase.

## Sub-Investigations

When an investigation has multiple related sub-topics, sub-investigation folders nest **inside** the root investigation folder:

```
AWS/Identity/EntraAbac/EntraAbacClaimsMechanisms/   ← rollup
  investigation.json
  investigation.md
  validation_report.md
  SamlClaimsVsScim/                                 ← sub-investigation
    investigation.json
    ...
  PrincipalTagIamConditions/                        ← sub-investigation
    investigation.json
    ...
```

The root folder's `investigation.json` is the **rollup** — synthesized from all sub-investigation JSONs, never hand-authored.

## Files in Each Investigation Folder

| File | Audience | Required |
|------|----------|---------|
| `investigation.md` | Engineers | Always |
| `investigation.json` | Agents | Always (authoritative source) |
| `validation_report.md` | All | Always |
| `brief_leadership.md` | Engineering Leadership | Technical investigations only |
| `brief_po.md` | Product Owners / PMs / EMs | Technical investigations only |
| `glossary.md` | All | When concepts are populated |

All markdown files except `validation_report.md` are generated by:

```
python3 /Users/samfakhreddine/repos/workspace/investigator/scripts/json_to_md.py <investigation_dir>
```

Never hand-edit generated markdown. All corrections go into `investigation.json` and are regenerated by script.

## Git Workflow

After all investigations in a session are complete and validated:

```bash
git add <BroadTopic>/<SubTopic>/<PascalCaseName>/
git commit -m "investigation: <PascalCaseFolderName> — <one-line summary of key finding>"
git push
```

Never commit partial or unvalidated investigations.


# SOURCE: /Users/samfakhreddine/repos/local-drafts/bumblingdon/CLAUDE.md

# Bumblingdon

Presidential simulation CLI game. Player is a party nominee who won their primary, 6 months before the general election. Start date is the system clock — no hardcoded dates.

## Tech Stack

- TypeScript (ESM, strict mode)
- Ink 6.8.0 (React 19 for terminal UI)
- Ollama 0.6.3 (local LLM, llama3.2)
- better-sqlite3 (SQLite, WAL mode)
- Zod 4.3.6 (schema validation)
- Vitest (testing)

## Architecture

Three-layer: `src/logic/` (game rules, state machine, LLM) → `src/data/` (SQLite repos) → `src/presentation/` (Ink components, React hooks).

- **GameController** orchestrates the game loop via dependency injection (repos, config, ScenarioGenerator)
- **GameStateMachine** enforces phase transitions: initializing → generating → active_briefing ↔ active_scenario ↔ resolving → session_complete
- **ScenarioGenerator** tries LLM first, falls back to hardcoded scenarios
- **GameStateRepository** handles saves (auto-save, manual, emergency file fallback)
- **CalendarState** is immutable; dates derived from `day` via `getDateForDay()`

## Key Conventions

- All imports use `.js` extensions
- No linter/formatter configured
- Tests use Vitest (`describe`/`it`/`expect`)
- `calendarDate` was removed from `GameState` — derive dates from `day` using `getDateForDay()` from `calendar.ts`
- `GameController` is never instantiated directly in production code (only type-imported by presentation layer)

## API Contracts

`docs/api-contracts.md` is the canonical reference for all public exports, interfaces, and function signatures.

**Keep it in sync.** Any time you change an exported interface, type, function signature, class constructor, or component props — update `docs/api-contracts.md` in the same commit. This includes:
- Adding/removing/renaming fields on exported interfaces or types
- Changing function parameter types or return types
- Adding/removing exported functions or classes
- Changing constructor dependencies

Do not treat this as optional documentation — it is the contract other code depends on.

## Reflexion Memory

After every task completion (implement, refactor, bug fix, review), record what you learned in WFC reflexion memory. This is mandatory, not optional.

```bash
wfc helpers memory-search <keywords>   # check if a learning already exists
wfc memory recall <query>              # semantic recall before starting work
```

**What to record:**
- Non-obvious gotchas discovered during implementation (e.g., "Zod strips unknown keys silently — no migration needed when removing schema fields")
- Merge/conflict patterns (e.g., "multiple tasks editing the same file's import block cause worktree merge conflicts — merge in topological order")
- Architectural constraints learned the hard way (e.g., "GameController has no async private method precedent — adding one cascades to all callers")
- Design decisions and their rationale (e.g., "start date uses system clock, not hardcoded — game premise is 6 months before election from today")

**When to recall:** Before starting any implementation or refactor, run `wfc memory recall` with relevant keywords to check for prior learnings.

## Game Design Skill

Use `/bumblingdon-game-design` when designing, implementing, or debugging any game mechanic. It has domain knowledge for: alignment systems, approval ratings, event pools, consequence chains, pacing governors, advisor trust, faction dynamics, LLM content generation, campaign promises, endgame scoring, and election simulation. Use it before making game balance decisions.

## Commands

```bash
npx vitest run              # run all tests
./node_modules/.bin/tsc --noEmit  # type check
```

# CLAUDE.md - mcp-arr

MCP server for the *arr media management suite (Sonarr, Radarr, Lidarr, Readarr, Prowlarr).

## Tech Stack

- **Language:** TypeScript
- **Runtime:** Node.js (ES modules)
- **Protocol:** Model Context Protocol (MCP)
- **Build:** TypeScript compiler (tsc)

## Architecture

```
src/
├── index.ts          # Server entry point, tool registration
├── tools/            # Tool implementations by service
│   ├── sonarr.ts     # TV show management
│   ├── radarr.ts     # Movie management
│   ├── lidarr.ts     # Music management
│   ├── readarr.ts    # Book management
│   └── prowlarr.ts   # Indexer management
└── types.ts          # Shared TypeScript types
```

## Development Commands

```bash
# Build
npm run build

# Watch mode
npm run watch

# Test locally (requires env vars)
node dist/index.js
```

## Environment Variables

| Variable | Required | Description |
|----------|----------|-------------|
| SONARR_URL | For Sonarr | Base URL (e.g., http://localhost:8989) |
| SONARR_API_KEY | For Sonarr | API key from Sonarr settings |
| RADARR_URL | For Radarr | Base URL |
| RADARR_API_KEY | For Radarr | API key |
| LIDARR_URL | For Lidarr | Base URL |
| LIDARR_API_KEY | For Lidarr | API key |
| READARR_URL | For Readarr | Base URL |
| READARR_API_KEY | For Readarr | API key |
| PROWLARR_URL | For Prowlarr | Base URL |
| PROWLARR_API_KEY | For Prowlarr | API key |

## Constraints

```yaml
rules:
  - id: no-hardcoded-urls
    description: Never hardcode service URLs or API keys
    check: All service access via environment variables

  - id: consistent-tool-naming
    description: Tool names follow pattern {service}_{action}
    examples:
      - sonarr_get_series
      - radarr_search
      - lidarr_get_albums

  - id: error-handling
    description: All API calls must handle errors gracefully
    requirements:
      - Check for missing env vars before API call
      - Return meaningful error messages
      - Don't expose raw API errors to users

  - id: trash-guides-integration
    description: TRaSH Guides tools use embedded guide data
    note: Guide data fetched from trash-guides.info at runtime
```

## Common Tasks

### Adding a New Tool

1. Add tool definition in appropriate `src/tools/{service}.ts`
2. Register in `src/index.ts` tool list
3. Update README.md "Available Tools" section
4. Update CHANGELOG.md

### Testing Changes

```bash
# Build first
npm run build

# Test with timeout (needs env vars set)
timeout 10 node dist/index.js
```

### Publishing

1. Update CHANGELOG.md
2. `npm version patch|minor|major`
3. `git push && git push --tags`
4. `npm publish`

## API Patterns

All *arr services follow similar REST patterns:
- GET `/api/v3/{resource}` - List all
- GET `/api/v3/{resource}/{id}` - Get one
- POST `/api/v3/{resource}` - Create
- PUT `/api/v3/{resource}/{id}` - Update
- DELETE `/api/v3/{resource}/{id}` - Delete
- POST `/api/v3/command` - Trigger actions (search, refresh, etc.)

# Modernization Agent Workspace

## Mission
Build a reusable modernization skill system that teams can adopt without inheriting maintainer-only workflow noise.

## Boundary
- The product surface lives under `skills/`.
- The maintainer dogfood lane lives under `dogfood/`.
- Do not make the modernization skill depend on dogfood logs, sync mechanics, or maintainer runbooks.

## Canonical Product Artifacts
- `README.md`
- `GETSTARTED.md`
- `ROADMAP.md`
- `docs/architecture/skill-boundaries.md`
- `skills/app-modernization-pro/SKILL.md`
- `skills/app-modernization-agentic-team/SKILL.md`
- `skills/dogfood-workflow/SKILL.md`
- `skills/dogfood-workflow/scripts/install_dogfood_skill.py`
- `skills/app-modernization-pro/scripts/scaffold_modernization_pack.py`
- `skills/app-modernization-pro/examples/`
- `tests/test_scaffold_modernization_pack.py`
- `scripts/check_handoff_integrity.py`

## Maintainer Lane
- Dogfood process, logs, release policy, and operational runbooks are isolated under `dogfood/`.
- If the task is about log sync, release readiness, collision recovery, or maintainer workflow, switch to `dogfood/AGENTS.md`.

## Operating Contract
1. Do not restart from scratch unless explicitly told.
2. Keep modernization-facing docs and skill behavior independent from dogfood implementation details.
3. Stay inside this repo; do not use this workspace to mutate app repos.
4. When changing architecture or workflow boundaries, record the decision in `docs/adr/`.
5. Leave the repo in a better handoff state than you found it.

## Handoff Quickstart
1. Read `README.md`.
2. Read `GETSTARTED.md`.
3. Read `ROADMAP.md`.
4. Read both skill `SKILL.md` files.
5. If the task is maintainer/dogfood work, stop here and continue from `dogfood/AGENTS.md`.

## Definition of Done
- Skill or product-facing doc change implemented.
- Validation run and recorded.
- ADR impact handled or marked N/A.
- Next LLM can continue without rereading chat history.

# Dogfood Lane

## Mission
Harden the modernization skill workspace while keeping maintainer-only process isolated from the product skill surface.

## Scope
- Dogfood logs and local copies under `dogfood/logs/`
- Sync and reconciliation tooling under `dogfood/scripts/`
- Maintainer runbooks, release policy, and deep roadmap under `dogfood/docs/`

## Canonical Artifacts
- `dogfood/AGENTS.md`
- `dogfood/GETSTARTED.md`
- `dogfood/ROADMAP.md`
- `dogfood/logs/dogfoodlog.jsonl`
- `dogfood/logs/dogfoodlog.md`
- `dogfood/scripts/dogfoodlog_jsonl.py`
- `dogfood/scripts/dogfood_sync.py`
- `dogfood/docs/roadmaps/2026-04-skill-workspace-roadmap.md`
- `dogfood/docs/runbooks/dogfood-collision-recovery.md`
- `dogfood/docs/release/skill-pack-versioning.md`
- `dogfood/docs/release/skill-pack-release.template.json`
- `dogfood/docs/packaging/skill-distribution-guide.md`

## Operating Contract
1. Keep dogfood mechanics out of the modernization skill surface.
2. Treat `dogfood/logs/dogfoodlog.jsonl` as canonical read-mostly history.
3. Each agent writes only to its own local log copy; canonical writes go through `dogfood/scripts/dogfood_sync.py`.
4. Reassess `dogfood/ROADMAP.md` from fresh dogfood evidence during active sessions.
5. When process or boundary decisions change, update `docs/adr/`.

1. Read `README.md`.
2. Read `AGENTS.md`.
3. Read `dogfood/AGENTS.md`.
4. Read `dogfood/GETSTARTED.md`.
5. Continue from the top open maintainer item.


# SOURCE: /Users/samfakhreddine/repos/local-drafts/gitrdun-blog/CLAUDE.md

# CLAUDE.md

This file provides guidance to Claude Code (claude.ai/code) when working with code in this repository.

## Commands

```bash
npm run dev          # dev server (default port 4321)
npm run dev -- --port 4322 --host 0.0.0.0   # dev on port 4322, network-accessible
npm run build        # production build → dist/
npm run ci           # astro check + build (runs in pre-push hook)
npx playwright test  # full test suite (builds + previews first)
npx playwright test tests/layout.spec.ts --grep "footer"  # single test by name
```

## Deploying to Cloudflare Pages

Always use `--branch main` — without it the deploy goes to a preview URL, not production:

```bash
npm run build && npx wrangler pages deploy --branch main
```

Or use the helper: `bash scripts/deploy.sh` (requires `CLOUDFLARE_API_TOKEN` and `CLOUDFLARE_ACCOUNT_ID` in `.env.local`).

## Architecture

**Astro 5 static site** — all pages are pre-rendered to `dist/`. No server runtime.

### Content

Blog posts live in `src/content/blog/` as `.md` or `.mdx`. Frontmatter schema is enforced in `src/content.config.ts`:

```yaml
title: string
description: string
pubDate: date
audience: "engineer" | "engineering-leader" | "csuite" | "product-owner" | "ai-skeptic" | "general"
tags: string[]
pinned: boolean   # optional — pinned post sorts first on homepage
```

### Audience filter

`src/scripts/audience.ts` defines `AUDIENCE_KEYS` and `AUDIENCE_MAP`. The homepage filter buttons map selector keys (`engineer`, `engineering-leader`, `csuite`, `all`) to sets of audience values. A post is shown when its `audience` field is in the active set.

### Design system

**`src/styles/design-system.css` is the single source of truth** for all tokens, layout geometry, and component styles. Never hardcode values that are already tokens:

| Token | Value | Use |
|---|---|---|
| `--content-wide` | 1400px | nav, masthead, homepage, blog listing |
| `--content-narrow` | 960px | blog posts, about page |
| `--content-pad` | 40px | standard side padding |
| `--content-pad-sm` | 16px | mobile side padding |
| `--unit` | 8px | base spacing unit |

Palette: `--blue #1D3557`, `--red #E63946`, `--yellow #F4A261`, `--black #111111`, `--white #F1FAEE`.

### Playwright tests

Tests run against a built preview (`npm run build && npm run preview`) — not the dev server. `tests/fixtures.ts` blocks Google Fonts requests to keep tests fast and offline-safe.

**`scripts/routes.mjs` is the single source of truth for test routes** — it auto-discovers blog slugs from the filesystem. When adding a new post that contains `.callout` elements, add its path to `POSTS_WITH_CALLOUTS` in that file.

### OG images

`npm run gen-og` generates static OG images using `scripts/gen-og.mjs`. Fonts are cached in `scripts/.og-fonts/` (gitignored).


# SOURCE: /Users/samfakhreddine/repos/local-drafts/costGuy/.worktrees/task-004/AGENTS.md

# AI Agent Collaboration Guide

**Project**: AWS Cost Optimization Scanner  
**Architecture**: Python single-package with plugin-based architecture  
**Agent Framework**: WFC (Workflow Control Framework)

---

## Overview

This project was designed and planned through a multi-agent AI collaboration workflow. This document serves as a guide for future AI agents (or human developers) working on this codebase.

---

## Planning Artifacts

### Core Documents

All planning documents are located in `.wfc/planning/`:

| Document | Purpose | Status |
|----------|---------|--------|
| `.wfc/planning/BA-AWS-COST-OPTIMIZER.md` | Business requirements (MoSCoW, acceptance criteria) | ✅ Complete |
| `.wfc/planning/TASKS.md` | 22 implementation tasks with dependencies | ✅ Complete |
| `.wfc/planning/PROPERTIES.md` | 12 formal properties (safety, liveness, invariants, performance) | ✅ Complete |
| `.wfc/planning/TEST-PLAN.md` | Test strategy (unit, integration, e2e) | ✅ Complete |
| `.wfc/planning/VALIDATE.md` | Architecture validation (7.8/10 → 8.3/10 after Python switch) | ✅ Complete |
| `.wfc/planning/ARCHITECTURE-CHANGE.md` | TypeScript → Python migration rationale | ✅ Complete |
| `.wfc/planning/deepen-log.md` | Research findings from AWS docs and best practices | ✅ Complete |

### Workflow History

1. **Business Analysis** (`wfc-ba`) - Gathered requirements, defined MoSCoW priorities
2. **Planning** (`wfc-plan`) - Generated TASKS.md, PROPERTIES.md, TEST-PLAN.md
3. **Research** (`wfc-deepen`) - Added 33 annotations from AWS docs and industry patterns
4. **Validation** (`wfc-validate`) - Evaluated architecture, scored 7.8/10
5. **Architecture Change** - Switched TypeScript → Python based on validation findings
6. **Ready for Implementation** - All planning complete, ready for `wfc-implement`

---

## Agent Collaboration Patterns

### Pattern 1: Sequential Planning Pipeline

```
wfc-ba → wfc-plan → wfc-deepen → wfc-validate → wfc-implement
```

**When to use**: New features requiring multi-file changes across services.

**Example**: This project followed this exact pipeline.

### Pattern 2: Parallel Implementation

```
wfc-implement spawns N subagents (one per task) in parallel git worktrees
```

**When to use**: Tasks with clear dependencies and no conflicts.

**Example**: TASK-010 (CloudTrail), TASK-011 (S3), TASK-012 (KMS) can run in parallel.

### Pattern 3: Review-Driven Iteration

```
wfc-implement → wfc-review → fix issues → wfc-review → merge
```

**When to use**: After implementation, before merging to main.

**Example**: Each task should be reviewed before PR creation.

---

## Task Execution Strategy

### Dependency Graph

The 22 tasks are organized in 5 layers:

1. **Canary** (TASK-001): Validate Python setup
2. **Foundation** (TASK-002 to TASK-009): Models, AWS clients, orchestrator
3. **Scanners** (TASK-010 to TASK-012): CloudTrail, S3, KMS plugins
4. **Integration** (TASK-013 to TASK-016): CLI, output, Docker
5. **Safety Rails** (TASK-017 to TASK-022): Tests, dry-run, confidence scores

### Parallel Execution Groups

**Group 1** (after TASK-001):
- TASK-002 (Finding model)
- TASK-004 (Logger)

**Group 2** (after TASK-008):
- TASK-010 (CloudTrail scanner)
- TASK-011 (S3 scanner)
- TASK-012 (KMS scanner)

**Group 3** (after TASK-013):
- TASK-019 (Dry-run mode)
- TASK-020 (Confidence scores)
- TASK-021 (Per-service rate limiters)
- TASK-022 (Max accounts flag)

---

## Agent Instructions for Implementation

### For `wfc-implement` Orchestrator

**Prerequisites**:
- Git repository initialized ✅
- `.wfc/planning/TASKS.md` exists with 22 parseable tasks ✅
- Clean working directory ✅

**Execution**:
1. Run TASK-001 (canary) first
2. If canary passes, spawn parallel agents for independent tasks
3. Each agent works in isolated git worktree
4. Each agent follows TDD workflow (test → implement → verify)
5. Each agent creates PR targeting `develop` branch

### For Task Implementation Agents

**Context to provide**:
- Task ID and description from `.wfc/planning/TASKS.md`
- Related properties from `.wfc/planning/PROPERTIES.md`
- Test requirements from `.wfc/planning/TEST-PLAN.md`
- Research findings from `.wfc/planning/deepen-log.md`

**Workflow**:
1. Read task acceptance criteria
2. Write tests first (pytest)
3. Implement minimal code to pass tests
4. Verify against formal properties
5. Create PR with task ID in title

### For Review Agents

**Review dimensions**:
1. **Security**: No hardcoded credentials, input validation, read-only operations
2. **Correctness**: Logic matches acceptance criteria, edge cases handled
3. **Performance**: Rate limiting, async/await, memory management
4. **Maintainability**: Clear naming, docstrings, type hints
5. **Reliability**: Error handling, logging, graceful degradation

**Consensus threshold**: 9.5/10 required for merge approval.

---

## Key Design Decisions

### Why Python?

**Original**: TypeScript/Node.js monorepo  
**Changed to**: Python single-package  
**Reason**: Validation findings (`.wfc/planning/VALIDATE.md`) showed:
- Monorepo complexity overkill for MVP (3 scanners)
- boto3 more mature than AWS SDK v3
- Easier for DevOps teams to extend
- Simpler distribution (pip + Docker)

**Impact**: Reduced from 24 tasks to 22, improved validation score from 7.8/10 to 8.3/10.

### Why Plugin Architecture?

**Rationale**:
- 11 services to scan (MVP: 3, future: 8 more)
- Parallel development (3 engineers can work on different scanners)
- Easy to add new services without modifying core

**Implementation**: Python Protocol for type-safe plugin interface.

### Why Formal Properties?

**Rationale**:
- Read-only operations are critical (PROP-001: no write operations)
- Performance SLA is strict (PROP-010: 60-minute scan for 100 accounts)
- Security is non-negotiable (PROP-002: credential security)

**Usage**: Each task links to properties it must satisfy.

---

## Common Pitfalls (from Research)

### CloudTrail Lake (TASK-010)
- ⚠️ **25 TB/month threshold** determines pricing model (one-year vs seven-year)
- ⚠️ Cost is $2.50 per 1M events ingested (uncompressed)
- ⚠️ Recommend advanced event selectors to exclude high-volume data events

### S3 Intelligent-Tiering (TASK-011)
- ⚠️ **128 KB minimum object size** - objects below this always stay in Frequent Access
- ⚠️ Don't recommend for buckets with mostly <128 KB objects
- ⚠️ Access patterns: GetObject resets timer, HeadObject does not

### KMS Optimization (TASK-012)
- ⚠️ **S3 bucket keys** reduce KMS requests by 99% for S3 encryption
- ⚠️ Data key caching (AWS Encryption SDK) reduces API calls
- ⚠️ Cost is $0.03 per 10,000 requests

### Rate Limiting (TASK-007, TASK-021)
- ⚠️ AWS throttles at service-specific limits
- ⚠️ Implement per-service rate limiters (CloudTrail: 10 req/sec, S3/KMS: 100 req/sec)
- ⚠️ Use exponential backoff with jitter for retries

### Credentials (TASK-005)
- ⚠️ STS tokens expire after 1 hour
- ⚠️ Implement refresh logic for scans >45 minutes
- ⚠️ Never log credential values - log only source (profile/role)

---

## Testing Strategy

### Unit Tests (pytest)
- **Location**: `tests/unit/`
- **Coverage target**: 80% line coverage
- **Mocking**: Use `moto` for AWS service mocking
- **Pattern**: Test each model, utility, and plugin in isolation

### Integration Tests (pytest + moto)
- **Location**: `tests/integration/`
- **Coverage**: End-to-end scanner workflows
- **Pattern**: Mock AWS APIs, verify Finding generation

### Example Test Structure

```python
# tests/unit/test_finding.py
def test_finding_valid():
    finding = Finding(
        service="CloudTrail",
        resource_id="arn:aws:cloudtrail:...",
        issue="High-volume events",
        estimated_monthly_savings=12000,
        severity=Severity.HIGH,
        recommendation="Add event selectors",
        documentation_link="https://docs.aws.amazon.com/...",
        remediation_snippet="aws cloudtrail put-event-selectors ..."
    )
    assert finding.severity == Severity.HIGH

# tests/integration/test_cloudtrail_scanner.py
@mock_aws
def test_cloudtrail_scanner_detects_high_volume():
    # Setup moto mocks
    client = boto3.client('cloudtrail', region_name='us-east-1')
    client.create_event_data_store(Name='test-store')
    
    # Run scanner
    scanner = CloudTrailScanner()
    findings = scanner.scan(session, '123456789012', 'us-east-1')
    
    # Verify
    assert len(findings) == 1
    assert findings[0].estimated_monthly_savings == 12000
```

---

## Distribution & Deployment

### Installation Methods

1. **PyPI** (future):
   ```bash
   pip install aws-cost-optimizer
   ```

2. **From source**:
   ```bash
   git clone https://github.com/your-org/aws-cost-optimizer
   cd aws-cost-optimizer
   pip install -e .
   ```

3. **Docker**:
   ```bash
   docker build -t aws-cost-optimizer .
   docker run aws-cost-optimizer scan --accounts 123456789012 --regions us-east-1
   ```

### Usage Examples

```bash
# Scan single account
aws-cost-optimizer scan --profile my-profile --accounts 123456789012 --regions us-east-1

# Scan all accounts in organization
aws-cost-optimizer scan --profile org-master --org-scan --regions us-east-1,us-west-2

# Dry-run mode (no API calls)
aws-cost-optimizer scan --dry-run --accounts 123456789012 --regions us-east-1

# Limit blast radius
aws-cost-optimizer scan --org-scan --max-accounts 10 --regions us-east-1
```
