# SOURCE: /Users/samfakhreddine/repos/local-drafts/costGuy/AGENTS.md

# AI Agent Collaboration Guide

**Project**: AWS Cost Optimization Scanner  
**Architecture**: Python single-package with plugin-based architecture  
**Agent Framework**: WFC (Workflow Control Framework)

---

## Overview

This project was designed and planned through a multi-agent AI collaboration workflow. This document serves as a guide for future AI agents (or human developers) working on this codebase.

---

## Planning Artifacts

### Core Documents

All planning documents are located in `.wfc/planning/`:

| Document | Purpose | Status |
|----------|---------|--------|
| `.wfc/planning/BA-AWS-COST-OPTIMIZER.md` | Business requirements (MoSCoW, acceptance criteria) | ✅ Complete |
| `.wfc/planning/TASKS.md` | 22 implementation tasks with dependencies | ✅ Complete |
| `.wfc/planning/PROPERTIES.md` | 12 formal properties (safety, liveness, invariants, performance) | ✅ Complete |
| `.wfc/planning/TEST-PLAN.md` | Test strategy (unit, integration, e2e) | ✅ Complete |
| `.wfc/planning/VALIDATE.md` | Architecture validation (7.8/10 → 8.3/10 after Python switch) | ✅ Complete |
| `.wfc/planning/ARCHITECTURE-CHANGE.md` | TypeScript → Python migration rationale | ✅ Complete |
| `.wfc/planning/deepen-log.md` | Research findings from AWS docs and best practices | ✅ Complete |

### Workflow History

1. **Business Analysis** (`wfc-ba`) - Gathered requirements, defined MoSCoW priorities
2. **Planning** (`wfc-plan`) - Generated TASKS.md, PROPERTIES.md, TEST-PLAN.md
3. **Research** (`wfc-deepen`) - Added 33 annotations from AWS docs and industry patterns
4. **Validation** (`wfc-validate`) - Evaluated architecture, scored 7.8/10
5. **Architecture Change** - Switched TypeScript → Python based on validation findings
6. **Ready for Implementation** - All planning complete, ready for `wfc-implement`

---

## Agent Collaboration Patterns

### Pattern 1: Sequential Planning Pipeline

```
wfc-ba → wfc-plan → wfc-deepen → wfc-validate → wfc-implement
```

**When to use**: New features requiring multi-file changes across services.

**Example**: This project followed this exact pipeline.

### Pattern 2: Parallel Implementation with wfc-task-agent

```
wfc-implement spawns N wfc-task-agent subagents (one per task) in parallel git worktrees
```

**CRITICAL**: All task implementation MUST use `wfc-task-agent`, NOT `kiro_default`.

**When to use**: Tasks with clear dependencies and no conflicts.

**Example**: TASK-010 (CloudTrail), TASK-011 (S3), TASK-012 (KMS) can run in parallel.

**How to invoke**:
```typescript
use_subagent({
  command: "InvokeSubagents",
  content: {
    subagents: [{
      agent_name: "wfc-task-agent",
      query: "Implement TASK-XXX: [description]...",
      relevant_context: "[dependencies and context]"
    }]
  }
})
```

**Why wfc-task-agent?**
- Pre-configured with Python/git/testing tools
- Auto-approved commands (no permission prompts)
- Follows TDD workflow automatically
- Writes minimal, correct code
- Proper error handling and logging
- Reduces implementation time by ~50%

### Pattern 3: Review-Driven Iteration

```
wfc-implement → wfc-review → fix issues → wfc-review → merge
```

**When to use**: After implementation, before merging to main.

**Example**: Each task should be reviewed before PR creation.

---

## Task Execution Strategy

### Dependency Graph

The 22 tasks are organized in 5 layers:

1. **Canary** (TASK-001): Validate Python setup
2. **Foundation** (TASK-002 to TASK-009): Models, AWS clients, orchestrator
3. **Scanners** (TASK-010 to TASK-012): CloudTrail, S3, KMS plugins
4. **Integration** (TASK-013 to TASK-016): CLI, output, Docker
5. **Safety Rails** (TASK-017 to TASK-022): Tests, dry-run, confidence scores

### Parallel Execution Groups

**Group 1** (after TASK-001):
- TASK-002 (Finding model)
- TASK-004 (Logger)

**Group 2** (after TASK-008):
- TASK-010 (CloudTrail scanner)
- TASK-011 (S3 scanner)
- TASK-012 (KMS scanner)

**Group 3** (after TASK-013):
- TASK-019 (Dry-run mode)
- TASK-020 (Confidence scores)
- TASK-021 (Per-service rate limiters)
- TASK-022 (Max accounts flag)

---

## Custom Agent Configuration

### wfc-task-agent

This project uses a custom agent (`wfc-task-agent`) for parallel task implementation with auto-approved tools.

**Location**: `~/.kiro/agents/wfc-task-agent.json`

**Configuration**:
```json
{
  "$schema": "https://raw.githubusercontent.com/aws/amazon-q-developer-cli/refs/heads/main/schemas/agent-v1.json",
  "name": "wfc-task-agent",
  "description": "Specialized agent for implementing WFC tasks in isolated git worktrees with TDD workflow",
  "prompt": "You are a specialized implementation agent for WFC (Workflow Control Framework) tasks.\n\nYour role:\n1. Create git worktrees for isolated task implementation\n2. Follow TDD workflow: write tests first, then implement\n3. Write minimal, correct code that satisfies acceptance criteria\n4. Commit changes with proper task messages\n5. Focus on Python best practices: type hints, Pydantic models, async/await\n\nKey principles:\n- Write only the ABSOLUTE MINIMAL code needed\n- Follow acceptance criteria exactly\n- Use proper Python type hints\n- Implement proper error handling\n- Log appropriately (never log credentials)\n- Test edge cases\n\nYou have full access to filesystem, bash, and git operations.",
  "tools": [
    "fs_read",
    "fs_write",
    "execute_bash",
    "grep",
    "glob",
    "code",
    "thinking"
  ],
  "allowedTools": [
    "fs_read",
    "fs_write",
    "execute_bash",
    "grep",
    "glob",
    "code",
    "thinking"
  ],
  "toolsSettings": {
    "execute_bash": {
      "autoAllowReadonly": true,
      "allowedCommands": [
        "git .*",
        "mkdir .*",
        "touch .*",
        "python3 -m venv .*",
        "\\.venv/bin/pip .*",
        "\\.venv/bin/pytest .*",
        "ls .*",
        "cat .*",
        "pwd",
        "cd .*"
      ]
    }
  },
  "resources": [
    "file://.wfc/planning/TASKS.md",
    "file://.wfc/planning/PROPERTIES.md",
    "file://.wfc/planning/TEST-PLAN.md"
  ]
}
```

**Why Custom Agent?**
- Eliminates tool approval friction during parallel execution
- Pre-configured with Python/git/testing tools
- Follows TDD workflow automatically
- Reduces implementation time by ~50%

**Usage**:
```javascript
use_subagent({
  agent_name: "wfc-task-agent",
  query: "Implement TASK-XXX: [description]...",
  relevant_context: "[dependencies and context]"
})
```

## Agent Instructions for Implementation

### For `wfc-implement` Orchestrator

**Prerequisites**:
- Git repository initialized ✅
- `.wfc/planning/TASKS.md` exists with 22 parseable tasks ✅
- Clean working directory ✅
- Custom `wfc-task-agent` configured ✅

**Execution**:
1. Run TASK-001 (canary) first
2. If canary passes, spawn parallel `wfc-task-agent` subagents for independent tasks
3. Each agent works in isolated git worktree (`.worktrees/task-NNN/`)
4. Each agent follows TDD workflow (test → implement → verify)
5. Integrate all worktrees into `develop` branch

### For Task Implementation Agents

**CRITICAL**: All task implementation MUST be done by `wfc-task-agent` subagent, NOT `kiro_default`.

**How to invoke wfc-task-agent**:
```typescript
use_subagent({
  command: "InvokeSubagents",
  content: {
    subagents: [{
      agent_name: "wfc-task-agent",
      query: "Implement TASK-XXX: [description from TASKS.md]",
      relevant_context: "[dependencies, acceptance criteria, related properties]"
    }]
  }
})
```

**Context to provide**:
- Task ID and description from `.wfc/planning/TASKS.md`
- Related properties from `.wfc/planning/PROPERTIES.md`
- Test requirements from `.wfc/planning/TEST-PLAN.md`
- Research findings from `.wfc/planning/deepen-log.md`

**Workflow**:
1. Read task acceptance criteria
2. Write tests first (pytest)
3. Implement minimal code to pass tests
4. Verify against formal properties
5. Create PR with task ID in title

### For Review Agents

**Review dimensions**:
1. **Security**: No hardcoded credentials, input validation, read-only operations
2. **Correctness**: Logic matches acceptance criteria, edge cases handled
3. **Performance**: Rate limiting, async/await, memory management
4. **Maintainability**: Clear naming, docstrings, type hints
5. **Reliability**: Error handling, logging, graceful degradation

**Consensus threshold**: 9.5/10 required for merge approval.

---

## Key Design Decisions

### Why Python?

**Original**: TypeScript/Node.js monorepo  
**Changed to**: Python single-package  
**Reason**: Validation findings (`.wfc/planning/VALIDATE.md`) showed:
- Monorepo complexity overkill for MVP (3 scanners)
- boto3 more mature than AWS SDK v3
- Easier for DevOps teams to extend
- Simpler distribution (pip + Docker)

**Impact**: Reduced from 24 tasks to 22, improved validation score from 7.8/10 to 8.3/10.

### Why Plugin Architecture?

**Rationale**:
- 11 services to scan (MVP: 3, future: 8 more)
- Parallel development (3 engineers can work on different scanners)
- Easy to add new services without modifying core

**Implementation**: Python Protocol for type-safe plugin interface.

### Why Formal Properties?

**Rationale**:
- Read-only operations are critical (PROP-001: no write operations)
- Performance SLA is strict (PROP-010: 60-minute scan for 100 accounts)
- Security is non-negotiable (PROP-002: credential security)

**Usage**: Each task links to properties it must satisfy.

---

## Common Pitfalls (from Research)

### CloudTrail Lake (TASK-010)
- ⚠️ **25 TB/month threshold** determines pricing model (one-year vs seven-year)
- ⚠️ Cost is $2.50 per 1M events ingested (uncompressed)
- ⚠️ Recommend advanced event selectors to exclude high-volume data events

### S3 Intelligent-Tiering (TASK-011)
- ⚠️ **128 KB minimum object size** - objects below this always stay in Frequent Access
- ⚠️ Don't recommend for buckets with mostly <128 KB objects
- ⚠️ Access patterns: GetObject resets timer, HeadObject does not

### KMS Optimization (TASK-012)
- ⚠️ **S3 bucket keys** reduce KMS requests by 99% for S3 encryption
- ⚠️ Data key caching (AWS Encryption SDK) reduces API calls
- ⚠️ Cost is $0.03 per 10,000 requests

### Rate Limiting (TASK-007, TASK-021)
- ⚠️ AWS throttles at service-specific limits
- ⚠️ Implement per-service rate limiters (CloudTrail: 10 req/sec, S3/KMS: 100 req/sec)
- ⚠️ Use exponential backoff with jitter for retries

### Credentials (TASK-005)
- ⚠️ STS tokens expire after 1 hour
- ⚠️ Implement refresh logic for scans >45 minutes
- ⚠️ Never log credential values - log only source (profile/role)

---

## Testing Strategy

### Unit Tests (pytest)
- **Location**: `tests/unit/`
- **Coverage target**: 80% line coverage
- **Mocking**: Use `moto` for AWS service mocking
- **Pattern**: Test each model, utility, and plugin in isolation

### Integration Tests (pytest + moto)
- **Location**: `tests/integration/`
- **Coverage**: End-to-end scanner workflows
- **Pattern**: Mock AWS APIs, verify Finding generation

### Example Test Structure

```python
# tests/unit/test_finding.py
def test_finding_valid():
    finding = Finding(
        service="CloudTrail",
        resource_id="arn:aws:cloudtrail:...",
        issue="High-volume events",
        estimated_monthly_savings=12000,
        severity=Severity.HIGH,
        recommendation="Add event selectors",
        documentation_link="https://docs.aws.amazon.com/...",
        remediation_snippet="aws cloudtrail put-event-selectors ..."
    )
    assert finding.severity == Severity.HIGH

# tests/integration/test_cloudtrail_scanner.py
@mock_aws
def test_cloudtrail_scanner_detects_high_volume():
    # Setup moto mocks
    client = boto3.client('cloudtrail', region_name='us-east-1')
    client.create_event_data_store(Name='test-store')
    
    # Run scanner
    scanner = CloudTrailScanner()
    findings = scanner.scan(session, '123456789012', 'us-east-1')
    
    # Verify
    assert len(findings) == 1
    assert findings[0].estimated_monthly_savings == 12000
```

## Distribution & Deployment

### Installation Methods

1. **PyPI** (future):
   ```bash
   pip install aws-cost-optimizer
   ```

2. **From source**:
   ```bash
   git clone https://github.com/your-org/aws-cost-optimizer
   cd aws-cost-optimizer
   pip install -e .
   ```

3. **Docker**:
   ```bash
   docker build -t aws-cost-optimizer .
   docker run aws-cost-optimizer scan --accounts 123456789012 --regions us-east-1
   ```

### Usage Examples

```bash
# Scan single account
aws-cost-optimizer scan --profile my-profile --accounts 123456789012 --regions us-east-1

# Scan all accounts in organization
aws-cost-optimizer scan --profile org-master --org-scan --regions us-east-1,us-west-2

# Dry-run mode (no API calls)
aws-cost-optimizer scan --dry-run --accounts 123456789012 --regions us-east-1

# Limit blast radius
aws-cost-optimizer scan --org-scan --max-accounts 10 --regions us-east-1
```

# SOURCE: /Users/samfakhreddine/repos/local-drafts/oilShock/AGENTS.md

# AGENTS.md

## Project

Pantry Buffer Planner v2 is a client-side web application that helps households build a region-aware, scenario-aware shopping list to hedge against a 12-18 month food and energy price disruption tied to the Hormuz crisis research.

The v2 product must preserve the sound household math from v1, then add:

- Regional profiles
- Scenario modeling
- Phased action timeline
- Research traceability for every recommendation

## Source Of Truth

Use these artifacts first:

1. `documents/pantry-calculator.jsx`
   - This is the v1 reference implementation.
   - It contains the current adult-equivalent math, household structure, item list shape, category model, and multi-household behavior.

2. `documents/document.pdf`
   - This is intended to be the primary research source for scenario definitions, hedge rankings, exposure logic, and evidence notes.
   - Do not fabricate citations, probabilities, rankings, or evidence chains from memory.

3. The current product brief for "Pantry Buffer Planner v2"
   - Treat the planning brief as a working product source alongside the research PDF.
   - If the brief and future research content conflict, prefer the research document and update the product artifacts accordingly.

## Current Repository State

- This repo currently contains documents, not a scaffolded application.
- There is no backend, auth system, or persistence layer in place.
- The existing implementation is a single React component with inline styles and in-memory state.
- The repo is not currently a git repository in this working directory.

## What v1 Already Does

Preserve these behaviors unless a later spec explicitly changes them:

- Household composition is modeled using age-based adult-equivalent multipliers.
- Buffer depth is entered in weeks.
- Users can manage multiple households and see per-household or combined totals.
- Pantry quantities are calculated as:
  `adult_equivalents * weeks * per_item_weekly_rate`
- Some items are conditionally shown based on household composition, such as senior-oriented and kid-oriented items.

Relevant v1 implementation details live in `documents/pantry-calculator.jsx`.

## v2 Product Direction

Build around four primary experiences:

1. Region selection
   - User chooses a region.
   - UI explains the region's exposure profile.

2. Scenario selection
   - User chooses Scenario A, B, C, or a probability-weighted default.
   - UI explains what the selected scenario implies.

3. Household composition
   - Preserve the v1 composition model.
   - Default buffer depth can vary by scenario.

4. Generated shopping list
   - This is the primary working screen.
   - It must be filterable, sortable, printable/exportable, and annotated with phased timing.

Secondary views:

- Commodity hedge table with explanation
- Standalone phased action checklist/timeline

## Core Product Rules

- Every recommendation must be traceable to a source passage.
- Region must materially change the output, not just the labels.
- Scenario must materially change urgency, default buffer depth, and timeline framing.
- The calculator remains client-side unless a later requirement explicitly justifies a backend.
- English-only is acceptable for phase one.
- Print and PDF export are first-class requirements, not polish.

## Region Model Expectations

Each region profile should eventually capture:

- Region identifier and label
- Measurement system
- Currency
- Staple grain pattern
- Default cooking oils
- Protein norms
- Typical retail pack sizes
- Exposure vector
- Region-specific substitution rules
- Region-specific warnings or panic-buy guidance

Expected launch coverage from the brief:

- United States
- Canada
- Western Europe
- UK and Ireland
- Eastern Europe
- East Asia
- Southeast Asia
- South Asia
- Middle East and North Africa
- Sub-Saharan Africa
- Oceania

It is acceptable to seed fewer regions first, but the initial schema must support all of them cleanly.

## Scenario Model Expectations

Support the scenario set described in the brief:

- Scenario A: ceasefire holds, about 35% probability
- Scenario B: ceasefire collapses, about 25% probability
- Scenario C: Iranian toll regime, about 40% probability
- Weighted default based on those probabilities

Scenario should affect:

- Default buffer depth
- Item urgency
- Timeline framing
- Explanation text shown to the user

Do not hard-code scenario behavior into UI components if it belongs in structured data.

## Item Data Expectations

The v1 flat item list needs to grow into a richer schema. Each item should support fields like:

- `id`
- `name`
- `category`
- `baseUnit`
- `baseRatePerAdultWeek`
- `packFormat`
- `fertilizerSensitivity`
- `oilTransportSensitivity`
- `shelfLifeBand`
- `middleEastInputExposure`
- `hedgeRanking`
- `regionalAvailability`
- `regionalSubstitutes`
- `evidenceNote`
- `evidenceSource`
- `timelinePhase`
- `scenarioAdjustments`

If the research source is incomplete, prefer explicit missing-data markers over guessed values.

## Engineering Guardrails

- Keep the application client-side by default.
- Use a strict three-tier architecture: presentation/templates, domain logic, and data/content.
- Follow SOLID and DRY when introducing modules, components, and shared logic.
- Treat contracts as first-class architecture. Every cross-tier boundary must have an explicit runtime-validated schema.
- In TypeScript, use Zod as the default Pydantic-like contract system unless the repo is later standardized on something else.
- Prefer schema-first definitions and infer TypeScript types from those schemas rather than maintaining parallel hand-written interfaces and validators.
- Treat dependency selection conservatively to reduce supply-chain risk.
- Any newly added or upgraded package must be at least 45 days old based on its public release date before it is allowed into the repo.
- Move content and model data out of components and into structured JSON or typed data modules.
- Separate calculation logic from presentation logic and keep source-of-truth rules out of UI files.
- Do not repeat the v1 monolithic single-file pattern in production code.
- Keep presentation markup/templates separate from business logic modules; do not bury all behavior, markup, and styling in one file.
- Validate all external and persisted inputs at the boundary: research-derived data, JSON content, `localStorage`, URL/query params, and any future import/export payloads.
- Do not pass raw `unknown`, `any`, or unchecked JSON objects into domain logic.
- Preserve a responsive layout for mobile use in-store.
- Use Tailwind CSS for production styling.
- Do not use inline style objects for standard component styling.
- Build print-friendly output early enough that the layout does not need to be rewritten later.
- Local persistence via `localStorage` is acceptable.
- Do not add accounts, cloud sync, supplier integrations, or barcode features in v2 unless the scope is explicitly expanded.
- Frontend design should feel modern, intentional, and editorial rather than generic AI-themed UI.
- Avoid default purple gradients and other stereotypical LLM-app styling unless the product direction explicitly changes.

## Suggested Initial Architecture

Prefer a structure close to this once the app is scaffolded:

```text
src/
  app/
  presentation/
    components/
    layouts/
    pages/
  domain/
    contracts/
    calc/
    scoring/
    state/
    formatting/
    traceability/
  data/
    items/
    regions/
    scenarios/
    content/
  styles/
    tailwind.css
```

If using TypeScript, define runtime schemas and inferred types for region profiles, items, scenarios, planner state, and persisted payloads before building the UI around them.

## TypeScript Contract Pattern

For this repo, Zod is the default TypeScript analogue to Pydantic.

- Define the runtime schema once with `z.object(...)`.
- Infer the static TypeScript type from that schema with `z.infer`.
- Use `parse` for seeded data that must fail fast during development and build-time validation.
- Use `safeParse` for recoverable user or persistence inputs such as `localStorage`.
- Keep validated domain objects readonly where practical so downstream code cannot mutate source-of-truth content casually.
- Avoid duplicate `interface` plus validator definitions for the same shape unless there is a proven reason.

## Recommended Initial Work Order

1. Define the shared contract and validation layer.
2. Define the region profile schema.
3. Define the expanded item schema.
4. Seed at least two complete region profiles.
5. Encode the scenario model and probability-weighted default.
6. Port the v1 household math into a reusable calculation module.
7. Build the four-screen flow.
8. Add evidence traceability UI.
9. Add print/export support.
10. Add optional local persistence.

## Non-Goals For v2

Do not expand into these areas unless explicitly requested:

- Live price tracking
- Inventory management
- Barcode scanning
- Supplier integration
- Medical advice
- Financial advice
- Evacuation advice
- Full localization beyond English
- User accounts

## Agent Behavior

When working in this repository:

- Start from the source documents before changing product direction.
- Preserve the v1 calculator math unless there is a documented reason to change it.
- Use `documents/document.pdf` for exact evidence mapping.
- Do not invent commodity hedge rankings or citations.
- Prefer small, reviewable data and UI increments.
- Call out any assumption that should later be replaced with sourced research.

## Immediate Constraint

The repo still lacks an application scaffold. Agents should focus on:

- Schema design
- UI architecture
- Porting the v1 calculator logic
- Research-backed traceability plumbing

Agents should avoid presenting unsourced research details as final content.

<!-- wfc:start -->
# WFC — Code Intelligence for oilShock

This project uses WFC for multi-agent code review, planning, and implementation.

## Always Do

- **MUST run `/wfc-review` before merging any PR.** The 5-reviewer consensus system (Security, Correctness, Performance, Maintainability, Reliability) catches issues that single-pass review misses.
- **MUST run impact analysis before editing widely-called symbols.** Use `wfc helpers impact <symbol>` to check blast radius at depth 1/2/3 before modifying functions with many callers.
- **MUST check knowledge freshness.** Run `wfc helpers status` — if knowledge is stale, results may be outdated.
- **MUST follow TDD workflow: write tests FIRST, verify they FAIL (RED), then implement (GREEN).** WFC enforces this — agents that skip the RED phase are aborted with `RedPhaseViolationError`. Never write implementation code before you have a failing test that proves the behavior doesn't exist yet.
- When planning features, use `/wfc-plan` for structured planning with adaptive interview.
- When implementing, use `/wfc-implement` for parallel TDD-based execution with worktree isolation.

## Code Discipline

These rules override default AI coding tendencies. Full details in `~/.wfc/rules/`.

1. **No silent fallbacks** — never use `??` or `||` to mask data that should not be missing. Throw instead.
2. **No catch-all try/catch** — business logic must let errors propagate. Catch only at boundaries (API routes, event handlers).
3. **Tests must break when code breaks** — if deleting the implementation doesn't fail the test, the test is worthless. Assert concrete values, not existence.
4. **No invented API surface** — never call methods, import symbols, or use options you haven't confirmed exist. When uncertain, state it.
5. **Minimal diffs only** — change only what the task requires. No drive-by refactors, no unrelated "improvements".
6. **500-line file hard cap** — no source file may exceed 500 lines (all lines including comments). Split before you hit it.
7. **Three-tier architecture** — Presentation (thin) → Logic (pure, no I/O) → Data (no business rules). Never skip a tier.
8. **No AI leakage** — branch names, commits, PR titles must never reveal which AI tool was used. Use `feat/`, `fix/`, `chore/` prefixes only.

## Skill Quick Reference

| Task | Skill |
|------|-------|
| Full auto pipeline | `/wfc-lfg "feature"` |
| Quick single feature | `/wfc-build "feature"` |
| Structured planning | `/wfc-plan` |
| Parallel TDD implementation | `/wfc-implement` |
| 5-agent consensus review | `/wfc-review` |
| Business analysis | `/wfc-ba` |
| Fix PR comments | `/wfc-pr-comments` |

## Never Do

- NEVER push directly to `main`. Always use feature branches with PR.
- NEVER branch from a feature branch. Always branch from `main`.
- NEVER skip pre-commit hooks (`--no-verify`).
- NEVER commit failing tests.
- NEVER commit dev artifacts from `~/.wfc/` to the repo.
- NEVER write plans, reviews, or dev artifacts into the repo. Store in `~/.wfc/projects/{{repo}}/`.
- NEVER run `make format` after commit — run it before.
- NEVER write implementation code before writing a failing test. TDD RED-GREEN-REFACTOR is enforced, not optional.
- NEVER use `??` or `||` to hide data that should not be missing — throw an error instead.
- NEVER reveal AI tool names (claude, copilot, cursor, codex) in branches, commits, or PRs.

## Observability

```bash
wfc helpers status         # active pipelines + knowledge freshness
wfc helpers doctor         # environment health check
wfc helpers resume         # find resumable interrupted pipelines
wfc helpers clean          # dry-run GC for stale state files
wfc helpers timeline       # telemetry event trail (last 7 days)
```

<!-- wfc:end -->


# SOURCE: /Users/samfakhreddine/repos/rax/qbr_prep/AGENTS.md

# AI Agent Guide

Instructions for AI coding assistants working on the AlertOps QBR Tool.

## Quick Reference

### Technology Stack
- **Python**: >= 3.12 with full type annotations
- **Package Manager**: `uv` (not pip)
- **Testing**: pytest + hypothesis (property-based)
- **UI**: Rich library for TUI, Flask for webapps

### Common Commands
```bash
# Setup
uv sync
source .venv/bin/activate

# Run application
python -m alertops_qbr                    # Interactive TUI
python -m alertops_qbr --dashboard --start 2025-01-01 --end 2025-03-31

# Testing
pytest                                     # All tests
pytest -v                                  # Verbose
pytest tests/properties/                   # Property-based tests

# Webapps
cd dashboard_webapp && uv run flask run --port 5002
cd classifier_webapp && uv run flask run --port 5001
```

## Project Structure

```
alertops_qbr/
├── api/           # API client, config
├── core/          # Business logic (classifier, SLA, validators, orchestrator)
├── models/        # Dataclasses (Alert, ProcessedAlert)
├── generators/    # Excel, dashboard, metrics, calculators, extractors, cache
├── ui/            # CLI, TUI
└── utils/         # Constants, errors, timezone

classifier_webapp/ # Flask app for "Other" alert classification
dashboard_webapp/  # Flask app for browser-based dashboard generation
tests/             # Unit and property-based tests
docs/specs/        # Specification documents
```

## Key Files by Task

### Modifying Classification Logic
1. `alertops_qbr/core/classifier.py` - Main classification functions
2. `alertops_qbr/utils/constants.py` - Keywords, thresholds, severity definitions
3. `docs/specs/SEVERITY_CLASSIFICATION_SPEC.md` - Reference specification

### Adding Dashboard Features
1. `alertops_qbr/generators/dashboard.py` - HTML generation, template handling
2. `alertops_qbr/generators/dashboard_processor.py` - Data processing
3. `alertops_qbr/generators/metrics.py` - Metric dataclasses
4. `alertops_qbr/generators/calculators.py` - Metric calculation classes
5. `alertops_qbr/generators/templates/dashboard.html` - HTML template

### Modifying Instance Enrichment
1. `alertops_qbr/generators/instance_enrichment.py` - API-based name lookup
2. `alertops_qbr/generators/instance_cache.py` - Persistent caching
3. `alertops_qbr/generators/extractors.py` - Instance/RDS extraction

### Adding CLI Options
1. `alertops_qbr/ui/cli.py` - Argument parsing, non-interactive mode
2. `alertops_qbr/ui/tui.py` - Interactive terminal UI

### Error Handling
1. `alertops_qbr/utils/errors.py` - All error classes and exit codes

## Coding Conventions

### Type Hints
Use Python 3.12+ syntax:
```python
def process(alerts: list[Alert]) -> dict[str, int]:
    result: dict[str, int] = {}
    name: str | None = None
    ...
```

### Dataclasses
Use for all data models:
```python
@dataclass
class MyMetric:
    name: str
    count: int
    percentage: float = 0.0
```

### Imports
Absolute imports from package root:
```python
from alertops_qbr.models.alerts import Alert, ProcessedAlert
from alertops_qbr.core.classifier import classify_ticket
from alertops_qbr.utils.constants import SEV1_KEYWORDS
```

### Error Handling
Use centralized error classes:
```python
from alertops_qbr.utils.errors import ValidationError, APIError

if not valid:
    raise ValidationError("Specific error message")
```

## Testing Guidelines

### Unit Tests
- Place in `tests/` directory
- Name files `test_*.py`
- Test specific examples and edge cases

### Property-Based Tests
- Place in `tests/properties/`
- Use hypothesis library
- Test universal properties across inputs

Example:
```python
from hypothesis import given, strategies as st

@given(st.dates(), st.dates())
def test_date_range_validation(start, end):
    # Property: validation should never raise unexpected exceptions
    is_valid, _ = validate_date_range(start, end)
    assert isinstance(is_valid, bool)
```

## Bash Command Guidelines

### Avoid
- Chained commands with `&&` (breaks PTY)
- `source .venv/bin/activate && python ...`
- Long inline Python import tests

### Prefer
- Use `getDiagnostics` for syntax/type checking
- Direct execution: `.venv/bin/python -c "..."`
- Simple, single commands

## Common Patterns

### Adding a New Calculator
```python
# In alertops_qbr/generators/calculators.py
class MyNewCalculator:
    def calculate(self, alerts: list[ProcessedAlert], total: int) -> MyMetric:
        # Implementation
        return MyMetric(...)

# In alertops_qbr/generators/dashboard_processor.py
class DashboardProcessor:
    def __init__(self, ..., my_calculator: MyNewCalculator | None = None):
        self._my_calc = my_calculator or MyNewCalculator()
```

### Adding a New Metric
```python
# In alertops_qbr/generators/metrics.py
@dataclass(frozen=True)
class MyNewMetric:
    name: str
    value: int
    percentage: float

# Add to DashboardData
@dataclass
class DashboardData:
    ...
    my_new_metric: MyNewMetric | None = None
```

### Adding Dashboard Section
1. Add metric dataclass in `metrics.py`
2. Add calculator in `calculators.py`
3. Wire calculator in `dashboard_processor.py`
4. Add HTML builder method in `dashboard.py`
5. Add template placeholder in `templates/dashboard.html`

## Severity Classification Priority

Always maintain this order: SEV 1 → SEV 2 → SEV 4 → SEV 3

```python
# In classifier.py
def classify_severity(...) -> str:
    # Check SEV 1 conditions first
    if is_sev1_condition:
        return "SEV 1"
    
    # Then SEV 2
    if is_sev2_condition:
        return "SEV 2"
    
    # Then SEV 4 (before SEV 3!)
    if is_sev4_condition:
        return "SEV 4"
    
    # Default to SEV 3
    return "SEV 3"
```

## Environment Reclassification

Non-production detection is centralized in `classifier.py`. The `dashboard.py` reclassification reuses `detect_environment()` to stay in sync automatically.

```python
# All patterns defined in classifier.py
STAGING_PATTERNS = ["-staging/", "-staging-", "/staging", "-ite/", "-ite-"]
TEST_NONPROD_PATTERN = re.compile(r"[-/]test[/-]|[-/]test$", re.IGNORECASE)
TIER_NONPROD_PATTERN = re.compile(r"tier[1-9X]", re.IGNORECASE)
DEV_NONPROD_PATTERN = re.compile(r"[-/]dev[/-]|[-/]dev$|informatica-dev|\bDev\s+(?:Worker|Controller|Core)\b", re.IGNORECASE)
SANDBOX_NONPROD_PATTERN = re.compile(r"\bSbx\b|[-/]sandbox[/-]", re.IGNORECASE)
```

When adding new non-production patterns, only update `classifier.py`.

## Spec-Driven Development

Feature specs are in `.kiro/specs/`:
- `requirements.md` - User stories and acceptance criteria
- `design.md` - Technical design
- `tasks.md` - Implementation checklist

When implementing a spec:
1. Read all three documents first
2. Follow tasks in order
3. Reference requirements in code comments
4. Update task status as you complete items

## API Client Usage

```python
from alertops_qbr.api.client import AlertOpsClient
from alertops_qbr.api.config import ConfigManager

# Load config
config = ConfigManager()
config.load_api_key()

# Create client
client = AlertOpsClient(config.api_key, config.base_url)

# Fetch alerts
alerts = client.fetch_alerts(start_date, end_date)

# Get alert detail (for instance enrichment)
detail = client.get_alert_detail(alert_id)
```

## Instance Cache Usage

```python
from alertops_qbr.generators.instance_cache import InstanceCache

# Load cache (creates if not exists)
cache = InstanceCache()

# Check cache
if cache.contains(instance_id):
    name = cache.get(instance_id)

# Update cache
cache.set(instance_id, name)
cache.save()  # Persist to disk
```

## Progress Tracking

Use the `ProgressCallback` protocol for UI updates:
```python
class ProgressCallback(Protocol):
    def on_fetch_start(self) -> None: ...
    def on_fetch_progress(self, current: int, total: int, message: str) -> None: ...
    def on_fetch_complete(self, alert_count: int) -> None: ...
    def on_classify_progress(self, current: int, total: int) -> None: ...
    # ... etc
```

## Debugging Tips

1. Use `getDiagnostics` tool for type/syntax errors
2. Check `~/.alertops_qbr/instance_cache.json` for cache issues
3. Review `classifier_webapp/learned_mappings.json` for classification patterns
4. Enable logging in Flask apps for API debugging
